Buyu — Sales and Trade
advanced
10 min
Legal Tricks and the Threefold Classification of Deferments
Commentary on the rejection of a legal trick and the threefold classification of deferments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify debt deferments into invalid, valid but non-binding, and binding, and evaluate the rejected legal trick for loan deferment.

Core Idea
Deferments are of three types: invalid (sarf/salam), valid but not binding (loans, post-mortem), and binding (all others).

The commentary delves into legal stratagems (hiyal) attempted to make loan deferment binding, and then provides a comprehensive classification of all deferments according to their legal effect. This lesson equips you to categorize any deferment scenario and understand why the predominant Hanafi view rejects the trick.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Trick (Hila) for Loan Deferment
Read the description: the borrower transfers the creditor to another person for the debt, and the creditor then defers the transferee. Understand how this indirect method attempts to circumvent the prohibition.
The trick involves a transfer (hawala) or guarantee (kafala) to change the nature of the debt.
2
Learn Why the Trick Is Rejected
The commentary states that only al-Husari accepted this trick; the majority of companions reject it. The text says it is not to be issued as a fatwa. Understand the principle: what is prohibited directly cannot be achieved indirectly through a hila in this context.
The rejection is based on the strong stance against riba; the trick does not change the underlying riba.
3
Understand the Threefold Classification
The text summarizes: invalid (batil) for deferment of countervalues in sarf and salam; valid but non-binding (sahih ghayr lazim) for loans, debts after death, and certain cases; binding (lazim) for all other debts. Memorize these categories.
Invalid means the act is prohibited and has no effect. Valid but non-binding means the deferment is allowed but not enforceable; either party can revert.
4
Apply the Classification to Examples
Go through the examples provided: deferment after death of debtor, deferment by preemptor, deferment upon rescission. Classify each as one of the three types.
Use the text's list to see the nuances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وتأجيل كل دين إلا القرض) أي صح لأن الدين حقه فله أن يؤخره، سواء كان ثمن مبيع أو غيره تيسيراً على من عليه ألا ترى أنه يملك ابراءه مطلقاً فكذا مؤقتاً. ولا بد من قبوله ممن عليه الدين فلو لم يقبله بطلب التأخير فيكون حالاً؛ كذا ذكره الأسبيجابي . ويصح تعليق التأجيل بالشرط فلو قال رب الدين لمن عليه ألف حالة إن دفعت إلي غداً خمسمائة فالخمسمائة الأخرى مؤخرة عنك إلى سنة فهو جائز ؛ كذا في الذخيرة. وإنما لا يؤجل القرض لكونه إعارة وصلة في الابتداء حتى يصح بلفظ الإعارة ولا يملكه يملك التبرع كالصبي والوصي ومعاوضة في الانتهاء فعلى اعتبار الابتداء لا يلزم التأجيل فيه كما في الإعارة إذ لا جبر في التبرع، وعلى اعتبار الانتهاء لا لأنه يصح يصير بيع الدراهم بالدراهم نسيئة وهو ربا، ومرادهم من الصحة اللزوم ومن عدم صحته في القرض عدم اللزوم. وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا أجله بعد الاستهلاك أو قبله هو الصحيح، وليس من تأجيل القرض تأجيل بدل الدراهم أو الدنانير المستهلكة إذا باستهلاكها لا تصير قرضاً، والحيلة في لزوم تأجيل القرض أن يحيل المستقرض المقرض على آخر بدينه فيؤجل المقرض ذلك الرجل الثمن التعليق فإذا أبرأته براءة إسقاط وقع ورجع عليها ؛ كذا في الأشباه قوله : (فلا يطالب المشتري بالمبيع الخ) أي لا يكون للمشتري أن يطالب البائع بالمبيع حتى يدفع المشتري له الزيادة وللبائع حبس المبيع حتى يقبضها من المشتري هذا معنى هذه العبارة ولا يخفى أن المراد بالزيادة فيها الزيادة في وقد تقدم ذلك والكلام الآن في الزيادة في المبيع. قوله : (وهي حيلة تأجيل القرض) قال في النهر : لكن في السراج قال أبو يوسف : إذا أقرض رجل رجلاً مالاً فكفل به رجل عنه إلى وقت كان على. الكفيل إلى وقته وعلى المستقرض حالاً اهـ. وسيأتي في كتاب الكفالة ذكر المسألة أيضاً. ونقل المؤلف هناك عن التتارخانية معزياً إلى الذخيرة والغياثية ما يوافق ما في السراج، وذكر في أنفع الوسائل مثله عن عدة كتب وذكر أن هذه الحيلة لم يقل بها أحد غير الحصيري في التحرير وأنه إذا تعارض كلامه وحده مع كلام كل الأصحاب لا يفتي به . قوله : (بل كذلك لا . يصح تأجيل الدين في صورة الخ) قال في النهر بعد ذكره لها : وظاهر كلامهم يعطي أن في هذه المسائل لا يصح التأجيل أصلاً لا أنه يلزم المحال عليه فيلزم حينئذ ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وإذا لزم فإن كان للمحيل على المحال عليه فلا إشكال وإلا أقر المحيل بقدر المحال به للمحال عليه مؤجلاً إليه. أشار في المحيط وفي الظهيرية القبض المجحود يجوز تأجيله. وفي القنية من كتاب المداينات : قضى القاضي بلزوم الأجل في القرض بعد ما ثبت عنده تأجيل القرض معتمداً على قول مالك وابن أبي ليلى يصح ويلزم الأجل. وفي تلخيص الجامع من كتاب الحوالة : لو كفل بالحال مؤجلاً تأخر الأصيل وإن كان قرضاً لأن الدين واحد وهي حيلة تأجيل القرض إذ يثبت ضمناً ما قصداً كبيع الشرب والطريق، ولا يلزم ما أجل بعد الكفالة إذ موضوعها أن يضيف إلى اللازم بالكفالة إلا الدين حتى لو عكس تأخر عن الأصيل أيضا حذ والإبراء ا هـ . ولم يستثن المصنف رحمه الله تعالى من عدم صحة تأجيل القرض شيئاً واستثنى منه في الهداية ما إذا أوصى أن يقرض من ماله ألف درهم فلاناً إلى سنة حيث يلزم من ثلثه أن يقرضوه ولا يطالبوه قبل المدة لأنه وصية بالتبرع بمنزلة الوصية بالخدمة والسكنى فيلزم حقاً للموصي ولا ينحصر في هذه الصورة بل كذلك إذا كان له قرض على إنسان فأوصى أن يؤجل ولزم كما في القنية. وقد كتبنا في الفوائد الفقهية أن المستثنى لا ينحصر في القرض بل كذلك لا يصح تأجيل الدين في صور : الأولى لو مات المديون وحل المال فأجل الدائن لأن الدين في الذمة وفائدة التأجيل أن يتجر فيؤدي الثمن من نماء المال، فإذا من له الأجل تعين المتروك لقضاء الدين فلا يفيد التأجيل؛ كذا في الخلاصة، وظاهره في كل دين . وذكره في القنية في القرض الثانية أجل المشتري الشفيع في الثمن لم يصح كما سيأتي فيها وهو مذكور في القنية . اهـ. سنة صح وأرثه لم يصح مات أنه يصح . عن وفي الخلاصة : بموت البائع لا يبطل الأجل ويبطل بموت المشتري. الثالثة تأجيل ثمن المبيع عند الإقالة لا كما قدمناه القنية. والحاصل أن تأجيل الدين على ثلاثة أوجه : باطل وهو تأجيل بدلي الصرف والسلم وصحيح غير لازم وهو القرض والدين بعد الموت وتأجيل الشفيع وثمن المبيع بعد الإقالة ولازم فيما عدا ذلك. قال قاضيخان في فتاواه : المديون إذا قال برئت من الأجل أو لا حاجة لي في الأجل لهذا الدين لم يكن إبطالاً للأجل، ولو قال أبطلت الأجل أو قال تركته صار حالاً، والمديون إذا قضى الدين قبل حلول الأجل فاستحق المقبوض من القابض أو وجده زيوفاً فرده كان الدين عليه إلى أجله، ولو اشترى من مديونه شيئاً بالدين وقبضه ثم تقايلا البيع لا يعود الأجل، ولو يصح، ولا يلزم كما هو ظاهر ما في البحر إذ جعله ملحقاً بالفرض ثم قال : والحاصل أن تأجيل الديون على ثلاثة أوجه الخ. وقد علمت ما هو الواقع .اهـ قلت الظاهر أن المراد بالباطل هنا ما لا يجوز فعله والمضي وبالصحيح ما يجوز قوله: (وفي الخلاصة وإبطال الأجل الخ) أي إبطال الأجل
He said: 'And deferment of every debt except the loan' i.e., it is valid because the debt is his right, so he may delay it, whether it is the price of a sold item or otherwise, to make it easier for the debtor. Do you not see that he may discharge it absolutely, so likewise temporarily. Acceptance from the debtor is necessary; if he does not accept the request for deferment, it remains due immediately. Thus mentioned al-Asbijabi. It is valid to suspend the deferment on a condition: if the creditor says to one who owes him a thousand as a spot debt: 'If you pay me five hundred tomorrow, the other five hundred is deferred for you for a year,' it is permissible. Thus in al-Dhakhira. The loan is not deferred because it is a loan and a connection initially, so it is valid with the wording of a loan, and the creditor does not own the right to charity like a minor or executor, and it becomes an exchange at the end. So considering the beginning, deferment is not binding in it, as in a loan, since there is no compulsion in charity; and considering the end, it is not because it would become a sale of dirhams for dirhams on credit, which is riba. Their intention of validity is binding, and of its invalidity in the loan is non-binding. He applied it generally, so it includes whether he deferred it after consumption or before—that is the correct view. Deferment of the loan does not include deferment of the substitute for consumed dirhams or dinars because their consumption does not make it a loan. The trick for making deferment of a loan binding is that the borrower transfers the creditor to another person for his debt, and the creditor defers that person. ... He said: 'This is the trick for deferring a loan.' He said in al-Nahr: But in al-Siraj, Abu Yusuf said: If a man lends another money, and a third person becomes a guarantor for him for a term, the guarantor is responsible for the term, and the borrower is immediately liable. This will be mentioned later in the book of Kafala. The author there quotes from al-Tatar Khaniyya attributing to al-Dhakhira and al-Ghiyathiyya what agrees with al-Siraj, and mentions in Anfa' al-Wasa'il similar from several books, and mentions that this trick was not said by anyone except al-Husari in al-Tahrir, and that when his statement alone conflicts with the statements of all the companions, it is not to be issued as a fatwa. He said: 'But likewise, deferment of the debt is not valid in the following case...' He said in al-Nahr after mentioning it: The apparent meaning of their statements is that in these cases deferment is not valid at all, not that it becomes binding on the transferee... If it becomes binding, then if the transferor has a claim on the transferee, there is no problem; otherwise, the transferor acknowledges the amount transferred to the transferee as deferred. He indicated in al-Muhit and al-Zahiriyya that the denied payment may be deferred. In al-Qunyah from the book of Mudayanat: The judge ruled for the binding of the term in the loan after it was established that the deferment of the loan was agreed upon, relying on the statement of Malik and Ibn Abi Layla that it is valid and binding. In Talkhis al-Jami' from the book of Hawala: If someone guarantees a spot debt as deferred, the principal is delayed even if it is a loan, because the debt is one, and this is a trick for deferring the loan, as what is intended indirectly is established, like the sale of irrigation rights and right of way. And what is deferred after guarantee is not binding... He did not exclude anything from the invalidity of deferring a loan. Al-Hidayah excluded the case where one bequeaths that a thousand dirhams be lent to so-and-so for a year; then it becomes binding from his third that they lend it and do not demand it before the term, because it is a bequest of charity, like the bequest of service and dwelling, so it becomes a right of the testator. This is not limited to this case, but likewise if he had a loan on someone and bequeathed that it be deferred, it becomes binding, as in al-Qunyah. We have written in al-Fawa'id al-Fiqhiyya that the excluded cases are not limited to the loan, but likewise deferment of the debt is not valid in the following cases: First, if the debtor dies and the debt becomes due, and the creditor defers it, because the debt is in the liability, and the benefit of deferment is for the debtor to trade and pay from the produce of the wealth, so when the deceased (the one with the term) dies, the estate is assigned to pay the debt, so deferment is not beneficial. Thus in al-Khulasa, and it is apparent that it applies to every debt. Al-Qunyah mentioned it regarding the loan. Second, if the buyer defers the preemptor in the price, it is not valid, as will come later. This is mentioned in al-Qunyah. ... In al-Khulasa: With the death of the seller, the term does not become void, but it becomes void with the death of the buyer. Third, deferment of the price of the sold item upon rescission, it is not valid, as we have previously mentioned in al-Qunyah. The summary is that deferment of debts is of three types: invalid—which is deferment of the countervalues in currency exchange and salam; valid but not binding—which is the loan and the debt after death, and the deferment of the preemptor and the price after rescission; and binding in all other cases. Qadikhan said in his Fatawa: If the debtor says 'I am free from the term' or 'I have no need for the term for this debt,' that does not nullify the term. If he says 'I have nullified the term' or 'I have abandoned it,' it becomes due immediately. If the debtor pays the debt before the term, and then the payment is reclaimed from the recipient, or he finds it counterfeit and returns it, the debt remains until its term. If he buys something from his debtor with the debt and takes possession, then they rescind the sale, the term does not return. ... He said: The summary is that deferment of debts is of three types... I said: It appears that by 'invalid' here they mean what is not permissible to do and proceed with, and by 'valid' what is permissible. He said: '(And in al-Khulasa, nullification of the term...)' i.e., nullification of the term.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the matn statement 'And deferment of every debt except the loan.' The commentator explains that a creditor may defer any debt by agreement with the debtor, including the price of a sale or other debts, but a loan (qard) cannot be deferred because it is a gratuitous contract initially (like a loan) and if deferred it would become a sale of money for money on credit, which is riba. However, there is debate about certain exceptions: if the debtor dies and the creditor defers the debt from the estate, it is not valid. Also, there is discussion of a legal trick (hila) to make deferment binding by using a guarantor or transfer, but this is not accepted by most scholars except al-Husari. The passage concludes by categorizing all deferments into three types: invalid (for currency exchange and salam), valid but not binding (loan and debt after death, and certain cases), and binding (all other cases).

Key Terms
الحيلة (al-ḥīla): A legal stratagem to achieve a permissible end through indirect means, here to make deferment of a loan binding.
باطل (bāṭil): Void; having no legal effect. Deferment of sarf and salam are invalid.
صحيح غير لازم (ṣaḥīḥ ghayr lāzim): Valid but non-binding; the deferment is allowed but not enforceable; either party can rescind.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars, which of the following is a valid but non-binding deferment?
A) Deferment of the price in a sarf transaction.
B) Deferment of the price in a salam contract.
C) Deferment of a loan (qard).
D) Deferment of the price of a sold item.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification divides deferments into three categories—invalid, valid but non-binding, and binding—with loans and post-death debts falling into the non-binding category, and the majority rejects the legal trick to make loan deferment binding.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Three Categories of Debt Deferment (Ta'jīl al-Dayn)
Summarizes three debt deferment categories with examples and a dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories of debt deferment in Hanafi fiqh and apply the distinction to classify deferment scenarios as invalid, valid non-binding, or binding.

Core Idea
Debt deferment in Hanafi fiqh is not universally binding – loan deferment may be repudiated by the debtor.

In this passage from Al-Bahr al-Rā'iq, the commentator distills the Hanafi position on deferring debts into a clear three-fold classification. Understanding this classification is crucial for correctly applying contracts involving deferred payments, especially loans and sale transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its categories
The passage classifies deferment (ta'jīl) into three types: bāṭil (invalid), ṣaḥīḥ ghayr lāzim (valid but non-binding), and lāzim (binding). Determine what defines each category based on the examples given.
The invalid category concerns sarf (currency exchange) and salam (advance purchase) because they require immediate exchange.
2
Locate the disputed sub-issue
Loan deferment is listed as ṣaḥīḥ ghayr lāzim, but the passage notes that some scholars (Mālik, Ibn Abī Laylā) consider it binding. Understand the Hanafi default and how later fatwa works treat the judge's enforcement.
This dispute is a legitimate ikhtilāf within the broader fiqh tradition.
3
Derive the practical consequence
For each category, determine what happens if deferment is agreed upon. In the valid non-binding category, the debtor may cancel; in the binding category, both parties must adhere; in the invalid category, the contract itself is void.
The muftā bihī (operative ruling) is that loan deferment is ṣaḥīḥ ghayr lāzim.
4
Apply to new cases
Given a scenario involving deferment of a trade debt, a loan, or a sale after revocation, classify it into one of the three categories and state the ruling.
Refer to the examples in the passage: deferment of a price after iqāla falls under ṣaḥīḥ ghayr lāzim?

كتاب البيع باب المرابحة والتولية دين عن يمتنع المحال عليه فيلزم حينئذ ; كذا في فتح القدير. وإذا لزم فإن كان للمحيل على المحال عليه فلا إشكال وإلا أقر المحيل بقدر المحال به للمحال عليه مؤجلاً إليه. أشار في المحيط وفي الظهيرية القبض المجحود يجوز تأجيله. وفي القنية من كتاب المداينات : قضى القاضي بلزوم الأجل في القرض بعد ما ثبت عنده تأجيل القرض معتمداً على قول مالك وابن أبي ليلى يصح ويلزم الأجل. وفي تلخيص الجامع من كتاب الحوالة : لو كفل بالحال مؤجلاً تأخر الأصيل وإن كان قرضاً لأن الدين واحد وهي حيلة تأجيل القرض إذ يثبت ضمناً ما قصداً كبيع الشرب والطريق، ولا يلزم ما أجل بعد الكفالة إذ موضوعها أن يضيف إلى اللازم بالكفالة إلا الدين حتى لو عكس تأخر عن الأصيل أيضا حتى والإبراء ا هـ . ولم يستثن المصنف رحمه الله تعالى من عدم صحة تأجيل القرض شيئاً واستثنى منه في الهداية ما إذا أوصى أن يقرض من ماله ألف درهم فلاناً إلى سنة حيث يلزم من ثلثه أن يقرضوه ولا يطالبوه قبل المدة لأنه وصية بالتبرع بمنزلة الوصية بالخدمة والسكنى فيلزم حقاً للموصي ولا ينحصر في هذه الصورة بل كذلك إذا كان له قرض على إنسان فأوصى أن يؤجل ولزم كما في القنية. وقد كتبنا في الفوائد الفقهية أن المستثنى لا ينحصر في القرض بل كذلك لا يصح تأجيل الدين في صور : الأولى لو مات المديون وحل المال فأجل الدائن لأن الدين في الذمة وفائدة التأجيل أن يتجر فيؤدي الثمن من نماء المال، فإذا من له الأجل تعين المتروك لقضاء الدين فلا يفيد التأجيل؛ كذا في الخلاصة، وظاهره في كل دين . وذكره في القنية في القرض الثانية أجل المشتري الشفيع في الثمن لم يصح كما سيأتي فيها وهو مذكور في القنية . اهـ. سنة صح وأرثه لم يصح مات أنه يصح . عن وفي الخلاصة : بموت البائع لا يبطل الأجل ويبطل بموت المشتري. الثالثة تأجيل ثمن المبيع عند الإقالة لا كما قدمناه القنية. والحاصل أن تأجيل الدين على ثلاثة أوجه : باطل وهو تأجيل بدلي الصرف والسلم وصحيح غير لازم وهو القرض والدين بعد الموت وتأجيل الشفيع وثمن المبيع بعد الإقالة ولازم فيما عدا ذلك. قال قاضيخان في فتاواه : المديون إذا قال برئت من الأجل أو لا حاجة لي في الأجل لهذا الدين لم يكن إبطالاً للأجل، ولو قال أبطلت الأجل أو قال تركته صار حالاً، والمديون إذا قضى الدين قبل حلول الأجل فاستحق المقبوض من القابض أو وجده زيوفاً فرده كان الدين عليه إلى أجله، ولو اشترى من مديونه شيئاً بالدين وقبضه ثم تقايلا البيع لا يعود الأجل، ولو يصح، ولا يلزم كما هو ظاهر ما في البحر إذ جعله ملحقاً بالفرض ثم قال : والحاصل أن تأجيل الديون على ثلاثة أوجه الخ. وقد علمت ما هو الواقع .اهـ قلت الظاهر أن المراد بالباطل هنا ما لا يجوز فعله والمضي وبالصحيح ما يجوز قوله: (وفي الخلاصة وإبطال الأجل الخ) أي إبطال الأجل
كتاب البيع باب المرابحة والتولية ٢٠٤
حالاً[؟] ا نفعاً[؟] وجد بالمبيع عيباً فرده بقضاء عاد الأجل، ولو كان بهذا الدين المؤجل كفيل لا تعود الكفالة في الوجهين اهـ. . وفي الخلاصة وإبطال الأجل يبطل بالشرط الفاسد، ولو قال كلما دخل نجم ولم يؤد فالمال حال صح والمال يصير هـ.
Book of Sale, Chapter on Murabaha and Tawliya. A debt from which the assignee is prevented becomes binding then; thus in Fath al-Qadir. If it becomes binding, if the assignor has something on the assignee, no problem; otherwise the assignor acknowledges the amount assigned to the assignee as deferred to him. He indicated in al-Muhit and al-Zahiriyya: disputed receipt may be deferred. In al-Qunya from Kitab al-Madayanat: the judge ruled for the binding of the term in a loan after he established its deferment, relying on the opinion of Malik and Ibn Abi Layla that it is valid and the term is binding. In Talkhis al-Jami' from Kitab al-Hawala: if one guarantees a present debt as deferred, the principal debtor is delayed even if it is a loan, because the debt is one; it is a trick to defer a loan, for what is intended is established indirectly, like the sale of drinking right and path. What is deferred after guarantee is not binding, since its subject is to add to what is binding by guarantee except the debt; even if reversed, the principal also is delayed... And he did not exclude anything from the invalidity of deferring a loan except in al-Hidaya: if one bequeaths that a loan of one thousand dirhams be given from his wealth to so-and-so for one year, then it becomes binding from his third that they give it and do not demand it before the term, because it is a will of donation like the will of service and dwelling, so it becomes a right of the testator. It is not limited to this case... And in al-Fawa'id al-Fiqhiyya, the exception is not limited to loans; similarly deferring a debt is invalid in cases: first, if the debtor dies and the money becomes due, and the creditor defers, because the debt is in the dhimmah and the benefit of deferment is to trade and pay from the profit of wealth, but if the term holder dies, the property becomes assigned for [repaying] the debt so deferment does not benefit; thus in al-Khulasa. Second, the pre-emptor's deferment of the price is invalid... The summary: deferment of debt is of three types: invalid—deferment of the countervalues in exchange and salam; valid but not binding—loan and debt after death, and deferment of pre-emptor and price after revocation; binding—all other cases. Qadikhan said in his Fatawa: if the debtor says 'I am free of the term' or 'I have no need of the term', it is not cancellation; if he says 'I cancel the term' or 'I abandon it', it becomes due... and if he repays before term and then the payment is reclaimed or found defective and returned, the debt returns to its term. And the cancellation of the term is invalidated by a corrupt condition. And if he says 'whenever a term comes and he does not pay, the money becomes due', it is valid and the money becomes due.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, deals with the ruling on deferring debts (ta'jil al-dayn) in Hanafi fiqh. The author begins by discussing a scenario from hawala (transfer of debt) where deferment becomes binding. He then mentions a key ruling: judges may enforce deferment in loans based on the opinion of Imam Malik and Ibn Abi Layla, indicating a Hanafi deviation from the default position. The text then clarifies that loan deferment is generally invalid, except in a specific case of bequest. The core of the passage is a three-fold categorization of debt deferment: (1) invalid (batil) for deferred counter-values in exchange contracts like sarf (currency exchange) and salam (advance purchase), because these require immediate exchange; (2) valid but not binding (sahih ghayr lazim) for loans and debts after death, and for the pre-emptor's deferment of price or deferment of sale price after revocation (iqala); (3) binding (lazim) for all other debts. The passage then quotes Qadi Khan's fatawa on cancellation of deferment by the debtor, and ends with remarks on cancellation by corrupt conditions and conditional deferment. The author's own comment clarifies that 'invalid' means the action is impermissible and must be abandoned, while 'valid' permits the action. The ruling is presented as the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
تأجيل الدين (ta'jīl al-dayn): Postponement of the due date of a debt to a future term.
بدل الصرف (badal al-ṣarf): The countervalue in a currency exchange contract (sarf); must be exchanged hand-to-hand per Hanafi rules.
بدل السلم (badal al-salam): The price in a salam sale (advance purchase); must be paid at the time of contract.
صحيح غير لازم (ṣaḥīḥ ghayr lāzim): Valid contract but not binding (the party may rescind without penalty).
لازم (lāzim): Binding (a contract or condition that cannot be unilaterally revoked).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of an invalid (bāṭil) deferment?
A) Deferment of a loan (qarḍ)
B) Deferment of the countervalue in a currency exchange (ṣarf)
C) Deferment of a trade debt after revocation of sale (iqāla)
D) Deferment of a debt after the debtor's death

Key Takeaway
Debt deferment in Hanafi fiqh is classified into invalid (bāṭil), valid non-binding (ṣaḥīḥ ghayr lāzim), and binding (lāzim); loan deferment is valid but not binding, so the debtor may repudiate it.

Rules of Valid and Invalid Loans (Qard)
Lists conditions for valid loans, prohibited conditional loans, and related transactions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for a valid loan, explain why conditional loans (qard jar) are prohibited, and apply the Hanafi rulings on related transactions (buying fulus, aslam mali 'alayka, and sale of debt for debt).

Core Idea
A loan is valid only for fungible items; any condition benefiting the lender renders the loan haram (qard jar).

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq summarizes key Hanafi rulings on loans (qard). It establishes the basic validity requirement—loans are only for fungible goods—and then addresses a series of common but impermissible conditional loans (qard jar). It also clarifies the rules for hybrid transactions and the prohibition of certain exchanges. Understanding these rulings helps avoid inadvertent riba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic condition for a valid loan
The text states that a loan is permissible only for fungible items (mithliyyat) such as grains, oils, and eggs. The reasoning (talil) is that a loan is guaranteed by the return of a similar item (mithl). Non-fungible items cannot be loaned because they cannot be standardized as a debt in the dhimma.
Note the distinction: a valid loan (qard sahih) requires return of the same type (mithl), not the specific item, whereas an invalid loan (qard fasid) requires return of the specific item.
2
Recognize prohibited conditional loans (qard jar)
The text gives examples: lending broken dirhams with the condition to return sound ones, or lending food in one place with condition to repay in another. Any condition that brings a benefit to the lender beyond the repayment of the loan is prohibited and the condition is void.
This is based on the principle that a loan should not generate any profit or advantage for the lender (resembling riba).
3
Understand the ruling on repaying better quality without condition
If the borrower voluntarily repays with better quality (e.g., sound dirhams instead of broken) without any prior condition, it is permissible. However, there is a dispute whether the creditor must accept the better quality. The relied-upon Hanafi view is that the creditor is not forced to accept (though some say he is).
This shows the school's caution: even voluntary improvement without condition is allowed, but forcing acceptance would imply an unintended benefit.
4
Apply the rules to related transactions
The text covers: (a) buying fulus (coins) with a debt owed – valid with hand-to-hand possession; (b) 'aslam mali 'alayka' (lender orders borrower to exchange the debt) – prohibited per Abu Hanifa but allowed by the Sahibayn; (c) sale of debt for debt (bay' al-dayn bi al-dayn) – permissible if the parties separate after taking possession.
Each transaction is evaluated for its resemblance to riba or gharar. The Hanafi positions reflect a strict avoidance of speculative or usurious elements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تتمة في مسائل القرض قال في المحيط : ويجوز القرض فيما هو من ذوات الأمثال كالمكيل والموزون والعددي المتقارب كالبيض والجوز لأن القرض مضمون بالمثل، ولا يجوز في غير المثلي لأنه لا يجب ديناً في الذمة ويملكه المستقرض بالقبض كالصحيح والمقبوض بقرض فاسد يتعين للرد، وفي القرض الجائز لا يتعين بل يرد المثل وإن كان قائماً. وعن أبي يوسف ليس له إعطاء غيره إلا برضاه وعارية ما جاز قرضه قرض وما لا يجوز قرضه عارية ولا يجوز قرض جر بأن أقرضه دراهم مكسرة بشرط رد صحيحة أو أقرضه طعاماً في مكان بشرط رده في مكان آخر، فإن قضاه أجود بلا شرط جاز ويجبر الدائن على قبول الأجود وقيل لا؛ كذا في المحيط. وفي الخلاصة : القرض بالشرط حرام والشرط ليس بلازم بأن يقرض على أن يكتب إلى بلد كذا حتى يوفي دينه ا هـ . وفي المحيط : ولا بأس بهدية من عليه القرض والأفضل أن يتورع إذا علم أنه إنما يعطيه لأجل القرض أو أشكل، فإن علم أنه يعطيه لا لأجل القرض بل لقرابة أو صداقة بينهما لا يتورع، وكذا لو كان المستقرض معروفاً بالجود والسخاء جاز. ولا يجوز قرض مملوك أو مكاتب درهماً فصاعداً لأن فيه معنى التبرع. ولو اشترى بقرض له عليه فلوساً جاز ويشترط قبضها في المجلس، ولو أمر المقرض المستقرض أن يصارف بماله عليه لم يجز عند أبي حنيفة خلافاً لهما وهي مسألة أسلم مالي عليك. ولو دفع المستقرض إلى المقرض دراهم ليصرفها بدنانير ويأخد حقه منه فهو وكيل وأمين، فلو تلفت قبل أن يستوفي دينه لا يبطل دينه وبيع الدين بالدين جائز إذا افترقا عن قبضهما
Supplement on issues of loan. He said in al-Muhit: Loan is permissible in things that are fungibles (mithliyyat) like measured, weighed, and close numbers like eggs and walnuts, because a loan is guaranteed by similar (mithl). It is not permissible in non-fungible (non-mithli) because it does not become a debt in the dhimmah and the borrower owns it by taking possession, like a valid loan; what is taken by an invalid loan is specified for return, while in a valid loan it is not specified but a similar must be returned even if the item still exists. From Abu Yusuf: he cannot give other than it except with his consent. Whatever can be loaned can be given as 'ariyah, and whatever cannot be loaned can be 'ariyah. A 'jar' loan is not permissible: he lends him broken dirhams with condition to return sound ones, or he lends him food in one place with condition to return in another. If he repays better without condition, it is permissible and the creditor is forced to accept the better; some say no. Thus in al-Muhit. In al-Khulasa: a conditional loan is haram and the condition is not binding, e.g. he lends on condition that he writes to such-and-such place until he pays his debt. In al-Muhit: There is no problem with a gift from the borrower; it is better to abstain if he knows it is given due to the loan or if unclear. But if he knows it is not due to the loan but due to kinship or friendship, he does not abstain. Similarly if the borrower is known for generosity and munificence, it is permissible. A loan by a slave or a mukatab of a dirham or more is not permissible because it involves donation. If he buys with a loan he has on him coins (fulus), it is permissible, provided he takes possession in the session. If the lender orders the borrower to exchange (sarf) with what he owes him, it is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad); this is the issue of 'aslam mali 'alayka'. If the borrower gives dirhams to the lender to exchange for dinars and take his right from it, then he is a deputy and trustee; if it is lost before he recovers his debt, his debt is not invalidated. The sale of debt for debt is permissible if they separate after taking possession.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a supplement (tammat) on the fiqh of loans (qard). It begins by establishing the basic rule: a loan is valid only for fungible items (mithliyyat) such as grains, oils, eggs, etc., because such debts are repayable in kind (mithl). Non-fungible items (qimiyyat) cannot be loaned because they cannot be standardized in the dhimmah. An invalid loan (qard fasid) requires return of the specific item, whereas a valid loan requires return of the same type even if the original item is still intact. The text then addresses conditional loans, which are strictly prohibited: e.g., lending broken dirhams on condition of returning sound ones, or lending food on condition of returning it elsewhere. However, if the borrower voluntarily repays with better quality without any condition, it is permissible, and according to the relied-upon Hanafi position (contra Zufar), the creditor is obliged to accept the better quality. The passage also discusses prohibition of gifts from the borrower that are motivated by the loan, stating that if the gift is clearly due to kinship or friendship, it is acceptable. Loans by slaves are invalid because they involve donation. The text then covers hybrid transactions: purchasing coins (fulus) with a debt owed to the lender is valid with hand-to-hand possession (qabd in majlis). The ruling on 'aslam mali 'alayka' (a transaction where the borrower is told to exchange the debt money) is prohibited per Abu Hanifa. Finally, the sale of debt for debt (bay' al-dayn bi al-dayn) is permissible if the parties separate after taking possession. These rulings reflect the Hanafi school's emphasis on avoiding riba (usury) and speculative transactions.

Key Terms
القرض الجائز (al-qarḍ al-jā'iz): A valid loan that is not tied to any prohibited condition; the borrower must return the like (mithl) of what was borrowed.
القرض الجر (al-qarḍ al-jarr): A loan that brings a benefit to the lender, e.g., lending broken dirhams with condition to return sound ones, or lending with condition of repayment elsewhere.
ذوات الأمثال (dhawāt al-amthāl): Fungible items: those that can be exactly replaced by similar units, like grains, oil, eggs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on lending broken dirhams with the condition that the borrower returns sound dirhams?
A) Valid and binding
B) Valid but the condition is void
C) Invalid (bātil) and the loan is void
D) Permissible with dislike (makruh)

Key Takeaway
A loan is valid only for fungible items without any condition that benefits the lender; conditional loans (qard jar) are prohibited and the condition is void.

Buying the Loaned Item: Core Ruling and Condition
Explains the basic ruling and clarifies the object of sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the basic ruling for when a borrower buys the loaned item from the lender and distinguish between buying the actual commodity ('ayn) and the debt (dayn).

Core Idea
A borrower may buy the debt of his loan with immediate payment; buying the very same item he borrowed is invalid because he already owns it.

This lesson examines the fundamental rule from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq regarding a transaction often overlooked: the borrower purchasing the loaned item from the lender. The passage clarifies a crucial distinction: whether the purchase involves the specific loaned grain (al-karr al-'ayn) or the debt established in the borrower's liability (al-karr al-dayn). Understanding this distinction is vital to avoid invalid sales.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? (The borrower buying the loaned qar from the lender). What is the initial ruling? (It is permissible, jā'iz).
Note the immediate qualification: this permissibility comes with a condition.
2
Note the condition
What condition is attached to this permissibility? (Payment of the price must occur in the same sitting before parting).
This condition is derived from the prohibition of debt-for-debt exchange.
3
Examine the expert warnings
What does al-‘Imādī emphasize? (This is a crucial chapter that people neglect). What does al-Ramlī clarify? (The 'qar' means the debt, not the physical item, because buying one's own property is invalid).
Al-Ramli's clarification resolves a common misunderstanding.

المجلس) قال في الذخيرة فإن قيض المقرض الثمن من المستقرض قبل أن يتفرقا فالشراء ماض على صحته لأن الافتراق حصل بعد قبض أحد البدلين حقيقة فيما ليس بصرف، وإن افترقا القبض انتقض البيع وعاد الكر ديناً في ذمة قوله : (يجوز ويكره قال في الذخيرة ذكر الخصاف أن هذا جائز وهذا مذهب محمد بن بلخ فإنه أنه كان له سلع وكان إذا استقرض إنسان منه شيئاً كان يبيعه أولاً سلعة بثمن غال ثم روي سلمة إمام
In currency exchange or regarding the receipt of one of the two in non-currency exchange: And if the borrower buys the loaned qar from the lender, it is permissible, and the receipt of its price in the session is stipulated. Then if he paid the price and found a defect in the qar, he returns it, or paying the price in cash makes the contract void. And al-Imadi said: This is a chapter that must be memorized, and everyone is heedless of it. End from Fatawa al-Turi. His statement: 'And if the borrower buys the loaned qar from the lender, it is permissible, etc.' al-Ramli said: By qar is meant the debt established in the borrower's liability, not the actual qar, because purchasing it for him is not permissible since it is his property, as will come. End of al-Ramli's speech. And I say in al-Ashbah from the rulings of ownership: They differed regarding the loan: does the borrower own it by receipt or by disposal? Its benefit is what is in al-Bazzaziyyah: The lender sells to the borrower the borrowed qar that is in the borrower's hand before consumption: it is permissible because it has become the borrower's property; according to the second [opinion] it is not permissible because the borrower does not own it before consumption. End. And let one ponder the suitability of the reasoning for the ruling. End. Al-Hamawi said: Indeed the ruling is the opposite, as in al-Walwaljiyyah, al-Khaniyyah, and others. The cause of confusion is that 'la' fell from the statement of the first copyist from his statement 'it is permissible' where he said: The lender sells to the borrower before consumption: it is permissible, and the correct is 'it is not permissible'. And he added in his statement: 'and according to the second it is not permissible' and the correct is 'it is permissible'. And after correcting its wording by affirming 'la' in the first expression and dropping it from the second, the reasoning remains suitable for the ruling. End of al-Hamawi's speech. I said: And I have seen in two copies of al-Bazzaziyyah: 'it is not permissible' in the first and 'it is permissible' in the second, so there is no confusion. And al-Ramli pointed out in his previous statement a subtle thing: whoever does not notice it falls into error, namely that the lender's sale of the qar to the borrower is sometimes for the very qar he borrowed, and sometimes for that which is in his liability. If the first, then its ruling is what al-Bazzazi restricted by his statement 'the qar that is in the borrower's hand'. So its sale is not permissible if it is still in existence according to the two [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad]. It is said in al-Dhakhirah: Because according to the two, the borrower becomes owner of the qar by the very lending, so he becomes a buyer of his own property. According to Abu Yusuf, the borrowed qar remains the property of the lender, so the borrower becomes a buyer of another's property. And therefore ... it is valid. He said: And if the borrower is the one who sells the qar to the lender, it is permissible; the issue is mentioned without mentioning a dispute, and it is apparent according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because the borrower owns it by the very lending according to them, so he is only selling his own property. And the mashayikh differed on Abu Yusuf's saying: some said it is permissible because, according to his saying, even though the borrower owns it by the very lending, he is entitled to dispose of it by sale, gift, and consumption, so he becomes possessed of it, and by selling to the lender he disposes of it and consumes his ownership, and it ceases from the lender's ownership, so the sale is valid. End of al-Dhakhirah's speech. And if the second [i.e., what is in the liability], then it is said in al-Dhakhirah also: Muhammad said: A man lends a man a qar of food, and the borrower takes possession, then the borrower buys from the lender the qar of food that he owes him for one hundred dinars: it is permissible because the loaned qar is a debt owed by the borrower, not through a currency exchange contract nor a salam contract, and its sale is permissible. Then Muhammad did not mention whether the borrowed qar still exists in the borrower's hand at the time of purchase or is consumed, due to its being permissible absolutely. If it was consumed at the time of purchase, then permissibility is the saying of all because it becomes the borrower's property by consumption, and its equivalent becomes a debt in his liability without dispute. So if he buys the qar that he owes to the lender, he has added the purchase to something existent, so it is valid without dispute. And if it still exists, then the answer is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, because it is owned by the very receipt, and its equivalent becomes a debt in the liability. As for Abu Yusuf's saying, it should not be permissible because, according to his saying, the borrower does not become owner until he consumes it, and its equivalent does not become a debt in the liability before that. So if he adds the purchase to the qar that is in his liability, and there is no qar in his liability, he has added it to the non-existent, so it is not permissible. End. His statement: 'And the receipt of its substitute in the session is stipulated' – it is said in al-Dhakhirah: If the lender takes the price from the borrower before they part, the purchase remains valid because the parting occurred after the receipt of one of the two substitutes in reality in what is not currency exchange. And if they part before receipt, the sale is rescinded and the qar returns as a debt in the borrower's liability because the parting occurred on a debt for a debt. If it is said: The contract should not be invalidated because the qar in the borrower's liability is in the ruling of received. The answer: Even though it is in the ruling of received, it is a debt in reality, so if the dirhams are not received, it is a debt in reality and in ruling, and the preponderance is for the aspect of debtness, and consideration is given to the preponderant. End. And its completion in it is his statement: 'Then if he paid the price, etc.' – al-Ramli said: He is entitled to return it and claim the diminution due to the defect because he bought what was in his liability and paid him its price on the basis that it was sound, so when it appeared defective, he claims its diminution. As for the qar that is returned, it is not the sold item, contrary to the case where he bought it with a like qar, where he does not claim the diminution because that would be riba. For when a ribawi is sold for its genus, the condition is equality, and any excess is riba absolutely, whether sound or defective. So ponder. His statement: 'It is permissible and disliked' – it is said in al-Dhakhirah: al-Khassaf mentioned that this is permissible and this is the madhhab of Muhammad ibn Balkh, for he had goods, and when someone borrowed something from him, he would first sell a commodity at a high price, then ... it is narrated ... Imam
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a detailed commentary on the ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding a borrower purchasing the loaned item (qard) from the lender. The passage type is a ruling with proof, as it provides legal reasoning and intramadhhab disputes. The core ruling states that if the borrower buys the loaned qar (a measure of grain) from the lender, it is permissible only if the price is paid in the same sitting before parting. If the price is paid but the item is found defective, the buyer may return it and claim the diminution in value. However, if the price is paid in cash (naqd) without sitting conditions, the contract is void. This ruling is critical and often overlooked, as noted by al-Imadi. The commentary then clarifies that 'qar' here refers to the debt in the borrower's liability, not the physical item, because buying one's own property is invalid. A major intramadhhab dispute arises: do borrowers own the loaned item upon receipt (qabd) or only upon consumption (tasarruf)? According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), ownership occurs with receipt; according to Abu Yusuf, ownership occurs only after consumption. This affects whether the borrower can buy the very item from the lender; according to the two it is invalid (he would be buying his own property), while according to Abu Yusuf it may be valid (since it remains the lender's property). However, a textual corruption in al-Bazzaziyyah caused confusion, corrected by al-Hamawi: the correct text states it is not permissible in the first case (buying the actual item) and permissible in the second (buying the debt). The passage then distinguishes two scenarios: (1) buying the specific loaned item that still exists – according to the two it is not permissible, but according to Abu Yusuf it is permissible because the borrower becomes owner by disposal; (2) buying the debt (what is in the liability) – it is permissible whether the item is consumed or still exists, according to all, though Abu Yusuf's view on existence is problematic because the debt is not established before consumption. The condition of payment in the sitting is explained: if the price is paid before parting, the sale stands; if they part without payment, the sale is void because it becomes a debt-for-debt exchange. Finally, the defect ruling: if the buyer finds a defect, he may claim the deficiency because he bought a debt (the item in the dhimma); if he had bought it with a like qar (e.g., wheat for wheat), he cannot claim deficiency because any excess over equality would be riba.

Key Terms
الكرّ (al-karr): A measure of grain, often wheat or barley, used as a standard unit in Hanafi fiqh for loans and sales.
المستقرض (al-mustaqrid): The borrower who takes a loan (qard).
المقرض (al-muqrid): The lender who gives the loan.
المجلس (al-majlis): The session or sitting in which the contract is concluded; used here to require immediate payment to avoid separation before settlement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the fundamental condition for the borrower's purchase of the loaned qar from the lender to be valid?
A) The qar must be of the same type.
B) The price must be paid before the parties part.
C) The borrower must have already consumed the qar.
D) The lender must agree to sell at a discount.

Key Takeaway
A borrower may buy the debt (dayn) from the lender with immediate payment; buying the specific 'ayn is invalid because it is already owned by the borrower.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Intra-Madhhab Dispute: Ownership by Receipt vs. Consumption
Explains the intra-madhhab dispute on ownership timing and its effect on the validity of buying the 'ayn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding ownership of the loaned item and apply it to determine the validity of buying the specific 'ayn.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: ownership by receipt; Abu Yusuf: ownership by consumption. This determines if buying the 'ayn is valid.

This lesson delves into the intramadhhab dispute on the exact moment a borrower becomes owner of the loaned item. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, citing al-Bazzaziyyah and al-Dhakhirah, reveals a subtle difference that has practical consequences for the validity of buying the very item borrowed. Understanding this dispute is key to navigating similar transactions.

Guided Path
1
State the legal question
What is the issue being contested? (Does the borrower own the loaned item upon receipt or only upon consumption/disposal?)
2
Identify the two positions
What are the positions of the three main Hanafi imams? (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: ownership by receipt; Abu Yusuf: ownership by consumption).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Apply to the case of buying the 'ayn
How does each position affect the ruling when the borrower buys the specific loaned item from the lender? (Majority: invalid because it is own property; Abu Yusuf: valid because it is still lender's property).
4
Note the textual correction
What textual error in al-Bazzaziyyah caused confusion, and how was it corrected? (Al-Hamawi corrected a misplaced 'lā' that reversed the positions).
This shows the importance of textual criticism.

في الصرف أو عن قبض أحدهما في غير الصرف ولو اشترى المستقرض الكر القرض من المقرض جاز ويشترط قبض ثمنه في المجلس، فإن أدى الثمن فوجد بالكر عيباً رده أو نقد الثمن كان العقد باطلاً. وقال العمادي وهذا فصل لأنه ملكه كما سيأتي اهـ كلام الرملي. وأقول في الأشباه من أحكام الملك: اختلفوا في القرض هل يملكه المستقرض بالقبض أو بالتصرف؟ وفائدته ما في البزازية باع المقرض من المستقرض الكر المستقرض الذي في يد المستقرض قبل الاستهلاك يجوز لأنه صار ملكاً للمستقرض، وعند الثاني لا يجوز لأنه لا يملك المستقرض قبل الاستهلاك اهـ وليتأمل في مناسبة التعليل للحكم .اهـ. قال الحموي : فإن الحكم بالعكس كما في الولوالجية والخانية وغيرهما. وسبب الإشكال أن «لا» سقطت من كلام الناسخ الأول من قوله «يجوز حيث قال: باع المقرض من المستقرض قبل الاستهلاك يجوز والصواب «لا يجوز». وزاد في قوله وعند الثاني لا يجوز والصواب يجوز وبعد إصلاح عبارتها بإثبات لا في» العبارة الأولى وإسقاطها من الثانية بقي التعليل مناسباً للحكم . اهـ كلام الحموي. قلت : وقد رأيت في نسختين من البزازية لا يجوز في الأول ويجوز في الثاني فلا إشكال. هذا وقد نبه الرملي في عبارته السابقة على شيء دقيق من لم يلاحظه يقع في الخبط أن وهو بيع المقرض الكر من المستقرض تارة يكون للكر الذي استقرضه بعينه، وتارة يكون للذي في غدته، فإن كان الأول فحكمه ما قيده البزازي بقوله الكر الذي في يد المستقرض . فلا يجوز بيعه إذا كان قائماً عندهما. قال في الذخيرة : لأن عندهما المستقرض يصير ملكاً للمستقرض بنفس القرض فيصير مشترياً ملك نفسه . على قول أبي يوسف فالكر المستقرض باقٍ على ملك المقرض فيصير المستقرض شارياً ملك غيره مر ولذا أما فيصح . قال : ولو كان المستقرض هو الذي باع الكر من المقرض جاز ذكر المسألة من غير ذكر خلاف وأنه ظاهر على قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد لأن المستقرض ملكه بنفس القرض عندهما فإنما باع ملك لا نفسه. واختلف المشايخ على قول أبي يوسف بعضهم قالوا يجوز لأنه على قوله وإن كان المستقرض يملكه بنفس القرض إلا أنه يملك التصرف فيه بيعاً وهبة واستهلاكاً فيصير متملكاً له، وبالبيع من المقرض صار متصرفاً فيه ومستهلكاً على نفسه ملكه وزال عن ملك المقرض فصح البيع منه . اهـ كلام الذخيرة. وإن كان الثاني فقد قال في الذخيرة أيضاً قال محمد رجل أقرض رجلاً كراً من طعام وقبضه المستقرض، ثم إن المستقرض اشترى من المقرض الكر الطعام الذي له عليه بمائة دينار جاز لأن الكر القرض دين وجب على المستقرض لا بعقد الصرف ولا بعقد السلم وبيعه جائز. ثم إن محمداً لم يذكر أن الكر المستقرض قائم في يد المستقرض وقت الشراء أو مستهلك لجوازه مطلقاً، فإن كان مستهلكاً وقت الشراء فالجواز قول الكل لأنه يصير ملكاً للمستقرض بالاستهلاك ويجب مثله ديناً في ذمته بلا خلاف، فإذا اشترى الكر الذي عليه للمقرض فقد أضاف الشراء إلى ما هو موجود فيصح بلا خلاف، وإن قائماً فالجواب قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد رحمه الله لأنه مملوكاً بنفس القبض يصير ويجب مثله ديناً في الذمة. أما على قول أبي يوسف ينبغي أن لا يجوز لأنه على قوله لا يصير ملكاً للمستقرض ما لم يستهلكه، ولا يجب مثله ديناً في الذمة قبله، وإن أضاف الشراء إلى الكر الذي في ذمته ولا كر في ذمته فقد أضافه إلى المعدوم فلا يجوز اهـ. قوله: (ويشترط قبض بدله في المجلس) قال في الذخيرة فإن قيض المقرض الثمن من المستقرض قبل أن يتفرقا فالشراء ماض على صحته لأن الافتراق حصل بعد قبض أحد البدلين حقيقة فيما ليس بصرف، وإن افترقا القبض انتقض البيع وعاد الكر ديناً في ذمة المستقرض لأن الافتراق حصل عن دين بدين. فإن قيل : ينبغي أن لا يبطل العقد لأن الكر في ذمة المستقرض في حكم المقبوض. والجواب أنه وإن كان في حكم المقبوض إلا أنه دين حقيقة فالدراهم إذا لم تقبض فهو دين حقيقة وحكماً وكان الرجحان لجانب الدينية والعبرة للراجح .اهـ. وتمامه فيها قوله : (فإن أدى الثمن الخ) قال الرملي إنما كان له رده والرجوع بنقصان العيب لأنه شرى ما في ذمته ودفع له ثمنه على أنه سليم فبان معيباً فيرجع بنقصانه، وأما الكر المردود فليس هو المبيع بخلاف ما إذا اشتراه بكر مثله حيث لا يرجع بالنقصان لأنه يكون ربا إذ الربوي إذا بيع بجنسه فالشرط المساواة والزائد ربا مطلقاً سليماً كان أو معيباً فتأمل . قوله : (يجوز ويكره قال في الذخيرة ذكر الخصاف أن هذا جائز وهذا مذهب محمد بن بلخ فإنه أنه كان له سلع وكان إذا استقرض إنسان منه شيئاً كان يبيعه أولاً سلعة بثمن غال ثم روي سلمة إمام
In currency exchange or regarding the receipt of one of the two in non-currency exchange: And if the borrower buys the loaned qar from the lender, it is permissible, and the receipt of its price in the session is stipulated. Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a detailed commentary on the ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding a borrower purchasing the loaned item (qard) from the lender. The passage type is a ruling with proof, as it provides legal reasoning and intramadhhab disputes. The core ruling states that if the borrower buys the loaned qar (a measure of grain) from the lender, it is permissible only if the price is paid in the same sitting before parting. If the price is paid but the item is found defective, the buyer may return it and claim the diminution in value. However, if the price is paid in cash (naqd) without sitting conditions, the contract is void. This ruling is critical and often overlooked, as noted by al-Imadi. The commentary then clarifies that 'qar' here refers to the debt in the borrower's liability, not the physical item, because buying one's own property is invalid. A major intramadhhab dispute arises: do borrowers own the loaned item upon receipt (qabd) or only upon consumption (tasarruf)? According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), ownership occurs with receipt; according to Abu Yusuf, ownership occurs only after consumption. This affects whether the borrower can buy the very item from the lender; according to the two it is invalid (he would be buying his own property), while according to Abu Yusuf it may be valid (since it remains the lender's property). However, a textual corruption in al-Bazzaziyyah caused confusion, corrected by al-Hamawi: the correct text states it is not permissible in the first case (buying the actual item) and permissible in the second (buying the debt). The passage then distinguishes two scenarios: (1) buying the specific loaned item that still exists – according to the two it is not permissible, but according to Abu Yusuf it is permissible because the borrower becomes owner by disposal; (2) buying the debt (what is in the liability) – it is permissible whether the item is consumed or still exists, according to all, though Abu Yusuf's view on existence is problematic because the debt is not established before consumption. The condition of payment in the sitting is explained: if the price is paid before parting, the sale stands; if they part without payment, the sale is void because it becomes a debt-for-debt exchange. Finally, the defect ruling: if the buyer finds a defect, he may claim the deficiency because he bought a debt (the item in the dhimma); if he had bought it with a like qar (e.g., wheat for wheat), he cannot claim deficiency because any excess over equality would be riba.

Key Terms
القبض (al-qabd): Receipt or taking possession; in this context, the moment the borrower receives the loaned item.
التصرف (al-tasarruf): Disposal or consumption; the act of using or selling the item, which Abu Yusuf requires for full ownership.
الاستهلاك (al-istihlak): Consumption; using up the item so that it no longer exists in its original form.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the corrected text of al-Bazzaziyyah, what is the ruling on the lender selling the borrowed qar (the 'ayn) to the borrower before the borrower consumes it?
A) Valid according to all.
B) Invalid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; valid according to Abu Yusuf.
C) Valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; invalid according to Abu Yusuf.
D) Invalid according to all.

Key Takeaway
The ownership dispute affects whether buying the specific 'ayn is valid; the mufta bihi (majority) says invalid.

Conditions of Payment and Defect Claims
Explains the condition of payment and the rules for defect claims, including the riba consideration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why payment in the sitting is required and how defect claims are handled when buying the debt from the lender, including the special case of buying with like-kind goods.

Core Idea
Payment in the sitting prevents debt-for-debt exchange; defect claims allow return of deficiency but not if buying with same genus due to riba.

This lesson focuses on two critical aspects of the transaction: the condition of immediate payment and the rules for defects. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, citing al-Dhakhirah, explains why payment must be in the sitting to avoid riba al-nasi'ah, and what happens if the purchased debt turns out to be defective. A special nuance arises when the price is paid in the same genus (e.g., wheat for wheat) – here, defect claims are restricted to prevent riba al-fadl.

Guided Path
1
Understand the condition of payment in the sitting
Why must the price be paid before the parties part? (To prevent the transaction from becoming a sale of debt for debt, which is prohibited).
This is based on qiyas to sarf (currency exchange).
2
Analyze the consequence of parting without payment
What happens if they part before payment? (The sale is rescinded, and the qar returns as a debt in the borrower's liability).
This is because the contract becomes a debt-for-debt exchange.
3
Examine the defect ruling
If the borrower finds a defect in the qar after payment, what are his options? (He can return the qar and claim the diminution in value, but the returned qar is not the original sold item).
The original sold item was the debt in the dhimma, not the physical qar.
4
Distinguish the case of like-kind payment
What if the borrower buys the qar with a similar qar (e.g., wheat for wheat)? (He cannot claim a refund for defect because any difference in value would be riba – equality is required in ribawi transactions).
This is crucial: defect claims are not allowed when the price is of the same genus (ribawi).

In currency exchange or regarding the receipt of one of the two in non-currency exchange: And if the borrower buys the loaned qar from the lender, it is permissible, and the receipt of its price in the session is stipulated. Then if he paid the price and found a defect in the qar, he returns it, or paying the price in cash makes the contract void. And al-Imadi said: This is a chapter that must be memorized, and everyone is heedless of it. End from Fatawa al-Turi. His statement: 'And if the borrower buys the loaned qar from the lender, it is permissible, etc.' al-Ramli said: By qar is meant the debt established in the borrower's liability, not the actual qar, because purchasing it for him is not permissible since it is his property, as will come. End of al-Ramli's speech. And I say in al-Ashbah from the rulings of ownership: They differed regarding the loan: does the borrower own it by receipt or by disposal? Its benefit is what is in al-Bazzaziyyah: The lender sells to the borrower the borrowed qar that is in the borrower's hand before consumption: it is permissible because it has become the borrower's property; according to the second [opinion] it is not permissible because the borrower does not own it before consumption. End. And let one ponder the suitability of the reasoning for the ruling. End. Al-Hamawi said: Indeed the ruling is the opposite, as in al-Walwaljiyyah, al-Khaniyyah, and others. The cause of confusion is that 'la' fell from the statement of the first copyist from his statement 'it is permissible' where he said: The lender sells to the borrower before consumption: it is permissible, and the correct is 'it is not permissible'. And he added in his statement: 'and according to the second it is not permissible' and the correct is 'it is permissible'. And after correcting its wording by affirming 'la' in the first expression and dropping it from the second, the reasoning remains suitable for the ruling. End of al-Hamawi's speech. I said: And I have seen in two copies of al-Bazzaziyyah: 'it is not permissible' in the first and 'it is permissible' in the second, so there is no confusion. And al-Ramli pointed out in his previous statement a subtle thing: whoever does not notice it falls into error, namely that the lender's sale of the qar to the borrower is sometimes for the very qar he borrowed, and sometimes for that which is in his liability. If the first, then its ruling is what al-Bazzazi restricted by his statement 'the qar that is in the borrower's hand'. So its sale is not permissible if it is still in existence according to the two [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad]. It is said in al-Dhakhirah: Because according to the two, the borrower becomes owner of the qar by the very lending, so he becomes a buyer of his own property. According to Abu Yusuf, the borrowed qar remains the property of the lender, so the borrower becomes a buyer of another's property. And therefore ... it is valid. He said: And if the borrower is the one who sells the qar to the lender, it is permissible; the issue is mentioned without mentioning a dispute, and it is apparent according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because the borrower owns it by the very lending according to them, so he is only selling his own property. And the mashayikh differed on Abu Yusuf's saying: some said it is permissible because, according to his saying, even though the borrower owns it by the very lending, he is entitled to dispose of it by sale, gift, and consumption, so he becomes possessed of it, and by selling to the lender he disposes of it and consumes his ownership, and it ceases from the lender's ownership, so the sale is valid. End of al-Dhakhirah's speech. And if the second [i.e., what is in the liability], then it is said in al-Dhakhirah also: Muhammad said: A man lends a man a qar of food, and the borrower takes possession, then the borrower buys from the lender the qar of food that he owes him for one hundred dinars: it is permissible because the loaned qar is a debt owed by the borrower, not through a currency exchange contract nor a salam contract, and its sale is permissible. Then Muhammad did not mention whether the borrowed qar still exists in the borrower's hand at the time of purchase or is consumed, due to its being permissible absolutely. If it was consumed at the time of purchase, then permissibility is the saying of all because it becomes the borrower's property by consumption, and its equivalent becomes a debt in his liability without dispute. So if he buys the qar that he owes to the lender, he has added the purchase to something existent, so it is valid without dispute. And if it still exists, then the answer is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, because it is owned by the very receipt, and its equivalent becomes a debt in the liability. As for Abu Yusuf's saying, it should not be permissible because, according to his saying, the borrower does not become owner until he consumes it, and its equivalent does not become a debt in the liability before that. So if he adds the purchase to the qar that is in his liability, and there is no qar in his liability, he has added it to the non-existent, so it is not permissible. End. His statement: 'And the receipt of its substitute in the session is stipulated' – it is said in al-Dhakhirah: If the lender takes the price from the borrower before they part, the purchase remains valid because the parting occurred after the receipt of one of the two substitutes in reality in what is not currency exchange. And if they part before receipt, the sale is rescinded and the qar returns as a debt in the borrower's liability because the parting occurred on a debt for a debt. If it is said: The contract should not be invalidated because the qar in the borrower's liability is in the ruling of received. The answer: Even though it is in the ruling of received, it is a debt in reality, so if the dirhams are not received, it is a debt in reality and in ruling, and the preponderance is for the aspect of debtness, and consideration is given to the preponderant. End. And its completion in it is his statement: 'Then if he paid the price, etc.' – al-Ramli said: He is entitled to return it and claim the diminution due to the defect because he bought what was in his liability and paid him its price on the basis that it was sound, so when it appeared defective, he claims its diminution. As for the qar that is returned, it is not the sold item, contrary to the case where he bought it with a like qar, where he does not claim the diminution because that would be riba. For when a ribawi is sold for its genus, the condition is equality, and any excess is riba absolutely, whether sound or defective. So ponder. His statement: 'It is permissible and disliked' – it is said in al-Dhakhirah: al-Khassaf mentioned that this is permissible and this is the madhhab of Muhammad ibn Balkh, for he had goods, and when someone borrowed something from him, he would first sell a commodity at a high price, then ... it is narrated ... Imam
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a detailed commentary on the ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding a borrower purchasing the loaned item (qard) from the lender. The passage type is a ruling with proof, as it provides legal reasoning and intramadhhab disputes. The core ruling states that if the borrower buys the loaned qar (a measure of grain) from the lender, it is permissible only if the price is paid in the same sitting before parting. If the price is paid but the item is found defective, the buyer may return it and claim the diminution in value. However, if the price is paid in cash (naqd) without sitting conditions, the contract is void. This ruling is critical and often overlooked, as noted by al-Imadi. The commentary then clarifies that 'qar' here refers to the debt in the borrower's liability, not the physical item, because buying one's own property is invalid. A major intramadhhab dispute arises: do borrowers own the loaned item upon receipt (qabd) or only upon consumption (tasarruf)? According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), ownership occurs with receipt; according to Abu Yusuf, ownership occurs only after consumption. This affects whether the borrower can buy the very item from the lender; according to the two it is invalid (he would be buying his own property), while according to Abu Yusuf it may be valid (since it remains the lender's property). However, a textual corruption in al-Bazzaziyyah caused confusion, corrected by al-Hamawi: the correct text states it is not permissible in the first case (buying the actual item) and permissible in the second (buying the debt). The passage then distinguishes two scenarios: (1) buying the specific loaned item that still exists – according to the two it is not permissible, but according to Abu Yusuf it is permissible because the borrower becomes owner by disposal; (2) buying the debt (what is in the liability) – it is permissible whether the item is consumed or still exists, according to all, though Abu Yusuf's view on existence is problematic because the debt is not established before consumption. The condition of payment in the sitting is explained: if the price is paid before parting, the sale stands; if they part without payment, the sale is void because it becomes a debt-for-debt exchange. Finally, the defect ruling: if the buyer finds a defect, he may claim the deficiency because he bought a debt (the item in the dhimma); if he had bought it with a like qar (e.g., wheat for wheat), he cannot claim deficiency because any excess over equality would be riba.

Key Terms
القبض في المجلس (al-qabd fī al-majlis): Receipt of the price in the same sitting to avoid debt-for-debt.
العيب (al-‘ayb): Defect in the item delivered that reduces its value.
الربوي (al-ribawī): A commodity subject to riba rules (e.g., wheat, barley, gold, silver).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the passage say that if the parties part before payment, the sale is rescinded?
A) Because the contract becomes a debt-for-debt exchange.
B) Because the borrower loses ownership.
C) Because the lender changes his mind.
D) Because the qar is not yet consumed.

Key Takeaway
Payment in the sitting is essential to avoid debt-for-debt; defect claims are allowed for debt purchases but not when paying with the same ribawi genus.

Buying a Cheap Item at an Exorbitant Price to Obtain a Loan
Ruling statement on a type of disguised loan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on buying a paltry item at an inflated price for the purpose of obtaining a loan and explain why it is permissible but disliked.

Core Idea
A sale with inflated price to facilitate a loan is permissible but disliked if done out of need.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from al-Qunyah on a transaction that resembles a disguised loan. Understanding this ruling helps distinguish valid sales from prohibited forms of riba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction
The transaction is buying a cheap item (shay' yasir) at a high price (thaman ghalin) with the need for a loan.
2
Note the condition of need
The ruling is conditional upon having a need (haja) for the loan.
Need is a mitigating factor.
3
Determine the ruling
The ruling is 'yajuz wa yukrah' – permissible but disliked.
Dislike is tanzihan (not sinful but discouraged).
4
Reflect on the reasoning
Why disliked? Because it resembles riba (usury) due to the disparity between price and value.
The need justifies permissibility, but the resemblance to riba causes karaha.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي القنية من باب القروض شراء الشيء اليسير بثمن غال إذا كان له حاجة إلى القرض يجوز ويكره. استقرض عشرة دراهم فأرسل عبده ليأخذها من المقرض فقال المقرض دفعته إليه وأقر العبد به وقال دفعتها إلى مولاي وأنكر المولى قبض العبد العشرة فالقول له ولا شيء عليه، ولا يرجع المقرض على العبد لأنه أقر أنه قبضها بحق. استقراض الدقيق وزناً يجوز والاحتياط أن يبرئ كل صاحبه والجواز رواية عن أبي يوسف، ورواية الأصل بخلافه . استقراض الحنطة وزناً يجوز ، وعنهما خلافه . بخاري استقرض من سمرقندي حنطة ليدفعها ببخاري ليس له المطالبة إلا بسمرقند، وفي استقراض السرقين اختلاف المشايخ بناء على أنه مثلي أو قيمي واستقراض العجين في بلادنا وزناً يجوز لا جزافاً، ولم يتعرض لاستقراض الخميرة وينبغي الجواز من غير وزن وسئل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن خميرة يتعاطاها الجيوان أيكون ربا؟ فقال: «ما رآه المسلمون حسناً فهو حسن عند الله وما رآه المسلمون قبيحاً فهو عند الله قبيح. أنفق من قصاب لحوم ولم يذكر أنه قرض أو شراء فذلك قرض فاسد يملكه
And in al-Qunyah, from the chapter on loans: Buying a paltry item at an exorbitant price if one has a need for the loan is permissible but disliked. He borrowed ten dirhams and sent his slave to take them from the lender, and the lender said, 'I gave them to him,' and the slave acknowledged it and said, 'I gave them to my master,' and the master denied the slave's receipt of the ten. The word is the master's, and nothing is upon him, and the lender does not recourse against the slave because he acknowledged that he took them rightfully. Borrowing flour by weight is permissible, and the precaution is that each exonerate the other, and permissibility is a narration from Abu Yusuf, while the original narration opposes it. Borrowing wheat by weight is permissible, and from them there is opposition to it. A Bukhari borrowed wheat from a Samarqandi to deliver it in Bukhara; he is not entitled to demand except in Samarqand. And concerning borrowing manure, there is disagreement among the mashayikh based on whether it is a commodity of weight/measure or of value. And borrowing dough in our lands by weight is permissible, not by estimation. And he did not address borrowing yeast, and it should be permissible without weight. And the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, was asked about yeast traded between people: is it riba? He said: 'What the Muslims see as good is good in the sight of Allah, and what the Muslims see as evil is evil in the sight of Allah.' He spent on a butcher for meat and did not mention whether it was a loan or a purchase; that is an invalid loan; he owns it
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq cites rulings from al-Qunyah on various loan-related issues. The passage type is a series of ruling statements without detailed proofs. The first ruling addresses buying a small item at an inflated price if one needs the loan: it is permissible but disliked (makruh tanzihan). Then follows a case of agency in loan receipt: if a lender claims to have given the loan to the borrower's slave, and the slave admits but the master denies, the master's word is accepted, and the lender cannot claim from the slave because the slave admitted receiving it legitimately. Next, borrowing flour by weight is permissible (according to a narration from Abu Yusuf), but the original narration (Zahir al-Riwayah) is different (likely that borrowing flour is not permissible because it is not a standard practice). Similarly, borrowing wheat by weight is permissible, though there is opposition from the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Then, a case of borrowing wheat in one city to be repaid in another: the creditor cannot demand repayment except in the city of the loan (Samarqand). Borrowing manure (intrinsically impure?) is disputed based on whether it is considered a fungible (mithli) or non-fungible (qimi) commodity. Borrowing dough by weight is permissible in the author's land, but not by estimation. Borrowing yeast is probably permissible without weight because it is not a standard commodity for weight. Finally, a hadith is quoted about yeast: the Prophet (saw) said that what Muslims consider good is good, etc. The last line is incomplete: someone spent on a butcher for meat without specifying loan or purchase; the ruling is that it is an invalid loan (qard fasid) but the meat is owned by the recipient. The passage ends abruptly.

Key Terms
القنية (al-qunyah): A well-known Hanafi jurisprudential work by Imam al-Zayla'i.
القرض (al-qard): Loan; in this transaction, the need for a loan is the cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Permissible and recommended.
D) Permissible only if the price is not too high.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits buying a cheap item at an inflated price for need but considers it disliked due to resemblance to riba.

Agency in Loan Receipt: Dispute between Lender and Borrower
Ruling statement on agency dispute in loan receipt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling when a lender claims to have given the loan to the borrower's agent and the borrower denies receipt.

Core Idea
If a lender gives a loan to a slave sent by the borrower, the word of the borrower (master) is taken over the lender's word.

This lesson deals with a scenario where a loan is entrusted to an agent (slave) and a dispute arises. Understanding this ruling clarifies the burden of proof in loan-related agency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the dispute
Borrower sends slave to receive loan. Lender claims he gave to slave. Slave admits but master denies receiving.
2
Determine whose statement is accepted
The master's word (denial) is accepted (al-qawl lahu).
The master is not liable.
3
Consequence for the lender
Lender cannot recourse against the slave because slave admitted taking it rightfully (as agent).
The lender's only recourse is to the borrower, but borrower denies.
4
Reasoning
The slave's admission is not binding on the master because the master did not acknowledge it. The lender should have ensured delivery to the master directly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي القنية من باب القروض شراء الشيء اليسير بثمن غال إذا كان له حاجة إلى القرض يجوز ويكره. استقرض عشرة دراهم فأرسل عبده ليأخذها من المقرض فقال المقرض دفعته إليه وأقر العبد به وقال دفعتها إلى مولاي وأنكر المولى قبض العبد العشرة فالقول له ولا شيء عليه، ولا يرجع المقرض على العبد لأنه أقر أنه قبضها بحق. استقراض الدقيق وزناً يجوز والاحتياط أن يبرئ كل صاحبه والجواز رواية عن أبي يوسف، ورواية الأصل بخلافه . استقراض الحنطة وزناً يجوز ، وعنهما خلافه . بخاري استقرض من سمرقندي حنطة ليدفعها ببخاري ليس له المطالبة إلا بسمرقند، وفي استقراض السرقين اختلاف المشايخ بناء على أنه مثلي أو قيمي واستقراض العجين في بلادنا وزناً يجوز لا جزافاً، ولم يتعرض لاستقراض الخميرة وينبغي الجواز من غير وزن وسئل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن خميرة يتعاطاها الجيوان أيكون ربا؟ فقال: «ما رآه المسلمون حسناً فهو حسن عند الله وما رآه المسلمون قبيحاً فهو عند الله قبيح. أنفق من قصاب لحوم ولم يذكر أنه قرض أو شراء فذلك قرض فاسد يملكه
And in al-Qunyah, from the chapter on loans: Buying a paltry item at an exorbitant price if one has a need for the loan is permissible but disliked. He borrowed ten dirhams and sent his slave to take them from the lender, and the lender said, 'I gave them to him,' and the slave acknowledged it and said, 'I gave them to my master,' and the master denied the slave's receipt of the ten. The word is the master's, and nothing is upon him, and the lender does not recourse against the slave because he acknowledged that he took them rightfully. Borrowing flour by weight is permissible, and the precaution is that each exonerate the other, and permissibility is a narration from Abu Yusuf, while the original narration opposes it. Borrowing wheat by weight is permissible, and from them there is opposition to it. A Bukhari borrowed wheat from a Samarqandi to deliver it in Bukhara; he is not entitled to demand except in Samarqand. And concerning borrowing manure, there is disagreement among the mashayikh based on whether it is a commodity of weight/measure or of value. And borrowing dough in our lands by weight is permissible, not by estimation. And he did not address borrowing yeast, and it should be permissible without weight. And the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, was asked about yeast traded between people: is it riba? He said: 'What the Muslims see as good is good in the sight of Allah, and what the Muslims see as evil is evil in the sight of Allah.' He spent on a butcher for meat and did not mention whether it was a loan or a purchase; that is an invalid loan; he owns it
