Borrowing Fungible Commodities: Flour, Wheat, Manure, Dough, and Yeast
Series of ruling statements on borrowing various commodities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on borrowing various fungible commodities and identify the conditions for permissibility.

Core Idea
Borrowing flour and wheat by weight is permissible per one narration, but the original view opposes; borrowing non-standard items like manure is disputed based on whether they are mithli or qimi.

This lesson surveys several rulings on borrowing commodities that are measured by weight or volume. The rulings vary by commodity and by narration, reflecting intra-Hanafi differences and the importance of custom (urf) in determining whether something is fungible.

Guided Path
1
Identify each commodity and the ruling
Flour (dawaq) and wheat (hinta) are ruled permissible to borrow by weight, but with a narration opposing. Manure (sirqin) is disputed based on its classification. Dough (ajin) is permissible by weight, not by estimation. Yeast (khamira) is probably permissible without weight.
2
Understand the basis of dispute
For flour and wheat, the dispute is between a narration from Abu Yusuf (permissible) and the original narration (Zahir al-Riwayah) which likely prohibited. The 'original narration' is usually the dominant view.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Examine the geographic restriction
A Bukhari (from Bukhara) borrowed wheat from a Samarqandi; the creditor cannot demand repayment except in Samarqand (place of contract).
Place of performance is the place of contract unless agreed otherwise.
4
Apply the mithli/qimi distinction
Manure is disputed because it may not be standardizable, so scholars differ on whether it is mithli (fungible, like wheat) or qimi (value-based).
5
Note the custom-based ruling
Dough is borrowed by weight according to the custom of the author's land (biladuna). Yeast is likely permissible without weight because it is not typically weighed. The hadith supports that Muslim custom ('urf) is a valid source.

Source Text

قيمي (qimi): Non-fungible commodity that varies in value and cannot be exactly replaced; loans of qimi are invalid.

The Hanafi Definition of Riba and Its Explicit Conditions
Defines riba and explains conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of riba and identify its essential conditions (excess, without compensation, exchange, and stipulation).

Core Idea
Riba is an excess without compensation in an exchange of homogeneous goods measured by weight or volume.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes the foundational definition of riba in Hanafi fiqh. It begins with the linguistic meaning (excess), then specifies that not every excess is riba—only a particular type. The author, al-Marghinani, then gives the technical definition, breaking it down into key conditions. Understanding these conditions is essential to distinguish lawful profit from prohibited riba.

Guided Path
1
State the linguistic meaning
Identify the literal meaning of riba (excess/increase) and note that it is maqsur (defective noun).
The dual forms and attribution are also discussed.
2
Recognize the need for a technical definition
Understand that absolute excess is not riba by consensus; a specific type is intended.
Example: opening markets for profit is allowed.
3
Identify the technical definition
Locate the phrase: 'فضل مال بلا عوض في معاوضة مال بمال' and note its components.
This is the core definition.
4
Unpack each condition
List the explicit conditions: (1) excess (فضل), (2) without compensation (بلا عوض), (3) in an exchange (معاوضة).
The author also mentions homogeneity and the legal standard (weight/volume) as part of 'excess'.
5
Note the omitted condition
Identify the additional condition that the excess must be stipulated in the contract for one party, as clarified from al-Wiqayah.
This condition is necessary but not stated in the original matn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الربا
وجه مناسبته للمرابحة أن في كل منهما زيادة إلا أن تلك حلال وهذه حرام والحل هو الأصل في الأشياء فقدم ما يتعلق بتلك الزيادة على ما يتعلق بهذه والربا بكسر الراء وفتحها خطأ. وفي المصباح : الربا بالفضل والزيادة وهو مقصور على الأشهر، ويثني ربوان بالواو على الأصل وقد يقال ربيان على التخفيف وينسب إليه على لفظه فيقال ربوي؛ قاله أبو عبيد وغيره. وزاد المطرزي فقال : الفتح في النسبة خطأ ا هـ . وليس المراد مطلق الفضل بالإجماع فإن فتح الأسواق في سائر بلاد المسلمين للاستفضال والاسترباح وإنما المراد فضل خصوص. فلذلك عرفه شرعاً بقوله : (فضل مال بلا عوض في معاوضة مال بمال) أي فضل أحد المتجانسين على الآخر بالعيار الشرعي أي الكيل والوزن ففضل قفيزي شعير على قفيزي بر لا يكون رباً، وكذا فضل عشرة أذرع من ثوب هروي على خمسة منه . وقيد بقوله «بلا عوض» أي خال عنه ليخرج بیع کر بر وکر شعیر بكري بر وكري شعير فإن للثاني فضلاً على الأول لكنه غير خال عن العوض لصرف الجنس إلى خلاف جنسه. وقيد بالمعاوضة لأن الفضل الخالي عن العوض الذي في الهبة ليس بربا. وترك المصنف قيداً لا بد منه أن يكون الفضل
الخالي مشروطاً في العقد لأحد المتعاقدين. وقد قيده به في الوقاية وقال شارحها : إنما قيد به لأنه لو شرط لغيرهما لا يكون ربا. وفي البناية قال علماؤنا : هو بيع فيه فضل مستحق لأحد المتعاقدين خال عما يقابله من عوض شرط في هذا العقد، وعلى هذا سائر أنواع البيوع الفاسدة من قبيل الربا. وفي الذخيرة من كتاب المداينات من الفصل الثاني عشر في المتفرقات قال محمد: إذا اشترى الرجل من آخر عشرة دراهم فضة بعشرة دراهم فزاد عليها دانقاً فوهبه دانقاً ولم يدخله في البيع إن لم يكن مشروطاً في الشراء لا يفسد الشراء لأنه إذا وهب الدائق منه انعدم الربا قالوا إنما تصح هبة الدائق إذا كانت الدراهم بحيث يضرها الكسر لأنها حينئذ هبة مشاع فيما لا يحتمل القسمة .اهـ. وفي جمع العلوم الربا شرعاً عبارة عن عقد فاسد وإن لم يكن فيه زيادة لأن بيع الدرهم بالدرهم نسيئة ربا وإن لم يتحقق فيه زيادة ا هـ . ولا يرد على المصنف ما في جمع العلوم من ربا النسيئة لأن فيه فضلاً حكمياً والفضل في عبارته أعم منه ومن الحقيقي، وظاهر ما في جمع العلوم وغيره أن المشتري يملك الدرهم
Chapter of Riba. The reason for its placement after Murabaha is that in each there is an increase, except that one is lawful and this is unlawful, and permissibility is the original rule in things, so what pertains to that increase was placed before what pertains to this. Riba (with kasr of ra) and fath is a mistake. In al-Misbah: riba means excess and increase, and it is maqsur (defective) according to the more famous view. Its dual is ribawān with waw on the original, and it is sometimes said ribiyān with lightening, and it is attributed to it on its word so it is said ribawī. Abu Ubayd and others said it. Al-Mutarrizī added: fath in the attribution is a mistake. By consensus, absolute excess is not intended, for opening markets in all Muslim lands for seeking profit and gain is allowed. Rather, a specific excess is intended. Therefore, he defined it legally as: (Excess of property without compensation in an exchange of property for property), i.e., the excess of one of two homogeneous [items] over the other according to the legal standard, i.e., capacity and weight. So the excess of two qafizes of barley over two qafizes of wheat is not riba. Similarly, the excess of ten cubits of a Herawi cloth over five of it. He restricted with his statement 'without compensation,' i.e., free from it, to exclude the sale of a kurr of wheat and a kurr of barley for a kurr of wheat and a kurr of barley, for the second has an excess over the first but it is not free from compensation due to diverting the genus to a different genus. He restricted with 'exchange' because the excess free from compensation in a gift is not riba. The author omitted a necessary restriction: that the excess must be stipulated in the contract for one of the two contracting parties. Al-Wiqāyah restricted with it, and its commentator said: it was restricted with it because if it were stipulated for someone else, it would not be riba. In al-Bināyah, our scholars said: It is a sale in which there is an excess due to one of the two contracting parties, free of what corresponds to it from compensation stipulated in this contract. And upon this, all types of corrupt sales are from the category of riba. In al-Dhakhīrah, from the book of loans, from the twelfth chapter on miscellaneous matters, Muhammad said: If a man buys from another ten dirhams of silver with ten dirhams, and adds a dāniq, and gifts the dāniq to him and does not include it in the sale – if it was not stipulated in the purchase, the purchase is not corrupted, because when he gifts the dāniq, riba ceases. They said: The gift of the dāniq is only valid if the dirhams are such that breaking them harms them, because then it is a gift of undivided property that does not admit division. In Jam' al-‘Ulūm, riba legally is an expression for an corrupt contract, even if there is no increase, because selling a dirham for a dirham on credit is riba even if no increase is realized. There is no objection to the author from what is in Jam' al-‘Ulūm regarding ribā al-nasī’ah, because in it there is a virtual excess, and excess in his expression is more general than it and the actual excess. What is apparent from Jam' al-‘Ulūm and others is that the buyer owns the dirham.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is a detailed definition and explanation of riba (usury/interest) in Hanafi fiqh. It begins by discussing the linguistic meaning of riba (increase) and then moves to the technical definition: 'An excess of property without compensation in an exchange of property for property.' The author, al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah, explains that the excess must be between two homogeneous (mutajānisayn) items, meaning they are of the same genus (jins) and measured by the shar‘ī standard (capacity or weight). For example, an extra handful of barley over wheat is not riba because they are different genera. Similarly, an extra cubit in cloth is not riba because cloth is not measured by weight or volume. The condition 'without compensation' excludes cases where the excess is offset by something else, like exchanging a kurr of wheat and barley for a kurr of wheat and barley, where the extra barley is compensated by the wheat. The condition 'in an exchange' excludes gifts, where excess is allowed. However, the author notes that the original text omitted an essential condition: the excess must be stipulated in the contract for one of the contracting parties. If it is stipulated for a third party or not stipulated at all, it is not riba. This is supported by the ruling from al-Wiqayah and al-Binayah. The passage then addresses a potential objection: the definition seems to exclude riba al-nasī’ah (credit riba), where there is no excess of quantity but a deferment. The response is that riba al-nasī’ah involves a virtual excess (faḍl ḥukmī) because the deferred payment compensates for the immediate payment in a way that is considered an excess in legal effect. Thus the definition covers both actual and virtual excess.

Key Terms
الربا (al-ribā): Legal term for an excess without compensation in a contractual exchange of homogeneous goods measured by weight or volume.
فضل مال بلا عوض (faḍl māl bilā 'iwaḍ): Excess of property (in quantity or quality) that is not counterbalanced by any corresponding consideration in the contract.
العيار الشرعي (al-'iyār al-shar'ī): The legal standard of measurement: weight (wazn) for things like silver, gold, wheat, barley; and volume (kayl) for things like dates, salt.
المتجانسين (al-mutajānisayn): Two items of the same genus (jins), e.g., two types of wheat, two types of silver.
معاوضة (mu'āwaḍah): A bilateral exchange where each party gives and receives something; excludes gifts and other gratuitous transfers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for riba al-fadl according to the Hanafi definition in this passage?
A) The excess must be without compensation.
B) The transaction must be an exchange.
C) The items must be homogeneous and measured by weight or volume.
D) The excess must be in the form of money.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of riba requires six conditions: homogeneity, measurement by weight/volume, excess, no compensation, exchange, and stipulation; all must be present for the transaction to be ribawi.

The Condition of Stipulation and the Scope of Riba al-Nasi'ah
Expands on the stipulation condition and defines riba al-nasi'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the condition of stipulation to determine if an excess is ribawi and distinguish riba al-fadl from riba al-nasi'ah.

Core Idea
If the excess is not stipulated in the contract, it is not riba; credit riba involves a virtual excess.

This passage from Al-Hidayah further clarifies the definition of riba by addressing two important points. First, it presents a case from Imam Muhammad showing that an excess given voluntarily after the contract does not constitute riba if it was not stipulated. Second, it discusses riba al-nasi'ah (credit riba), where the excess is not physical but temporal, and explains how the definition covers it through the concept of virtual excess. Understanding these nuances prevents common misconceptions.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the example from al-Dhakhirah
Read the scenario: buying 10 dirhams of silver with 10 dirhams and an extra dāniq, which is then gifted. Determine why the purchase is not corrupted.
Focus on the condition that the extra must be stipulated.
2
Identify the requirement for the gift to be valid
Note that the gift of the dāniq is only valid if the dirhams are such that breaking them harms them, indicating it must be a gift of an undivided share.
This is a technical detail about the gift being in the form of undivided property.
3
Understand riba al-nasi'ah
Read the quote from Jam' al-‘Ulūm that defines riba as a corrupt contract even without increase, because deferment itself is considered a virtual excess.
Virtual excess means the deferred payment has a time value.
4
Reconcile the definition with riba al-nasi'ah
Understand why the author's phrase 'excess without compensation' includes virtual excess, so there is no objection to the definition.
The author's 'excess' is general (ʿāmm), covering both actual and virtual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الربا
وجه مناسبته للمرابحة أن في كل منهما زيادة إلا أن تلك حلال وهذه حرام والحل هو الأصل في الأشياء فقدم ما يتعلق بتلك الزيادة على ما يتعلق بهذه والربا بكسر الراء وفتحها خطأ. وفي المصباح : الربا بالفضل والزيادة وهو مقصور على الأشهر، ويثني ربوان بالواو على الأصل وقد يقال ربيان على التخفيف وينسب إليه على لفظه فيقال ربوي؛ قاله أبو عبيد وغيره. وزاد المطرزي فقال : الفتح في النسبة خطأ ا هـ . وليس المراد مطلق الفضل بالإجماع فإن فتح الأسواق في سائر بلاد المسلمين للاستفضال والاسترباح وإنما المراد فضل خصوص. فلذلك عرفه شرعاً بقوله : (فضل مال بلا عوض في معاوضة مال بمال) أي فضل أحد المتجانسين على الآخر بالعيار الشرعي أي الكيل والوزن ففضل قفيزي شعير على قفيزي بر لا يكون رباً، وكذا فضل عشرة أذرع من ثوب هروي على خمسة منه . وقيد بقوله «بلا عوض» أي خال عنه ليخرج بیع کر بر وکر شعیر بكري بر وكري شعير فإن للثاني فضلاً على الأول لكنه غير خال عن العوض لصرف الجنس إلى خلاف جنسه. وقيد بالمعاوضة لأن الفضل الخالي عن العوض الذي في الهبة ليس بربا. وترك المصنف قيداً لا بد منه أن يكون الفضل
الخالي مشروطاً في العقد لأحد المتعاقدين. وقد قيده به في الوقاية وقال شارحها : إنما قيد به لأنه لو شرط لغيرهما لا يكون ربا. وفي البناية قال علماؤنا : هو بيع فيه فضل مستحق لأحد المتعاقدين خال عما يقابله من عوض شرط في هذا العقد، وعلى هذا سائر أنواع البيوع الفاسدة من قبيل الربا. وفي الذخيرة من كتاب المداينات من الفصل الثاني عشر في المتفرقات قال محمد: إذا اشترى الرجل من آخر عشرة دراهم فضة بعشرة دراهم فزاد عليها دانقاً فوهبه دانقاً ولم يدخله في البيع إن لم يكن مشروطاً في الشراء لا يفسد الشراء لأنه إذا وهب الدائق منه انعدم الربا قالوا إنما تصح هبة الدائق إذا كانت الدراهم بحيث يضرها الكسر لأنها حينئذ هبة مشاع فيما لا يحتمل القسمة .اهـ. وفي جمع العلوم الربا شرعاً عبارة عن عقد فاسد وإن لم يكن فيه زيادة لأن بيع الدرهم بالدرهم نسيئة ربا وإن لم يتحقق فيه زيادة ا هـ . ولا يرد على المصنف ما في جمع العلوم من ربا النسيئة لأن فيه فضلاً حكمياً والفضل في عبارته أعم منه ومن الحقيقي، وظاهر ما في جمع العلوم وغيره أن المشتري يملك الدرهم
Chapter of Riba. The reason for its placement after Murabaha is that in each there is an increase, except that one is lawful and this is unlawful, and permissibility is the original rule in things, so what pertains to that increase was placed before what pertains to this. Riba (with kasr of ra) and fath is a mistake. In al-Misbah: riba means excess and increase, and it is maqsur (defective) according to the more famous view. Its dual is ribawān with waw on the original, and it is sometimes said ribiyān with lightening, and it is attributed to it on its word so it is said ribawī. Abu Ubayd and others said it. Al-Mutarrizī added: fath in the attribution is a mistake. By consensus, absolute excess is not intended, for opening markets in all Muslim lands for seeking profit and gain is allowed. Rather, a specific excess is intended. Therefore, he defined it legally as: (Excess of property without compensation in an exchange of property for property), i.e., the excess of one of two homogeneous [items] over the other according to the legal standard, i.e., capacity and weight. So the excess of two qafizes of barley over two qafizes of wheat is not riba. Similarly, the excess of ten cubits of a Herawi cloth over five of it. He restricted with his statement 'without compensation,' i.e., free from it, to exclude the sale of a kurr of wheat and a kurr of barley for a kurr of wheat and a kurr of barley, for the second has an excess over the first but it is not free from compensation due to diverting the genus to a different genus. He restricted with 'exchange' because the excess free from compensation in a gift is not riba. The author omitted a necessary restriction: that the excess must be stipulated in the contract for one of the two contracting parties. Al-Wiqāyah restricted with it, and its commentator said: it was restricted with it because if it were stipulated for someone else, it would not be riba. In al-Bināyah, our scholars said: It is a sale in which there is an excess due to one of the two contracting parties, free of what corresponds to it from compensation stipulated in this contract. And upon this, all types of corrupt sales are from the category of riba. In al-Dhakhīrah, from the book of loans, from the twelfth chapter on miscellaneous matters, Muhammad said: If a man buys from another ten dirhams of silver with ten dirhams, and adds a dāniq, and gifts the dāniq to him and does not include it in the sale – if it was not stipulated in the purchase, the purchase is not corrupted, because when he gifts the dāniq, riba ceases. They said: The gift of the dāniq is only valid if the dirhams are such that breaking them harms them, because then it is a gift of undivided property that does not admit division. In Jam' al-‘Ulūm, riba legally is an expression for an corrupt contract, even if there is no increase, because selling a dirham for a dirham on credit is riba even if no increase is realized. There is no objection to the author from what is in Jam' al-‘Ulūm regarding ribā al-nasī’ah, because in it there is a virtual excess, and excess in his expression is more general than it and the actual excess. What is apparent from Jam' al-‘Ulūm and others is that the buyer owns the dirham.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is a detailed definition and explanation of riba (usury/interest) in Hanafi fiqh. It begins by discussing the linguistic meaning of riba (increase) and then moves to the technical definition: 'An excess of property without compensation in an exchange of property for property.' The author, al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah, explains that the excess must be between two homogeneous (mutajānisayn) items, meaning they are of the same genus (jins) and measured by the shar‘ī standard (capacity or weight). For example, an extra handful of barley over wheat is not riba because they are different genera. Similarly, an extra cubit in cloth is not riba because cloth is not measured by weight or volume. The condition 'without compensation' excludes cases where the excess is offset by something else, like exchanging a kurr of wheat and barley for a kurr of wheat and barley, where the extra barley is compensated by the wheat. The condition 'in an exchange' excludes gifts, where excess is allowed. However, the author notes that the original text omitted an essential condition: the excess must be stipulated in the contract for one of the contracting parties. If it is stipulated for a third party or not stipulated at all, it is not riba. This is supported by the ruling from al-Wiqayah and al-Binayah. The passage then addresses a potential objection: the definition seems to exclude riba al-nasī’ah (credit riba), where there is no excess of quantity but a deferment. The response is that riba al-nasī’ah involves a virtual excess (faḍl ḥukmī) because the deferred payment compensates for the immediate payment in a way that is considered an excess in legal effect. Thus the definition covers both actual and virtual excess.

Key Terms
ربا النسيئة (ribā al-nasī'ah): Credit riba: a prohibited increase arising from deferment of delivery in an exchange of homogeneous ribawi items.
فضل حكمي (faḍl ḥukmī): A juristic (virtual) excess that is not physical but recognized by law, e.g., the time value in credit transactions.
هبة مشاع (hibah mushā'): A gift of an undivided share in property that does not admit division.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author of al-Hidayah say that his definition of riba as 'excess without compensation' is not contradicted by riba al-nasi'ah?
A) Because riba al-nasi'ah involves a physical excess as well.
B) Because the definition includes virtual excess.
C) Because riba al-nasi'ah is not considered riba in the Hanafi school.
D) Because the definition was only meant for riba al-fadl.

Key Takeaway
Riba al-nasi'ah is prohibited because deferment in ribawi items creates a virtual excess; the stipulation condition confirms that only contractual excess invalidates the sale.

Hanafi Definition of Riba and Its Three Conditions
Commentary on the definition of riba with conditions and rebuttal of objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of riba and identify the three conditions (excess, stipulation, lack of countervalue) that must all be present for a transaction to be riba.

Core Idea
Riba is a stipulated excess in the contract for one party without any countervalue—missing any condition negates riba.

This lesson unpacks the core definition of riba from the Hanafi school. We will break down each element and see why the contract must contain a stipulated excess for one party, and why that excess must be devoid of any compensating countervalue. Without these conditions, the transaction may be valid or merely corrupt—but not riba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a transaction (sale or exchange). The ruling is haram. We need to define what specifically makes it haram (riba).
Haram is the strong prohibition; if the conditions are met, the transaction is invalid and sinful.
2
Break down the definition
From al-Wiqayah: 'an excess stipulated in the contract for one of the two contracting parties'. This contains three key elements: excess (fadl), stipulation (mashrūtan fī al-ʿaqd), and for one party (li-aḥad al-mutaʿāqidayn). The commentator adds 'devoid of countervalue' from al-Binayah.
Each element is necessary; omitting any one removes the case from riba.
3
Understand each condition
Excess: any additional benefit (value, quantity, or right). Stipulated: the excess must be explicitly mentioned in the contract terms. For one party: the benefit must be for buyer or seller, not a third party. No countervalue: the excess is not balanced by any return (ʿiwaḍ).
If the excess is not stipulated, it might be a gift after the contract, which does not affect the original sale.
4
Examine the case from Imam Muhammad
Muhammad al-Shaybani gives an example: buying ten dirhams with ten dirhams plus a daniq gifted afterward. If the gift is not stipulated, the sale is valid because the gift is separate. This shows that stipulation is essential for riba.
The gift is only valid if the dirhams are indivisible; otherwise it is invalid and the sale becomes riba.
5
Distinguish riba from corrupt sales
The text argues that not all corrupt sales are riba. Only those with a condition providing extra benefit (without countervalue) are riba. Sales corrupt due to ignorance or harm are not riba.
This will be explored in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب الربا
الخالي مشروطاً في العقد لأحد المتعاقدين. وقد قيده به في الوقاية وقال شارحها : إنما قيد به لأنه لو شرط لغيرهما لا يكون ربا. وفي البناية قال علماؤنا : هو بيع فيه فضل مستحق لأحد المتعاقدين خال عما يقابله من عوض شرط في هذا العقد، وعلى هذا سائر أنواع البيوع الفاسدة من قبيل الربا. وفي الذخيرة من كتاب المداينات من الفصل الثاني عشر في المتفرقات قال محمد: إذا اشترى الرجل من آخر عشرة دراهم فضة بعشرة دراهم فزاد عليها دانقاً فوهبه دانقاً ولم يدخله في البيع إن لم يكن مشروطاً في الشراء لا يفسد الشراء لأنه إذا وهب الدائق منه انعدم الربا قالوا إنما تصح هبة الدائق إذا كانت الدراهم بحيث يضرها الكسر لأنها حينئذ من ربا النسيئة لأن فيه فضلاً حكمياً والفضل في عبارته أعم منه ومن الحقيقي، وظاهر ما في جمع العلوم وغيره أن المشتري يملك الدرهم (الخ) عبارة ابن الكمال خال عن عوض شرط في أحد البدلين قال في شرحه : فلو وجد الفضل في أحد البدلين ولم يكن مشروطاً في العقد أو كان مشروطاً فيه ولم يكن في أحد البدلين بأن يكون لغير البائع والمشتري لا يكون ربا. وإنما قال في أحد البدلين ولم يقل لأحد العاقدين لأن العاقد قد يكون وكيلاً وقد يكون فضولياً والمعتبر كون الفضل للبائع أو للمشتري اهـ . تأمل. قوله : (وعلى هذا سائر أنواع البيوع الفاسدة من قبيل الربا هذا التعميم غير ظاهر لأن من البيوع الفاسدة ما سكت فيه عن الثمن وبيع عرض بخمر أو بأم ولد فتجب القيمة ويملك بالقبض وكذا بيع جذع في سقف وذراع من ثوب يضره التبعيض وبيع ثوب من ثوبين والبيع إلى النيروز ونحو ذلك مما . سبب الفساد فيه الجهالة أو الضرر أو نحو ذلك . نعم يظهر ذلك في البيع الفاسد بسبب شرط فيه نفع لأحد العاقدين مما لا يقتضيه العقد ولا يلائمه، ويؤيد ذلك ما ذكره الزيلعي قبيل باب الصرف في بحث ما يبطل بالشرط الفاسد حيث قال : والأصل فيه أن كل ما كان مبادلة مال بمال يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة لا ما كان مبادلة مال بغير مال أو كان من التبرعات لأن الشروط الفاسدة من باب الربا وهو يختص بالمعاوضة المالية دون غيرها من المعاوضات والتبرعات لأن الربا هو الفضل الخالي عن العوض، وحقيقة الشروط الفاسدة هي زيادة ما لا يقتضيه العقد ولا يلائمه فيكون فيه فضل خال عن العوض وهو الربا بعينه .اهـ. ملخصاً قوله : (ولا يرد على المصنف ما في جمع العلوم الخ) ههنا . كلام وهو التعريف لا يصدق على ربا النسيئة. أما أولاً فلأن في صورة زيادة أحد البدلين الغير الحاضر على الآخر الحاضر فضل لكن غير خال عن العوض لأن نقدية الحاضر عوض لفضل غير الحاضر إلا أن يقال : إن الشرع لم يعتبرها عوضاً والمراد العوض الشرعي وأما ثانياً فلأن ربا النسيئة قد يتحقق مع التساوي بالمعيار الشرعي على ما سيجيء آنفاً إلا أن يقال : إن المقصود تعريف الربا الحقيقي المتبادر عند الإطلاق وإنما هو ربا الفضل فلا بأس بخروج ما ذكر عن التعريف كما لا يخفى فتدبر يعقوبية . الزائد إذا قبضه فيما إذا اشترى درهمين بدرهم فإنهم جعلوه من قبيل الفاسد، وهكذا صرح به الأصوليون في بحث النهي فقالوا : إن الربا وسائر البيوع الفاسدة من قبيل ما كان مشروعاً بأصله دون وصفه .
Book of Sales, Chapter on Riba. [Riba is] an excess stipulated in the contract for one of the two contracting parties. Al-Wiqayah restricted it with this, and its commentator said: He restricted it because if it were stipulated for someone else, it would not be riba. In al-Binayah, our scholars said: It is a sale in which there is an excess due to one of the contracting parties, devoid of any countervalue stipulated in this contract, and on this basis all types of corrupt sales are included in riba. In al-Dhakhirah from the book of Mudayanat, twelfth chapter on miscellaneous matters, Muhammad said: If a man buys ten silver dirhams with ten dirhams and adds a daniq, then gives the daniq as a gift without including it in the sale, and it is not stipulated, the purchase is not invalid because when he gives the daniq, riba ceases. They said: The gift of the daniq is only valid if the dirhams are such that breaking them harms them, because then it is a gift of joint ownership in something that does not admit division. In Jam' al-'Ulum: Riba in sacred law is an invalid contract even if there is no increase, because selling a dirham for a dirham on credit is riba even if no increase is realized. This does not refute the author's [definition] regarding riba al-nasi'ah because there is a juristic excess, and excess in his phrase includes both actual and juristic. Apparently from Jam' al-'Ulum and others, the buyer owns the excess upon receipt. The phrase of Ibn al-Kamal: Devoid of a countervalue stipulated in one of the two substitutes. His commentator said: If the excess exists in one of the two substitutes but was not stipulated in the contract, or was stipulated but does not occur in one of the substitutes (e.g., it is for someone other than the seller and buyer), it is not riba. He said 'in one of the two substitutes' and not 'for one of the two contracting parties' because the person contracting may be an agent or an unauthorized person, and the consideration is that the excess belongs to the seller or buyer. Ponder. His statement: 'On this basis all types of corrupt sales are from riba' – this generalization is not apparent because among corrupt sales are those where the price was left unspecified, a sale of a commodity for wine or for an umm walad, where the price is owed and ownership occurs by possession, and also a sale of a rafter in a ceiling, a cubit from a cloth that is harmed by division, a sale of one cloth from two cloths, a sale until Nawruz, and similar where the cause of corruption is ignorance or harm. Yes, this applies in a corrupt sale due to a condition involving benefit for one of the parties that the contract does not necessitate nor is compatible with. This is supported by what al-Zayla'i mentioned before the chapter on Sarf in the discussion on what is invalidated by a corrupt condition, where he said: The origin in this is that every exchange of property for property is invalidated by corrupt conditions, while exchange of property for non-property or donations is not, because corrupt conditions are from the chapter of riba, which is specific to financial compensation to the exclusion of other transactions and donations, because riba is the excess devoid of countervalue, and the reality of corrupt conditions is an addition that does not necessitate nor is compatible with the contract, thus containing an excess devoid of countervalue, which is exactly riba. In summary, his statement: 'What is in Jam' al-'Ulum of riba al-nasi'ah does not refute the author.' Here, the definition does not apply to riba al-nasi'ah. Firstly, because in the case of an increase of one of the two absent substitutes over the present one, there is an excess but it is not devoid of countervalue because the present cash is a countervalue for the excess of the absent item, unless it is said that sacred law does not consider it a countervalue and what is meant is sacred countervalue. Secondly, because riba al-nasi'ah may occur with equality in the sacred measure, as will be mentioned shortly, unless it is said that the intention is to define actual riba that comes to mind when the term is used, which is riba al-fadl, so the exclusion of the mentioned from the definition is not a problem. Ponder carefully, O Ya'qubi. The excess upon receipt in the case of buying two dirhams with one dirham – they considered it among the corrupt. Similarly, the usuliyyun explicitly stated in the discussion on prohibition that riba and all corrupt sales are of the type that are valid in their origin but not in their description.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage defines riba in the Hanafi school. The definition requires a stipulated excess in the contract for one party without corresponding countervalue. The commentator explains that if the excess is for someone else, it is not riba. He then discusses a case from Muhammad: buying ten silver dirhams with ten dirhams and giving an extra daniq as a gift—if the gift is not stipulated, the sale is valid. The gift must be permissible only if the dirhams are indivisible. Next, the passage addresses an objection: riba al-nasi'ah (credit riba) might not fit the definition, but the author responds that the definition covers both actual and juristic excess. The generalization that all corrupt sales are riba is critiqued: sales corrupt due to ignorance or harm are not riba; only those with a condition providing extra benefit are. This is supported by al-Zayla'i's principle about corrupt conditions. The passage concludes by stating that the purchaser owns the excess upon receipt, as in the case of buying two dirhams with one dirham, which is considered a corrupt sale.

Key Terms
الربا (al-ribā): An excess stipulated in the contract for one party without corresponding countervalue, including both riba al-faḍl and riba al-nasi'ah.
الفضل (al-faḍl): The excess in value or quantity received by one party over the other without countervalue.
العوض (al-ʿiwaḍ): The countervalue that balances the excess, preventing riba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition in this passage, what is required for a transaction to be considered riba?
A) Any excess in value between two exchanged items.
B) An excess stipulated in the contract for one party without corresponding countervalue.
C) Any sale that is corrupt due to ignorance.
D) Selling a dirham for a dirham on credit.

Key Takeaway
Riba in the Hanafi school is defined as a stipulated excess for one party without any countervalue—all three conditions must be present.

Are All Corrupt Sales Riba? The Hanafi Position
Critique of the generalization that all corrupt sales are riba.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between riba and corrupt sales due to ignorance/harm, and apply the rule that only sales with a condition of extra benefit (without countervalue) are considered riba.

Core Idea
Only corrupt sales with a stipulated benefit condition are riba; sales corrupt due to ignorance or harm are not riba.

The text reports a generalization in some Hanafi sources that 'all corrupt sales are from riba.' Our commentator challenges this, citing many examples where corruption stems from ignorance or harm, not an excess condition. We will explore this intra-madhhab dispute and understand the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the generalization and its source
In al-Wiqayah and al-Binayah, it is stated: 'On this basis all types of corrupt sales are included in riba.' This suggests a broad equation.
The 'basis' refers to the definition of riba as an excess with no countervalue.
2
Identify the commentator's critique
The commentator says this generalization is not apparent (ghayr ẓāhir) because many corrupt sales are due to ignorance or harm, not a condition of extra benefit.
Examples: unspecified price, selling wine, rafter in ceiling, etc.
3
Analyze the examples of non-riba corrupt sales
These sales are corrupt because of defect in the contract (e.g., ignorance of price, harm from lack of division), but they do not involve a stipulated extra benefit for one party. Therefore, they are not riba.
In such cases, the buyer owns upon receipt and pays market value; no excess is returned.
4
Apply al-Zayla'i's principle
Al-Zayla'i states that corrupt conditions invalidate only financial exchanges (property for property), not donations or exchanges of property for non-property. This confirms that riba is specific to financial compensation.
The corrupt condition is itself an excess without countervalue, i.e., riba.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that not all corrupt sales are riba. Only those with a condition providing an extra benefit devoid of countervalue are riba.
This is supported by later Hanafi authorities like Ibn Nujaym.

Source Text

من عوض شرط في هذا العقد، وعلى هذا سائر أنواع البيوع الفاسدة من قبيل الربا. وفي الذخيرة من كتاب المداينات من الفصل الثاني عشر في المتفرقات قال محمد: إذا اشترى الرجل من آخر عشرة دراهم فضة بعشرة دراهم فزاد عليها دانقاً فوهبه دانقاً ولم يدخله في البيع إن لم يكن مشروطاً في الشراء لا يفسد الشراء لأنه إذا وهب الدائق منه انعدم الربا قالوا إنما تصح هبة الدائق إذا كانت الدراهم بحيث يضرها الكسر لأنها حينئذ الفضل في أحد البدلين ولم يكن مشروطاً في العقد أو كان مشروطاً فيه ولم يكن في أحد البدلين بأن يكون لغير البائع والمشتري لا يكون ربا. وإنما قال في أحد البدلين ولم يقل لأحد العاقدين لأن العاقد قد يكون وكيلاً وقد يكون فضولياً والمعتبر كون الفضل للبائع أو للمشتري اهـ . تأمل. قوله : (وعلى هذا سائر أنواع البيوع الفاسدة من قبيل الربا هذا التعميم غير ظاهر لأن من البيوع الفاسدة ما سكت فيه عن الثمن وبيع عرض بخمر أو بأم ولد فتجب القيمة ويملك بالقبض وكذا بيع جذع في سقف وذراع من ثوب يضره التبعيض وبيع ثوب من ثوبين والبيع إلى النيروز ونحو ذلك مما . سبب الفساد فيه الجهالة أو الضرر أو نحو ذلك . نعم يظهر ذلك في البيع الفاسد بسبب شرط فيه نفع لأحد العاقدين مما لا يقتضيه العقد ولا يلائمه، ويؤيد ذلك ما ذكره الزيلعي قبيل باب الصرف في بحث ما يبطل بالشرط الفاسد حيث قال : والأصل فيه أن كل ما كان مبادلة مال بمال يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة لا ما كان مبادلة مال بغير مال أو كان من التبرعات لأن الشروط الفاسدة من باب الربا وهو يختص بالمعاوضة المالية دون غيرها من المعاوضات والتبرعات لأن الربا هو الفضل الخالي عن العوض، وحقيقة الشروط الفاسدة هي زيادة ما لا يقتضيه العقد ولا يلائمه فيكون فيه فضل خال عن العوض وهو الربا بعينه .اهـ. ملخصاً قوله : (ولا يرد على المصنف ما في جمع العلوم الخ) ههنا . كلام وهو التعريف لا يصدق على ربا النسيئة. أما أولاً فلأن في صورة زيادة أحد البدلين الغير الحاضر على الآخر الحاضر فضل لكن غير خال عن العوض لأن نقدية الحاضر عوض لفضل غير الحاضر إلا أن يقال : إن الشرع لم يعتبرها عوضاً والمراد العوض الشرعي وأما ثانياً فلأن ربا النسيئة قد يتحقق مع التساوي بالمعيار الشرعي على ما سيجيء آنفاً إلا أن يقال : إن المقصود تعريف الربا الحقيقي المتبادر عند الإطلاق وإنما هو ربا الفضل فلا بأس بخروج ما ذكر عن التعريف كما لا يخفى فتدبر يعقوبية . الزائد إذا قبضه فيما إذا اشترى درهمين بدرهم فإنهم جعلوه من قبيل الفاسد، وهكذا صرح به الأصوليون في بحث النهي فقالوا : إن الربا وسائر البيوع الفاسدة من قبيل ما كان مشروعاً بأصله دون وصفه .
Book of Sales, Chapter on Riba. [Riba is] an excess stipulated in the contract for one of the two contracting parties. Al-Wiqayah restricted it with this, and its commentator said: He restricted it because if it were stipulated for someone else, it would not be riba. In al-Binayah, our scholars said: It is a sale in which there is an excess due to one of the contracting parties, devoid of any countervalue stipulated in this contract, and on this basis all types of corrupt sales are included in riba. In al-Dhakhirah from the book of Mudayanat, twelfth chapter on miscellaneous matters, Muhammad said: If a man buys ten silver dirhams with ten dirhams and adds a daniq, then gives the daniq as a gift without including it in the sale, and it is not stipulated, the purchase is not invalid because when he gives the daniq, riba ceases. They said: The gift of the daniq is only valid if the dirhams are such that breaking them harms them, because then it is a gift of joint ownership in something that does not admit division. In Jam' al-'Ulum: Riba in sacred law is an invalid contract even if there is no increase, because selling a dirham for a dirham on credit is riba even if no increase is realized. This does not refute the author's [definition] regarding riba al-nasi'ah because there is a juristic excess, and excess in his phrase includes both actual and juristic. Apparently from Jam' al-'Ulum and others, the buyer owns the excess upon receipt. The phrase of Ibn al-Kamal: Devoid of a countervalue stipulated in one of the two substitutes. His commentator said: If the excess exists in one of the two substitutes but was not stipulated in the contract, or was stipulated but does not occur in one of the substitutes (e.g., it is for someone other than the seller and buyer), it is not riba. He said 'in one of the two substitutes' and not 'for one of the two contracting parties' because the person contracting may be an agent or an unauthorized person, and the consideration is that the excess belongs to the seller or buyer. Ponder. His statement: 'On this basis all types of corrupt sales are from riba' – this generalization is not apparent because among corrupt sales are those where the price was left unspecified, a sale of a commodity for wine or for an umm walad, where the price is owed and ownership occurs by possession, and also a sale of a rafter in a ceiling, a cubit from a cloth that is harmed by division, a sale of one cloth from two cloths, a sale until Nawruz, and similar where the cause of corruption is ignorance or harm. Yes, this applies in a corrupt sale due to a condition involving benefit for one of the parties that the contract does not necessitate nor is compatible with. This is supported by what al-Zayla'i mentioned before the chapter on Sarf in the discussion on what is invalidated by a corrupt condition, where he said: The origin in this is that every exchange of property for property is invalidated by corrupt conditions, while exchange of property for non-property or donations is not, because corrupt conditions are from the chapter of riba, which is specific to financial compensation to the exclusion of other transactions and donations, because riba is the excess devoid of countervalue, and the reality of corrupt conditions is an addition that does not necessitate nor is compatible with the contract, thus containing an excess devoid of countervalue, which is exactly riba. In summary, his statement: 'What is in Jam' al-'Ulum of riba al-nasi'ah does not refute the author.' Here, the definition does not apply to riba al-nasi'ah. Firstly, because in the case of an increase of one of the two absent substitutes over the present one, there is an excess but it is not devoid of countervalue because the present cash is a countervalue for the excess of the absent item, unless it is said that sacred law does not consider it a countervalue and what is meant is sacred countervalue. Secondly, because riba al-nasi'ah may occur with equality in the sacred measure, as will be mentioned shortly, unless it is said that the intention is to define actual riba that comes to mind when the term is used, which is riba al-fadl, so the exclusion of the mentioned from the definition is not a problem. Ponder carefully, O Ya'qubi. The excess upon receipt in the case of buying two dirhams with one dirham – they considered it among the corrupt. Similarly, the usuliyyun explicitly stated in the discussion on prohibition that riba and all corrupt sales are of the type that are valid in their origin but not in their description.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage defines riba in the Hanafi school. The definition requires a stipulated excess in the contract for one party without corresponding countervalue. The commentator explains that if the excess is for someone else, it is not riba. He then discusses a case from Muhammad: buying ten silver dirhams with ten dirhams and giving an extra daniq as a gift—if the gift is not stipulated, the sale is valid. The gift must be permissible only if the dirhams are indivisible. Next, the passage addresses an objection: riba al-nasi'ah (credit riba) might not fit the definition, but the author responds that the definition covers both actual and juristic excess. The generalization that all corrupt sales are riba is critiqued: sales corrupt due to ignorance or harm are not riba; only those with a condition providing extra benefit are. This is supported by al-Zayla'i's principle about corrupt conditions. The passage concludes by stating that the purchaser owns the excess upon receipt, as in the case of buying two dirhams with one dirham, which is considered a corrupt sale.

Key Terms
البيوع الفاسدة (al-buyūʿ al-fāsida): Corrupt sales – transactions that are invalid due to a defect in their conditions or subject matter.
الشرط الفاسد (al-sharṭ al-fāsid): A corrupt condition – a term in the contract that provides extra benefit to one party without being part of the exchange, invalidating the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in this lesson, which of the following is true?
A) All corrupt sales are considered riba.
B) Only corrupt sales due to a condition of extra benefit for one party (without countervalue) are riba.
C) Corrupt sales due to ignorance are also riba.
D) Only riba al-nasi'ah is considered riba.

Key Takeaway
Not all corrupt sales are riba; the key is whether the corruption stems from a stipulated excess without countervalue.

Ibra' from Riba After Consumption: Debts vs. Sacred Rights
Legal incident on ibra' after riba consumption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ibra' after consumption of a riba item and distinguish between the right of the servant and the right of the sacred law in corrupt sales.

Core Idea
After consumption of a riba item, the liability becomes a debt in the dhimma—a right of the servant that can be waived by ibra'.

This passage presents a real legal incident: a man bought gold at an unfair rate, later repented, and the seller granted ibra' after the gold was consumed. The initial fatwa allowed ibra', but Rukn al-Din objected, arguing it was a right of the sacred law. The author Ibn Nujaym resolves the dispute by distinguishing between two rights: the sacred right to annul the contract and the servant's right to the debt. After consumption, only the debt remains, and ibra' is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act is ibra' (waiver) after the subject matter of a riba transaction has been consumed. The ruling is that it is valid (mubah).
2
Locate the dalil
Al-Bazdawi's principle: in corrupt ribawi contracts, the consideration is owned upon receipt. Consumption creates a liability (damān) which is a debt in the dhimma.
This principle is key to the Hanafi position.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Since the excess is owned, consuming it incurs a liability that is a right of the servant, not the sacred law. The sacred right is to annul the contract, but after consumption annulment is impossible. Ibra' on the debt does not affect the sacred right.
The distinction between the two rights is crucial.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Rukn al-Din al-Ranjanwi argued ibra' does not work in riba because returning the excess is a right of the sacred law.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is validity of ibra' after consumption, as supported by al-Bazdawi, al-Hanati, and Ibn Nujaym.
The tarjih is based on the practical necessity and the distinction of rights.

Source Text

وفي كتاب المداينات من القنية قال أستاذنا وقعت واقعة في زماننا أن رجلاً كان يشتري الذهب الرديء زماناً الدينار بخمسة دوائق ثم تنبه فاستحل منهم فأبرؤوه عما بقي لهم عليه حال كون ذلك مستهلكاً فكتبت أنا وغيري أنه يبرأ . أو كتب ركن الدين الرانجاوي الإبراء لا يعمل في الربا لأن رده لحق الشرع وقال : أجاب به نجم الأئمة الحكيمي معللاً بهذا التعليل وقال : هكذا سمعته عن ظهير الدين المرغيناني قال رضي الله عنه : فقرب من ظني أن الجواب كذلك مع تردد فكنت أطلب الفتوى لأمحو جوابي عنه فعرضت هذه المسألة على علاء الدين الحناطي فأجاب أنه يبرأ إذا كان الإبراء بعد الهلاك وغضب من جواب غيره أنه لا يبرأ فازداد ظني بصحة جوابي ولم أمحه، ويدل على صحته ما ذكره البزدوي في غناء الفقهاء من جملة صور البيع الفاسد جملة العقود الربوية يملك العوض فيها بالقبض . قلت : فإذا كان فضل الربا مملوكاً للقابض بالقبض فإذا استهلكه على ملكه ضمن مثله، فلو لم يصح الابراء ورد مثله يكون ذلك رد ضمان ما استهلكه لا رد عين ما استهلك، ويرد ضمان ما استهلك لا يرتفع العقد السابق بل يتقرر مفيداً للملك في فضل الربا فلم يكن في رده فائدة
قوله: (ورد مثله) معطوف على قوله لو لم يصح الإبراء لا على الإبراء فهو فعل ماض ومثله مفعوله. قوله: (فيجب ذلك حقاً الله تعالى بنصب «يجب» بأن مضمرة بعد الفاء في جواب النفي وفي بعض النسخ ليجب باللام وفي بعضها فكيف يجب» . قوله : (وإنما الذي يجب حقاً للشرع الخ) قال بعض الفضلاء : قد علمت أن العقد المذكور تعلق بسببه حقان: حق العبد وهو رد عينه إن كان باقياً ورد ضمانه إن مستهلكاً، وحق الشرع وهو رد عينه بنقض العقد السابق المنهي عنه شرعاً، وإبراء العبد إنما يكون فيما يملكه وهو الدين الثابت في الذمة، ولا شك في براءته عنه لأن المالك قد أبرأه منه، وأما فيما لا يملكه وهو حق الشرع فلا عمل لإبرائه فيه لأنه ليس حقاً له وقد تعذر التصور بعد الهلاك، وكلام ركن الدين مفروض فيه ألا تراه علل بقوله «لأن رده لحق الشرع» وما ذكره البزدوي صريح في أن الثابت في الذمة وهو ضمانه قابل للإبراء فالواجب القطع بأن الضمان الثابت بالاستهلاك في الذمة يقع الإبراء عنه، وأما حق الشرع فلصاحبه لا دخل للعبد فيه فكيف يقول بإبرائه تأمل. وقد قدم قبل هذه الورقة بسبع ورقات الإبراء العام في ضمن عقد فاسد يمنع الدعوى؛ كذا في دعوى البزازية. وقد ذكرنا بعد هذا أن الإبراء عن الربا لا يصح فتسمع الدعوى به وتقبل البينة .اهـ. كلام شيخ شيخنا السيد الحموي في حاشية الأشباه. أقول: لا يخفى عليك أن الحادثة كانت في الإبراء بعد الاستهلاك وليس هذا إلا في حق العبد كما قرره، فحمل بعدم
And in Kitab al-Mudayanat from al-Qunyah: Our teacher said: An incident occurred in our time: a man used to buy inferior gold, each dinar for five daniqs, then he became conscious and sought a permissible way, so they granted him acquittal (ibra') from what remained owed, while the gold was already consumed. I and others wrote that he is acquitted. However, Rukn al-Din al-Ranjanwi wrote that ibra' does not work in riba because its return is a right of the sacred law. He said: Najm al-A'immah al-Hakimi answered with this reasoning, and said: Thus I heard from Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani, who said: It came close to my opinion that the answer is thus, with hesitation, and I was seeking a fatwa to erase my answer, but I presented this issue to 'Ala' al-Din al-Hanati, and he answered that the debtor is acquitted if the ibra' is after destruction, and he became angry at another answer that he is not acquitted. So my opinion increased in correctness, and I did not erase it. Supporting its correctness is what al-Bazdawi mentioned in Ghina' al-Fuqaha': Among the forms of corrupt sale, including all ribawi contracts, the consideration is owned upon receipt. I say: If the excess of riba is owned by the receiver upon receipt, and he consumes it while it is his property, then he is liable for its like. So if ibra' is invalid and he returns its like, that would be a return of the compensation for what he consumed, not a return of the very thing consumed. And returning the compensation for what he consumed does not nullify the previous contract; rather it is established as conferring ownership of the excess of riba, so there is no benefit in returning it. His statement: 'and returns its like' is coordinated with the statement 'if ibra' is not valid' not on ibra', so it is a past tense verb and 'mithluhu' is its object. His statement: 'then that is required as a right of Allah' – the word 'yajibu' is in the accusative with an implied 'an' after fa in response to the negative, and in some copies 'li-yajiba' with lam, and in some 'fa-kayfa yajibu'. His statement: 'Rather what is required as a right of the sacred law' – some virtuous one said: Know that the mentioned contract has two rights attached: the right of the servant, which is to return the very thing if it remains, or to return its compensation if consumed; and the right of the sacred law, which is to return the very thing by annulling the previous prohibited contract. The ibra' of the servant applies only to what he owns, which is the debt established in the dhimma, and there is no doubt that he is cleared from it because the owner has granted him acquittal. As for what he does not own, which is the right of the sacred law, his ibra' has no effect because it is not his right, and after destruction, returning the thing is impossible. The words of Rukn al-Din are based on that, for you see he reasoned with his saying 'because its return is a right of the sacred law'. What al-Bazdawi mentioned is explicit that what is established in the dhimma, which is its compensation, is subject to ibra'. Therefore it is necessary to be certain that the compensation established by consumption in the dhimma is subject to ibra'. As for the right of the sacred law, it is for its owner; the servant has no say in it, so how can one speak of his ibra'? Ponder. It was stated before this leaf by seven leaves that general ibra' within a corrupt contract prevents legal claims; thus in Da'awi al-Bazzaziyyah. We mentioned after this that ibra' from riba is not valid, so a legal claim with it is heard and evidence is accepted. This is the words of our teacher's teacher al-Sayyid al-Hamawi in his gloss on al-Ashbah. I say: It is not hidden from you that the incident was about ibra' after consumption, and this is only regarding the right of the servant, as he affirmed, so it is interpreted as [not applying to the right of the sacred law].
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage presents a waqi'ah (legal incident) from al-Qunyah. A man bought inferior gold for five daniqs per dinar, later repented, and the seller granted ibra' from the remaining debt after the gold was consumed. The initial fatwa by the author and others was that the purchaser is acquitted. However, Rukn al-Din argued ibra' is invalid because returning the excess is a right of the sacred law. The author then cites multiple later scholars who support the validity of ibra' after consumption, including al-Bazdawi's principle that in corrupt sales the consideration is owned upon receipt, meaning the excess becomes a debt in the dhimma. The author argues: since the excess is owned by the receiver, consumption creates a liability (damān) that is a right of the servant, not the sacred law. The right of the sacred law is to annul the original contract, but after consumption, annulment is impossible; the only remaining claim is the liability in the dhimma, which can be waived. The author concludes that ibra' is valid for the debt, but does not affect the sacred right. He reconciles a previous statement that ibra' from riba is not valid by explaining it referred to ibra' before consumption, or to the right of the sacred law.

Key Terms
الإبراء (al-ibrā'): A waiver or acquittal from a debt or liability in the dhimma.
الهلاك (al-halāk): Consumption or destruction of the subject matter, making return in kind impossible.
الضمان (al-ḍamān): Liability or compensation for the value of the consumed item, becoming a debt in the dhimma.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this incident, why is ibra' valid after the riba item has been consumed?
A) Because the sacred law permits waiving all rights in riba.
B) Because after consumption, the right of the sacred law ceases to exist.
C) Because the liability becomes a debt in the dhimma, which is a right of the servant and can be waived.
D) Because the original contract is considered void ab initio.

Key Takeaway
Ibra' from riba is valid after consumption because the liability becomes a debt in the dhimma, a right of the servant that can be waived.

Ibra' After Consumption of Riba Goods: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ibra' after riba consumption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi scholars differ on the validity of ibra' after ribawi goods are consumed, and state the stronger position with its supporting evidence.

Core Idea
Ibra' after consumption is valid for the creditor's right but not for Sharia's right.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a creditor can release a debtor from the obligation arising from a corrupt riba transaction after the goods have been consumed. The central issue is whether the right to reclaim the excess belongs to Sharia (which cannot be waived) or to the creditor (which can be waived). You will follow the reasoning of key Hanafi scholars to understand the basis for each view and the stronger position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and legal question
Consider a real incident: a man buys poor gold for a dinar on credit with an excess (riba). Later, the seller realizes the transaction is invalid and agrees to release the buyer from the remaining debt after the gold has been consumed. Is this ibra' valid?
The question hinges on whether the right to the excess belongs to Sharia or to the creditor.
2
State the ruling of the opposing scholars
Rukn al-Din al-Ranjawi and Najm al-A'imma al-Hakimi held that ibra' does not work because the return of the excess is a right of Sharia. The creditor cannot waive a Sharia right.
This view is based on the idea that riba is prohibited and the creditor has no authority to nullify the Sharia's command.
3
State the ruling of the supporting scholars
'Ala' al-Din al-Hannati and the author's teacher ruled that ibra' is valid after consumption. The author himself sides with this view, supported by al-Bazdawi's reasoning.
Key distinction: after consumption, the Sharia's right to annul the contract cannot be enforced; only the guarantee (damān) remains, which is a creditor's right.
4
Analyse the proof from al-Bazdawi
Al-Bazdawi states that in corrupt ribawi contracts, the consideration is owned by receipt. Thus, the excess is owned by the receiver. If he consumes it, he is liable for its equivalent. This liability is a debt (creditor's right) and can be discharged by ibra'.
The Sharia's right is limited to annulling the original contract if the excess still exists. Once consumed, that right is irrelevant.
5
Determine the practical difference and the mufta bihi
If ibra' is invalid, the debtor remains liable even after release. If valid, the debtor is discharged. The text leans toward validity after consumption, which is the stronger view.
This is the mufta bihi position: ibra' after consumption is effective.

البيع باب الربا
الزائد إذا قبضه فيما إذا اشترى در همين بدرهم فإنهم جعلوه من قبيل الفاسد، وهكذا صرح به الأصوليون في بحث النهي فقالوا : إن الربا وسائر البيوع الفاسدة من قبيل ما كان مشروعاً بأصله دون وصفه .
وفي كتاب المداينات من القنية قال أستاذنا وقعت واقعة في زماننا أن رجلاً كان يشتري الذهب الرديء زماناً الدينار بخمسة دوائق ثم تنبه فاستحل منهم فأبرؤوه عما بقي لهم عليه حال كون ذلك مستهلكاً فكتبت أنا وغيري أنه يبرأ . أو كتب ركن الدين الرانجاوي الإبراء لا يعمل في الربا لأن رده لحق الشرع وقال : أجاب به نجم الأئمة الحكيمي معللاً بهذا التعليل وقال : هكذا سمعته عن ظهير الدين المرغيناني قال رضي الله عنه : فقرب من ظني أن الجواب كذلك مع تردد فكنت أطلب الفتوى لأمحو جوابي عنه فعرضت هذه المسألة على علاء الدين الحناطي فأجاب أنه يبرأ إذا كان الإبراء بعد الهلاك وغضب من جواب غيره أنه لا يبرأ فازداد ظني بصحة جوابي ولم أمحه، ويدل على صحته ما ذكره البزدوي في غناء الفقهاء من جملة صور البيع الفاسد جملة العقود الربوية يملك العوض فيها بالقبض . قلت : فإذا كان فضل الربا مملوكاً للقابض بالقبض فإذا استهلكه على ملكه ضمن مثله، فلو لم يصح الابراء ورد مثله يكون ذلك رد ضمان ما استهلكه لا رد عين ما استهلك، ويرد ضمان ما استهلك لا يرتفع العقد السابق بل يتقرر مفيداً للملك في فضل الربا فلم يكن في رده فائدة
قوله: (ورد مثله) معطوف على قوله لو لم يصح الإبراء لا على الإبراء فهو فعل ماض ومثله مفعوله. قوله: (فيجب ذلك حقاً الله تعالى بنصب «يجب» بأن مضمرة بعد الفاء في جواب النفي وفي بعض النسخ ليجب باللام وفي بعضها فكيف يجب» . قوله : (وإنما الذي يجب حقاً للشرع الخ) قال بعض الفضلاء : قد علمت أن العقد المذكور تعلق بسببه حقان: حق العبد وهو رد عينه إن كان باقياً ورد ضمانه إن مستهلكاً، وحق الشرع وهو رد عينه بنقض العقد السابق المنهي عنه شرعاً، وإبراء العبد إنما يكون فيما يملكه وهو الدين الثابت في الذمة، ولا شك في براءته عنه لأن المالك قد أبرأه منه، وأما فيما لا يملكه وهو حق الشرع فلا عمل لإبرائه فيه لأنه ليس حقاً له وقد تعذر التصور بعد الهلاك، وكلام ركن الدين مفروض فيه ألا تراه علل بقوله «لأن رده لحق الشرع» وما ذكره البزدوي صريح في أن الثابت في الذمة وهو ضمانه قابل للإبراء فالواجب القطع بأن الضمان الثابت بالاستهلاك في الذمة يقع الإبراء عنه، وأما حق الشرع فلصاحبه لا دخل للعبد فيه فكيف يقول بإبرائه تأمل. وقد قدم قبل هذه الورقة بسبع ورقات الإبراء العام في ضمن عقد فاسد يمنع الدعوى؛ كذا في دعوى البزازية. وقد ذكرنا بعد هذا أن الإبراء عن الربا لا يصح فتسمع الدعوى به وتقبل البينة .اهـ. كلام شيخ شيخنا السيد الحموي في حاشية الأشباه. أقول: لا يخفى عليك أن الحادثة كانت في الإبراء بعد الاستهلاك وليس هذا إلا في حق العبد كما قرره، فحمل [بعدم؟] نقض عقد الربا فيجب ذلك حقاً الله تعالى، وإنما الذي يجب حقاً للشرع رد عين الربا إن كان قائماً لا رد ضمانه؛ انتهى ما في القنية.
Chapter on Sales: Section on Riba. The excess when it is received in the case of buying two dirhams for one dirham — they made it from the category of corrupt (fasid). Thus the usuliyyun explicitly stated in the discussion of prohibition, saying: Riba and all corrupt sales are from the category of what is legislated in its origin but not in its description. In the book of al-Madayinat from al-Qunyah, my teacher said: An incident occurred in our time that a man used to buy poor gold for a dinar for five daniqs over time, then he became aware and sought halal from them, so they released him from what remained for them while that was consumed. I and others wrote that he is released. Or Rukn al-Din al-Ranjawi wrote that ibra' does not work in riba because its return is due to the right of Sharia. He said: Najm al-A'imma al-Hakimi answered with this reasoning. He said: Thus I heard from Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani. He said: It became close to my opinion that the answer is so with hesitation, and I sought a fatwa to erase my answer about it. I presented this issue to 'Ala' al-Din al-Hannati, and he answered that he is released if the ibra' is after destruction, and he became angry at another answer that he is not released, so my opinion increased in the correctness of my answer, and I did not erase it. Evidence for its correctness is what al-Bazdawi mentioned in Ghina' al-Fuqaha': among the images of corrupt sale is the category of ribawi contracts: the consideration is owned by receipt. I said: if the excess of riba is owned by the receiver by receipt, then if he consumes it while it is his property, he is liable for its equivalent. If ibra' is not valid and its equivalent is returned, that would be returning a guarantee for what he consumed, not returning the actual thing consumed. Returning the guarantee for what was consumed does not annul the previous contract; rather it becomes established as beneficial for ownership of the excess of riba, so there is no benefit in its return. His statement: (and its equivalent is returned) is conjoined to his statement 'if ibra' is not valid', not to ibra', so it is a past tense verb and 'mithlahu' is its object. His statement: (so that is obligatory as a right of Allah) ... etc.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of ibra' (release) in a riba transaction after the ribawi goods have been consumed. The discussion arises from a real incident where a man bought gold on credit with a riba-like transaction and later the seller released him from the debt after the gold was consumed. The author presents multiple opinions: some early Hanafi scholars like Rukn al-Din al-Ranjawi held that ibra' does not work in riba because the return of the excess is a right of Sharia, not the creditor. However, others like 'Ala' al-Din al-Hannati and the author's teacher ruled that ibra' is valid if it occurs after the goods are destroyed (after consumption). The key rationale is that after consumption, only the guarantee (damān) of the equivalent remains in the debtor's liability, and this guarantee is a right of the slave (creditor), not of Sharia. The Sharia's right is to annul the original contract if the excess is still in existence, but once it is consumed, that right cannot be enforced. Therefore, ibra' by the creditor from his own right (the guarantee) is valid. The passage also cites al-Bazdawi's ruling that in corrupt ribawi contracts, the consideration is owned by receipt, so the excess becomes the receiver's property; thus after consumption, he is liable for its equivalent, and ibra' from that liability is effective. The final part from al-Qunyah summarizes that ibra' after consumption only applies to the slave's right, not the Sharia's right. The author notes that this is consistent with the general principle that ibra' from riba itself is not valid, but in this specific case it is.

Key Terms
إبراء (ibra'): Release from a debt; a creditor's waiver of the right to demand repayment.
ربا (riba): Usury or interest; any excess in exchange of ribawi goods of the same kind.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or liability to pay the equivalent of a consumed item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the discussion, when is ibra' from a riba debt considered valid?
A) Only before the ribawi goods are consumed
B) After the goods are consumed, because only the guarantee remains
C) Never, because riba is prohibited
D) Only if the creditor explicitly waives the Sharia's right

Key Takeaway
Ibra' after consumption of ribawi goods is valid because the remaining liability is a creditor's right, not a Sharia right.

The Prohibition of Riba: Proofs and Punishments
Exposition of textual evidence and punishments for riba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three primary sources for the prohibition of riba and identify the five punishments for its consumers according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Riba is prohibited by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma; its consumers face five dire punishments including war with Allah.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the conclusive evidence for the prohibition of riba. It establishes that riba is a major sin, supported by clear Quranic verses, abundant hadith, and the consensus of the Companions. The text also addresses the minority view of Ibn Abbas that riba is only in credit, providing a robust Hanafi response. Understanding these proofs is essential for every Muslim to avoid falling into this grave transgression.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage begins by stating that riba is haram (prohibited) by the Book, Sunnah, and Ijma. This is the foundational ruling. Note the absolute nature of the prohibition.
Riba includes both excess (fadl) and credit (nasi'ah).
2
Analyze the Quranic proofs and five punishments
The author cites specific verses and elaborates on five punishments from al-Mi'raj: confusion, destruction, war, disbelief, and eternal fire. Understand that these punishments are both in this world and the Hereafter.
Each punishment is supported by a Quranic verse and a hadith.
3
Examine the Sunnah evidence and the dispute
The Sunnah evidence is too numerous to count. The passage focuses on the dispute regarding riba al-fadl, where Ibn Abbas held a different view. Analyze the Hanafi response: majority Companions, restriction on measured/weighed items, retraction by Ibn Abbas, and later consensus.
Denial of riba al-nasi'ah is considered disbelief by consensus.
4
Derive the operative ruling for riba al-fadl
Despite the disagreement, the Hanafi school holds that riba al-fadl is haram. The passage provides the arguments that outweigh Ibn Abbas's opinion. The mufta bihi is the prohibition of both types.
The lesson emphasizes that consensus of the Followers overrides an individual Companion's view.

وهو محرم بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع. أما الكتاب فآيات منها وحرم الربا﴾ [البقرة : ۲۷۵] والمراد به فيها الفضل وهو الزيادة ليتعلق التحريم به لأن الأحكام لا تتعلق إلا بفعل المكلفين. ومنها لا تأكلوا الربا﴾ [آل عمران: ١٣٠] والمراد منه فيها نفس الزائد في بيع الأموال الربوية عند بيع بعضها بجنسه. وفي المعراج : ذكر الله لأكل الربا خمس عقوبات : أحدها التخبط قال تعالى لا يقومون إلا كما يقوم الذي يتخبطه الشيطان من المس [البقرة: ٢٧٥] قيل في معناه تنتفخ بطنه يوم القيامة فيصير لا تحمله قدماه فيصير كلما قام سقط بمنزلة من أصابه المس، ويؤيده الحديث يملأ بطنه ناراً بقدر ما أكل من الربا والمراد به الافتضاح على رؤوس الاشهاد كما في حديث آخر «ينصب لواء يوم القيامة لآكلي الربا فيجتمعون تحته ثم يساقون إلى النار والثاني المحق قال الله تعالى يمحق الله الربا﴾ [البقرة: ٢٧٦] والمراد الهلاك والاستئصال، وقيل ذهاب البركة والاستمتاع حتى لا ينتفع هو به ولا ولده من بعده والثالث الحرب قال الله تعالى فآذنوا بحرب من الله ورسوله ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۷۹] المعنى في القراءة بالمد اعلموا الناس يا أكلة الربا أنكم حرب الله ورسوله بمنزلة قطاع الطريق، وفي قراءة بغير المد أي اعلموا أن أكلة الربا حرب الله . الرابع الكفر قال الله تعالى وذروا ما بقي من الربا إن كنتم مؤمنين) [البقرة : ٢٧٨] وقال والله لا يحب كل كفار أثيم أي كفار باستحلال الربا والخامس الخلود في النار قال تعالى ومن عاد فأولئك أصحاب النار هم فيها خالدون ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٧٥] يؤيده قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «کل درهم واحد من الربا أشد من ثلاث وثلاثين زنية يزنيها الرجل ومن نبت لحمه من الحرام فالنار أولى به والمقصود من كتاب البيوع بيان الحلال الذي هو بيع شرعاً والحرام الذي هو ربا ولهذا قيل لمحمد : لا تصنف في الزهد شيئاً؟ قال : صنفت كتاب البيوع وليس الزهد إلا اجتناب الحرام والرغبة في الحلال؛ كذا في المبسوط وأما السنة فأكثر من أن تحصى قال الإمام الأسبيجابي : اتفقوا على أنه إذا أنكر ربا النساء يكفر وفي ربا الفضل في القدر اختلاف فإن ابن عباس رضي الله تعالى عنه لا يرى الربا إلا في النسيئة للحديث إنما الربا في النسيئة وكلمة «إنما للحصر إلا أن عامة الصحابة احتجوا بأحاديث. والجواب عن تعلق ابن عباس أنه منصرف إلى ما ليس بمكيل ولا موزون لقوله آخره إلا ما كيل أو وزن على أن ابن عباس رجع عن هذا القول، فإن لم يثبت رجوعه فاجماع التابعين به يرفعه اهـ. ما في المعراج.
And it is prohibited by the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus. As for the Book, among the verses: [Allah] 'has forbidden riba' (2:275) — the intended meaning here is the excess, which is the increase, so that the prohibition relates to it, because rulings only relate to the actions of the legally responsible. And among them: 'Do not consume riba' (3:130) — the intended meaning here is the very excess in selling ribawi properties when selling some of them for their own kind. In al-Mi'raj: Allah mentioned for the consumers of riba five punishments: first, confusion (al-takhabbuth) — He said: 'They will not stand except as stands one whom the devil has touched by insanity' (2:275). It is said in its meaning: his stomach will swell on the Day of Judgment so that his legs cannot carry him; whenever he stands he falls, like one touched by insanity. This is supported by the hadith: 'He will fill his belly with fire equivalent to what he consumed of riba' — the meaning is disgrace before witnesses, as in another hadith: 'A banner will be set up on the Day of Judgment for the consumers of riba; they will gather beneath it, then they will be driven to the Fire.' Second, destruction (al-mahq) — Allah said: 'Allah destroys riba' (2:276) — the meaning is perdition and eradication; it is also said it means loss of blessing and enjoyment so that neither he nor his children after him benefit from it. Third, war (al-harb) — Allah said: 'Then be informed of a war from Allah and His Messenger' (2:279) — the meaning in the reading with madd: inform the people, O eaters of riba, that you are at war with Allah and His Messenger like highway robbers. In a reading without madd: know that the eaters of riba are at war with Allah. Fourth, disbelief (al-kufr) — Allah said: 'And leave what remains of riba, if you are believers' (2:278). And He said: 'Allah does not love any ungrateful sinner' — i.e., disbelievers by making riba lawful. Fifth, eternal abode in the Fire (al-khulud fi al-nar) — He said: 'And whoever returns [to riba] — those are the companions of the Fire; they will abide therein eternally' (2:275). This is supported by his saying, peace be upon him: 'Every single dirham of riba is more severe than thirty-three acts of fornication committed by a man, and whoever's flesh is nourished by the unlawful, the Fire is more deserving of him.' The purpose of the Book of Sales is to clarify the lawful which is sale according to Sharia and the unlawful which is riba. For this, it was said to Muhammad: 'Why do you not write on asceticism?' He said: 'I wrote the Book of Sales; asceticism is nothing but avoiding the unlawful and desiring the lawful.' So it is in al-Mabsut. As for the Sunnah, it is too numerous to count. Imam al-Isbijabi said: They agreed that if one denies riba al-nasi'ah, he disbelieves. In riba al-fadl regarding quantity, there is a difference. Ibn Abbas did not consider riba except in credit (nasi'ah) due to the hadith: 'Riba is only in credit' — the word 'innama' is for restriction. However, the majority of Companions argued with hadith. The response to Ibn Abbas' argument is that it applies to what is not measured or weighed, because he said at the end: 'except what is measured or weighed.' Moreover, Ibn Abbas retracted this view; if his retraction is not confirmed, then the consensus of the Followers after him nullifies it. End of what is in al-Mi'raj.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage presents the proofs for the prohibition of riba from the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus, as a foundational lesson. The author states unequivocally that riba is haram by all three primary sources. From the Quran, he cites two key verses: 'And He has forbidden riba' (2:275) and 'Do not consume riba' (3:130). He explains that the prohibition attaches to the excess (al-fadl) because legal rulings only address actions of the mukallaf. Then, from al-Mi'raj, he enumerates five punishments for the consumer of riba: (1) confusion and resurrection like one possessed, (2) destruction of wealth, (3) being at war with Allah and His Messenger, (4) being categorized as a disbeliever (by making it lawful), and (5) eternal abode in the Fire. Each is supported by hadith. The author also relates that the purpose of writing the Book of Sales is to distinguish halal sales from riba, and that asceticism is essentially avoiding the haram and desiring the halal. Regarding the Sunnah, he notes that it is abundant, and then addresses a disagreement: some, like Ibn Abbas, held that riba is only in credit (nasi'ah) and not in excess (fadl). However, the majority of Companions, and later the consensus of the Followers, established that riba is also prohibited in excess when items are exchanged for the same kind. The response to Ibn Abbas is that his apparent restriction applies only to non-measured and non-weighed items, and that he later retracted. If retraction is not proven, the consensus of the Followers overrides his individual view. Thus, the consensus (ijma) is established.

Key Terms
ربا الفضل (riba al-fadl): Excess in quantity when exchanging same-type ribawi items, e.g., exchanging 1 dirham for 2 dirhams of same quality.
ربا النساء (riba al-nasi'ah): Riba due to delay in payment; interest on credit transactions when exchanging same-type items with deferment.
التخبط (al-takhabbuth): A state of confusion and insanity, used here to describe the resurrection of those who consumed riba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the punishment mentioned for the consumer of riba that is described as 'war from Allah and His Messenger'?
A) Confusion and insanity on the Day of Judgment
B) Destruction of wealth
C) Being at war with Allah and His Messenger
D) Eternal abode in the Fire

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of riba is definitively established by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma, and includes both credit-based and excess-based riba, with severe punishments in this world and the Hereafter.

The Prohibition of Riba and Refutation of Ibn Abbas
Establishes prohibition of riba via Quran, Sunnah, Ijma and refutes Ibn Abbas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on riba (both fadl and nasi'ah), cite the Quranic and Sunnah proofs, and explain why the view of Ibn Abbas is not accepted in the school.

Core Idea
Riba is forbidden in all forms — both excess in spot (fadl) and deferment (nasi'ah) — by Quran, Sunnah, and consensus.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq establishes the absolute prohibition of riba, citing multiple Quranic verses, the five punishments, and the consensus of the Companions. It also addresses and refutes the minority view of Ibn Abbas, who limited riba to credit transactions based on a hadith. By the end of this lesson, you will be able to articulate the complete Hanafi position and defend it against the opposing argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Sources
The text states that riba is haram by the Book, Sunnah, and Ijma. Note the two categories: riba al-fadl (excess in spot exchange) and riba al-nasi'ah (credit).
2
Analyze the Quranic Proofs
Examine the verses cited: 'Wa harrama al-riba' (2:275), 'La ta'kulu al-riba' (3:130), and the five punishments. Understand that the prohibition attaches to the act of taking excess (fadl).
The five punishments are confusion, destruction, war, disbelief, and eternity in Fire.
3
Understand the Refutation of Ibn Abbas
Ibn Abbas held that riba is only in nasi'ah based on 'innama al-riba fi al-nasi'ah'. The Hanafi response: either he meant non-measured items, or he retracted, and the consensus of the Tabi'in overrides.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf resolved by tarjih.
4
Determine the Operative Ruling (Mufta Bihi)
The Hanafi school follows the majority of Sahaba; both riba al-fadl and riba al-nasi'ah are haram. This is the mufta bihi.
