نقض عقد الربا فيجب ذلك حقاً الله تعالى، وإنما الذي يجب حقاً للشرع رد عين الربا إن كان قائماً لا رد ضمانه؛ انتهى ما في القنية. وهو محرم بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع. أما الكتاب فآيات منها ﴿وحرم الربا﴾ [البقرة: ٢٧٥] والمراد به فيها الفضل وهو الزيادة ليتعلق التحريم به لأن الأحكام لا تتعلق إلا بفعل المكلفين. ومنها ﴿لا تأكلوا الربا﴾ [آل عمران: ١٣٠] والمراد منه فيها نفس الزائد في بيع الأموال الربوية عند بيع بعضها بجنسه. وفي المعراج : ذكر الله لأكل الربا خمس عقوبات : أحدها التخبط قال تعالى ﴿لا يقومون إلا كما يقوم الذي يتخبطه الشيطان من المس﴾ [البقرة: ٢٧٥] قيل في معناه تنتفخ بطنه يوم القيامة فيصير لا تحمله قدماه فيصير كلما قام سقط بمنزلة من أصابه المس، ويؤيده الحديث يملأ بطنه ناراً بقدر ما أكل من الربا والمراد به الافتضاح على رؤوس الاشهاد كما في حديث آخر «ينصب لواء يوم القيامة لآكلي الربا فيجتمعون تحته ثم يساقون إلى النار والثاني المحق قال الله تعالى ﴿يمحق الله الربا﴾ [البقرة: ٢٧٦] والمراد الهلاك والاستئصال، وقيل ذهاب البركة والاستمتاع حتى لا ينتفع هو به ولا ولده من بعده والثالث الحرب قال الله تعالى ﴿فآذنوا بحرب من الله ورسوله﴾ [البقرة: ٢٧٩] المعنى في القراءة بالمد اعلموا الناس يا أكلة الربا أنكم حرب الله ورسوله بمنزلة قطاع الطريق، وفي قراءة بغير المد أي اعلموا أن أكلة الربا حرب الله . الرابع الكفر قال الله تعالى ﴿وذروا ما بقي من الربا إن كنتم مؤمنين﴾ [البقرة: ٢٧٨] وقال ﴿والله لا يحب كل كفار أثيم﴾ أي كفار باستحلال الربا والخامس الخلود في النار قال تعالى ﴿ومن عاد فأولئك أصحاب النار هم فيها خالدون﴾ [البقرة: ٢٧٥] يؤيده قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «کل درهم واحد من الربا أشد من ثلاث وثلاثين زنية يزنيها الرجل ومن نبت لحمه من الحرام فالنار أولى به والمقصود من كتاب البيوع بيان الحلال الذي هو بيع شرعاً والحرام الذي هو ربا ولهذا قيل لمحمد : لا تصنف في الزهد شيئاً؟ قال : صنفت كتاب البيوع وليس الزهد إلا اجتناب الحرام والرغبة في الحلال؛ كذا في المبسوط وأما السنة فأكثر من أن تحصى قال الإمام الأسبيجابي : اتفقوا على أنه إذا أنكر ربا النساء يكفر وفي ربا الفضل في القدر اختلاف فإن ابن عباس رضي الله تعالى عنه لا يرى الربا إلا في النسيئة للحديث إنما الربا في النسيئة وكلمة «إنما للحصر إلا أن عامة الصحابة احتجوا بأحاديث. والجواب عن تعلق ابن عباس أنه منصرف إلى ما ليس بمكيل ولا موزون لقوله آخره إلا ما كيل أو وزن على أن ابن عباس رجع عن هذا القول، فإن لم يثبت رجوعه فاجماع التابعين به يرفعه اهـ. ما في المعراج.
The nullification of the contract of riba is obligatory as a right of Allah Almighty. Rather, what is obligatory as a right of the Law is the return of the very riba if it still exists, not its guarantee; end of what is in al-Qunyah. And it is prohibited by the Book, Sunnah, and Ijma. As for the Book, among the verses are: 'And Allah has forbidden riba' (2:275) – what is intended by it is al-fadl meaning the increase, so that prohibition attaches to it because legal rulings only attach to the actions of the responsible person. And among them: 'Do not consume riba' (3:130) – what is intended by it is the increased amount itself in the sale of ribawi goods when selling some of them for the same genus. In al-Mi'raj: Allah mentioned for the consumer of riba five punishments: First: confusion – He said: 'They will not stand except as one whom Satan has touched by insanity' (2:275). It is said in its meaning that his belly will swell on the Day of Judgment so that his legs cannot carry him, so whenever he stands he falls, like one afflicted with insanity. This is supported by the hadith: 'He will fill his belly with fire to the extent of the riba he consumed.' What is meant is disgrace before the witnesses as in another hadith: 'A banner will be raised on the Day of Judgment for the consumers of riba, they will gather under it, then they will be driven to the Fire.' Second: destruction – Allah said: 'Allah destroys riba' (2:276) – meaning annihilation and eradication; it is said, loss of blessing and enjoyment so that neither he nor his children after him benefit from it. Third: war – Allah said: 'Then be informed of a war from Allah and His Messenger' (2:279); the meaning in the reading with madd is: 'Inform the people, O consumers of riba, that you are at war with Allah and His Messenger, like highway robbers.' In a reading without madd it means: 'Know that the consumers of riba are at war with Allah.' Fourth: disbelief – Allah said: 'And leave what remains of riba, if you are believers' (2:278); and He said: 'And Allah does not love any sinful disbeliever' – meaning a disbeliever through legalizing riba. Fifth: eternity in the Fire – Allah said: 'And whoever returns, those are the companions of the Fire, they will abide therein' (2:275). This is supported by his saying, peace be upon him: 'Every single dirham of riba is more severe than thirty-three acts of fornication that a man commits, and whoever's flesh grows from the unlawful, the Fire is more appropriate for him.' The purpose of the book of sales is to explain the lawful that is sale according to the Shariah and the unlawful that is riba. For this reason it was said to Muhammad: 'Do you not write something on asceticism?' He said: 'I have written the book of sales, and asceticism is nothing but avoiding the unlawful and desiring the lawful.' End quote from al-Mabsut. As for the Sunnah, it is too numerous to count. Imam al-Asbijabi said: They agreed that if someone denies riba al-nasi'ah he disbelieves, but regarding riba al-fadl in measure there is disagreement. Indeed, Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, does not consider riba except in nasi'ah due to the hadith: 'Riba is only in nasi'ah' and the word 'innama' indicates restriction. However, the generality of the Companions argued with hadiths. The answer to Ibn Abbas' argument is that his statement is directed to that which is not measured or weighed, because of his statement at the end: 'except what is measured or weighed.' Moreover, Ibn Abbas retracted this opinion; but if his retraction is not established, then the consensus of the Tabi'in overrides it. End quote from al-Mi'raj.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the prohibition of riba, establishing the position of the Hanafi school. The author begins by stating that nullifying a riba contract is a right of Allah, and the obligatory act is to return the actual riba if it still exists, not its guarantee. This sets the legal consequence of a riba transaction. Then he declares that riba is prohibited by the three primary sources: the Quran, the Sunnah, and scholarly consensus (ijma). For the Quran, he cites two key verses: 'And Allah has forbidden riba' (2:275) and 'Do not consume riba' (3:130), explaining that the prohibition attaches to the act of taking excess (fadl) in ribawi goods. He then elaborates on the five punishments Allah has mentioned for the consumer of riba, as detailed in al-Mi'raj: confusion at resurrection, destruction of wealth, being declared at war with Allah, being counted among disbelievers (by legalizing riba), and eternity in Hellfire. Each punishment is supported by Quranic verses and hadiths. The purpose of the book of sales is to distinguish lawful sale from unlawful riba, as Imam Muhammad said that asceticism is avoiding the unlawful. For the Sunnah proof, he cites Imam al-Asbijabi: there is consensus that denying riba al-nasi'ah is disbelief, but there was disagreement on riba al-fadl in measure. The minority view of Ibn Abbas, who held that riba is only in nasi'ah (credit) based on the hadith 'innama al-riba fi al-nasi'ah', is refuted: either he meant non-measured items, or he retracted, and if retraction is unproven, the consensus of the Tabi'in overrides his individual view. The Hanafi position follows the majority of the Sahaba.

Key Terms
ربا (ribā): An unlawful excess in exchange of certain goods (ribawi items) either in measure/weight (riba al-fadl) or in deferment (riba al-nasi'ah).
نسيئة (nasī'ah): Deferment of payment or delivery in exchange of ribawi items; riba al-nasi'ah is the prohibited excess due to time.
فضل (faḍl): The increase or excess in quantity when exchanging ribawi items of the same genus in a spot transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is true regarding the prohibition of riba?
A) Riba is only prohibited in credit transactions (nasi'ah).
B) Both riba al-fadl (excess in spot) and riba al-nasi'ah are prohibited.
C) Riba al-fadl is permissible if done hand-to-hand without deferment.
D) The prohibition of riba is only based on the Quran, not Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Riba is absolutely prohibited in all its forms, and the Hanafi school rejects any attempt to limit it to credit transactions alone.

Legal Stratagems (Hiyal) to Avoid Riba: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Presents hiyal to avoid riba with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the use of hiyal to avoid riba and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Hiyla to avoid riba: permissible according to the Sahibayn, makruh according to a weak riwaya from Imam Muhammad.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores a classic Hanafi debate: are legal stratagems (hiyal) that circumvent riba permissible? While normal transactions to avoid riba are accepted, Imam Muhammad is reported to have disliked them in some contexts. The text presents the dispute and the eventual tarjih, giving you a clear view of how later scholars settled the issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
Determine what the hival (legal stratagems) are meant to achieve—avoiding riba while reaching a financial goal. Note the initial ruling: 'la ba'sa' (no harm) reported from Abu Yusuf and al-Shaybani.
2
Spot the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Al-Baqqali transmitted a report from Imam Muhammad that such hiyal are makruh. Meanwhile, the 'two' (the Sahibayn) hold there is no harm. Recognize that both views exist within the school.
The 'two' here refers to Abu Yusuf and the standard view of al-Shaybani, as distinct from the weak riwaya.
3
Analyze the limitation by al-Zarruji
Al-Zarruji explains that Muhammad's karahah applies only when the stratagem is structured after a loan (i.e., a post-loan arrangement). If the sale happens first and then payment is made, there is no disagreement—all agree it is permissible.
This limitation narrows the scope of the dispute significantly.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Based on the tarjih of al-Zarruji and the general acceptance in works like al-Qunyah, the relied-upon position is permissibility (la ba'sa). The weak riwaya from Muhammad is not given operative weight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخلاصة : لو قضى بجواز بيع الدرهم بالدرهمين يداً بيد بأعيانهما أخذاً كلام ركن الدين على معنى أنه لا للإبراء يصح عن الربا نفسه وإن صح في ذاته لكنه لا يناسب الحادثة المسؤول عنها فلا ينبغي حمله على ذلك فتدبر . قوله : (لا رد ضمانه) يعني حقاً للشرع وأما من الصحابة وافقه بقول ابن عباس لا ينفذ وإن كان مختلفاً بين الصحابة لأنه لا أن أحداً . يعلم فكان مهجوراً اهـ وفي القنية من الكراهية : لا بأس بالبيوع التي يفعلها الناس للتحرز عن الربا. ثم رقم آخر هي مكروهة ذكر البقالي الكراهة عن محمد وعندهما لا بأس به. قال الزرنجري : خلاف محمد في العقد بعد القرض أما إذا باع ثم دفع الدراهم لا بأس بالاتفاق اهـ . وفي القنية من الكراهية: يجوز للمحتاج الاستقراض بالربح .اهـ. وفي الخلاصة معزياً إلى النوازل : رجل له على آخر عشرة دراهم فأراد أن يؤجلها إلى سنة ويأخذ منه ثلاثة عشر فالحيلة أن يشتري منه بتلك العشرة متاعاً ويقبض المتاع منه وقيمة المتاع عشرة ثم يبيع المتاع منه بثلاثة عشر إلى سنة اهـ .
And in al-Khulasa: If a judge rules for the permissibility of selling one dirham for two dirhams hand-to-hand with their exact identities, taking the speech of Rukn al-Din as meaning that it is not for absolution, it is valid concerning riba itself even if it is valid in itself, but it does not suit the incident inquired about, so it should not be interpreted that way, so reflect. His statement: '(not its guarantee)' means as a right of the Law. And as for some of the Companions agreeing with Ibn Abbas's statement, it is not enforceable even if it was disputed among the Companions, because no one knows it, so it is abandoned. End. And in al-Qunyah from the chapter of karahah: There is no harm in the transactions that people perform to guard against riba. Then another report: They are makruh. Al-Baqqali reported karahah from Muhammad, while according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?) there is no harm. Al-Zarruji said: The disagreement of Muhammad pertains to the contract after the loan; as for when he sells then pays the dirhams, there is no harm by agreement. End. And in al-Qunyah from the chapter of karahah: It is permissible for the needy to borrow with profit. End. And in al-Khulasa attributed to al-Nawazil: A man has ten dirhams owed to him by another, and he wants to defer it for one year and take thirteen dirhams. The stratagem is that he buys from him goods with those ten dirhams, takes possession of the goods (the value of the goods being ten), then sells the goods back to him for thirteen dirhams on credit for one year. End.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage belongs to the discussion of legal stratagems (hiyal) used to avoid falling into riba while still achieving financial objectives. It begins by citing a problematic case from al-Khulasa: a ruling by a judge allowing the sale of one dirham for two dirhams hand-to-hand, but the author clarifies that this is not a proper discharge. Then the text returns to the earlier issue of guarantee. It notes that some Companions initially agreed with Ibn Abbas's restricted view on riba, but this view is not enforceable because it is abandoned (mahjur). Then it presents rulings from al-Qunyah: the general transactions people do to avoid riba are not blameworthy (la ba'sa). However, al-Baqqali reports karahah (dislike) from Imam Muhammad for such stratagems, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad? careful: 'عندهما' usually means the two disciples, i.e., Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but here it says 'عندهما', meaning according to the two, and they say la ba'sa. So there is a dispute: Muhammad (maybe alone) considers them makruh, while Abu Yusuf and another (maybe Muhammad with them?) Actually the text: 'ذكر البقالي الكراهة عن محمد وعندهما لا بأس به.' This likely means: al-Baqqali transmitted karahah from Muhammad, while according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is no harm. That is confusing because Muhammad is mentioned twice. Possibly the text means Muhammad alone held karahah, and the other two (Abu Yusuf and al-Shaybani? But al-Shaybani is the same as Muhammad. So it might be: al-Baqqali transmitted karahah from Muhammad, and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad?) or another pair. However, the phrase is from the madhhab literature. Al-Zarruji clarifies: Muhammad's disagreement is specifically when the contract is made after the loan; if he sells first then pays the dirhams, there is no harm by agreement. Then another ruling: it is permissible for the needy to borrow with profit (a form of riba but through a stratagem). Finally, a concrete example: A debtor wants to defer payment and increase the amount. The stratagem is a double sale: the creditor buys goods from the debtor for the existing debt (10 dirhams), takes possession, then sells the same goods back on credit for 13 dirhams. This avoids outright riba while achieving the increase.

Key Terms
حيلة (ḥīlah): A legal stratagem that achieves a permissible outcome while avoiding an otherwise prohibited element (like riba), typically through a series of valid contracts.
كراهية (karāhiyah): Legal dislike: an action that is not haram but is discouraged. In this context, al-Baqqali transmitted karahah from Imam Muhammad regarding certain hiyal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on using legal stratagems (hiyal) to avoid riba according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) They are absolutely prohibited.
B) They are makruh according to all Hanafi imams.
C) They are permissible (la ba'sa) according to the Sahibayn, though there is a weak riwaya of karahah from Imam Muhammad.
D) They are only permissible if the debtor is in dire need.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position permits legal stratagems to avoid riba, though a weak riwaya from Imam Muhammad discourages them.

Permissibility of Legal Stratagems (Hiyal) to Avoid Riba
Practical rulings on permissible stratagems to avoid riba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on legal stratagems (hiyal) to avoid riba, identify the intra-madhhab disagreement between Imam Muhammad and the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and apply the specific hila of sale and buy-back to a debt deferral scenario.

Core Idea
Hanafi hiyal to avoid riba are permissible when done without explicit riba, though Imam Muhammad disliked some forms.

This lesson examines a practical ruling on legal stratagems (hiyal) used by Muslims to avoid falling into riba (usury) in financial transactions. The Hanafi school widely permits such stratagems as a means to achieve lawful objectives, but there is a subtle disagreement within the school regarding their permissibility when they follow a loan. The passage then provides a concrete example of a permissible hila to defer a debt with an increase through a sale and buy-back, which is a classic Hanafi device.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling on hiyal
Read the opening sentence from al-Quniyah: 'There is no harm in the transactions that people perform to guard against usury.' This establishes the default permissibility of hiyal as a means to avoid riba.
The ruling is mubah (permissible) according to the majority of the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi disagreement
The passage then mentions that Al-Baqqali reported dislike (karahah) from Imam Muhammad, while according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) there is no harm. Al-Zarjari clarifies that the disagreement is restricted to the case where a sale occurs after a loan; if the sale is done first, all agree on permissibility.
This distinction is crucial: the timing of the sale relative to the loan changes the ruling.
3
Analyze the specific hila
The passage from al-Khulasa provides a concrete hila: A man has a debt of ten dirhams owed to him. He wants to defer it for a year and receive thirteen dirhams. The stratagem is: (1) He buys goods worth ten dirhams from the debtor, paying the debt as the price (thus extinguishing the debt). (2) He takes possession of the goods. (3) He sells the same goods back to the debtor for thirteen dirhams, payable after one year. This results in a lawful deferred sale with a profit.
The key condition is that the first sale is genuine, with actual possession of goods, and the second sale is a separate transaction.
4
Apply the ruling to the intra-madhhab dispute
Now map the hila to the disagreement: If the original debt is seen as a loan, and then the sale is conducted, it corresponds to the case where Imam Muhammad disliked it. However, the hila as presented is structured as two separate sales, not a loan followed by a sale. Therefore, it falls under the category where all agree it is permissible (the sale first, then payment).
Thus the mufta bihi (operative position) is permissibility, following Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي القنية من الكراهية : لا بأس بالبيوع التي يفعلها الناس للتحرز عن الربا. ثم رقم آخر هي مكروهة ذكر البقالي الكراهة عن محمد وعندهما لا بأس به. قال الزرنجري : خلاف محمد في العقد بعد القرض أما إذا باع ثم دفع الدراهم لا بأس بالاتفاق اهـ . وفي القنية من الكراهية: يجوز للمحتاج الاستقراض بالربح .اهـ. وفي الخلاصة معزياً إلى النوازل : رجل له على آخر عشرة دراهم فأراد أن يؤجلها إلى سنة ويأخذ منه ثلاثة عشر فالحيلة أن يشتري منه بتلك العشرة متاعاً ويقبض المتاع منه وقيمة المتاع عشرة ثم يبيع المتاع منه بثلاثة عشر إلى سنة اهـ .
And in al-Quniyah from the chapter on dislikes: There is no harm in the transactions that people perform to guard against usury. Then another number: They are disliked. Al-Baqqali mentioned dislike from Muhammad, while according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) there is no harm in it. Al-Zarjari said: The disagreement of Muhammad is in the contract after a loan; as for when he sells and then pays the dirhams, there is no harm by agreement. And in al-Quniyah from the chapter on dislikes: It is permissible for the needy to borrow with profit. And in al-Khulasa, attributed to al-Nawazil: A man has ten dirhams owed to him by another; he wants to defer them for a year and take thirteen dirhams. The stratagem is that he buys goods from him with those ten dirhams, takes possession of the goods which are worth ten dirhams, then sells the goods back to him for thirteen dirhams to be paid after a year.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on legal stratagems (hiyal) used to avoid riba in financial transactions. It begins by quoting al-Quniyah that transactions people commonly use to avoid riba are permissible. However, there is a differing opinion recorded: some say they are disliked (makruh). This difference is attributed to Imam Muhammad, who holds a stricter view when the transaction is combined with a loan. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two, 'andahuma), there is no harm. Al-Zarjari clarifies that the disagreement pertains specifically to a sale after a loan; if the sale is conducted first and then the payment, all agree it is permissible. The text then presents a specific hila: a debtor who wants to extend the term and increase the amount can do so by a sale of goods. The creditor buys goods from the debtor for the original debt, takes possession, then sells them back at a higher price deferred. This is a standard Hanafi stratagem to avoid apparent riba while achieving the desired outcome. The lesson classifies this as a ruling statement because it provides practical rulings without extensive proof, though it references scholarly authorities.

Key Terms
الحيلة (al-hīlah): A legal stratagem; a permissible means to achieve a lawful objective while avoiding an unlawful ruling, such as deferring debt with increase through a sale.
الربا (al-ribā): Usury or interest; the prohibited increase in a loan or exchange of certain commodities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which case does Imam Muhammad disagree with Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf?
A) When the sale is conducted before any loan transaction.
B) When the sale is conducted after a loan transaction.
C) When the goods are not physically exchanged.
D) When the price is not specified.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits hiyal to avoid riba, with the only intra-madhhab caution being that the sale should not follow a loan to avoid Imam Muhammad's dislike.

Defining the Cause (Illah) of Riba: Capacity and Genus in Hanafi Law
Definition and analysis of the cause of riba.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the cause (illah) of riba as capacity and genus, and identify its components.

Core Idea
The Hanafi cause of riba is capacity (kīl/wazn) and genus (jins) – these two elements define the prohibition.

In this lesson, we explore the precise definition of the cause (illah) of riba according to the Hanafi school. The matn states that the cause is 'capacity and genus' (al-qadr wa al-jins). The commentary clarifies what these terms mean, excluding other measures such as length or count, and explains how genus is determined by specific name and purpose.

Guided Path
1
Define 'illa in Hanafi usul
According to the passage, 'illa is that to which the establishment of a ruling is ascribed without intermediary. This distinguishes it from conditions and causes.
The linguistic meaning relates to change; the terminological meaning is as above.
2
Analyze 'capacity' (qadr)
Capacity is restricted to kīl (volume) for measurable items and wazn (weight) for weighable items. Other measures like length or count are not considered.
This restriction is emphasized in Fath al-Qadir.
3
Analyze 'genus' (jins)
Genus is determined by the specific name and the purpose of the item. For example, wheat and barley are different genera; dates are one genus; different meats are different genera.
The passage gives many examples from Fath al-Qadir.
4
Apply to examples
Using the definitions, classify items and determine whether they are same or different genera, and identify if capacity applies.
Example: unboiled oil vs boiled scented oil – same genus (oil) but the perfume is an increase, making the trade impermissible.

- بسكون الراء - جنسان لاختلاف الصنعة وقيام الثوب بها، وكذا المروي المنسوج ببغداد وخراسان واللبد اللامتي والطالقاني والتمر كله جنس واحد والحديد والرصاص والشبه أجناس، وكذا غزل الصوف والشعر واللحم الضاني والمعزي والبقري والألية واللحم وشحم البطن أجناس، ودهن البنفسج والخيري جنسان والأدهان المختلفة أصولها أجناس، ولا يجوز بيع رطل زيت غير مطبوخ برطل مطبوخ مطيب لأن الطيب زيادة ا هـ .
His statement: 'and its cause is capacity and genus' meaning the cause of riba, that is, the obligation of equality which when lost makes riba necessary. Thus al-Sighnaqi explained it in his commentary on al-Ikhsikti in Usul and he mentioned it in al-Kafi as question and answer. And in Fath al-Qadir: meaning the cause of prohibition of increase. And in al-Mi'raj: meaning the cause of the prohibition of riba and the obligation of equality. And 'illa in language is an occupying illness; its plural is 'ilal; and God afflicted him thus he is afflicted (ma'lul); and i'talla means he became ill; and i'talla means he clung to his proof; and a'alahu bi kalimah means he made it defective; from this come the 'ilal (defects) of jurists and their i'tilal. As for in usul, they said: in language it is that which changes; from this illness is called 'illa because by its occurrence the state of the place changes from strength to weakness; similarly the wound is called 'illa because by its occurrence on the wounded the ruling of the situation changes. And in terminology: that to which the establishment of a ruling is ascribed without intermediary. Thus the condition (shart) is excluded because the ruling's establishment is not ascribed to it; likewise the cause (sabab) and relationship and the cause of the cause because they are by intermediary. This definition includes the posited causes (al-'ilal al-mawdu'ah) like sale and marriage. And it includes the derived causes (al-mustanbitah) like effective causes in analogies. And what is meant by capacity is kilo in measurable items and weight in weighable items, so the identifier of the ruling is restricted to them; the expression 'capacity' is more concise but includes what is not correct, as it includes length and count which are not from the property of riba. So much so in Fath al-Qadir. But after they placed capacity in place of kilo and weight, how could it include other than them? And jins in language is a species of everything, plural ajans; it is more general than naw'. Animal is a jins, human is a naw'. It is reported from al-Khalil: 'this is mujanis (similar to) this', meaning it resembles it; this is stated in al-Tahdhib as well. And from some: 'so-and-so does not befriend people' if he lacks discrimination and intelligence. Al-Asma'i denies these two usages and says it is speech of the later generations and not Arabic. So much so in al-Misbah. And in Fath al-Qadir: And difference of genus is known by difference of specific name and difference of purpose; so wheat and barley are two genera according to us because the individuals of each are indicated in the hadith. And the Herati and Marwazi cloth are two genera due to difference of manufacturing and the cloth's value by it. Likewise the Marwazi woven in Baghdad and Khurasan, and felt of Lamti and Taliqani, and dates are all one genus; iron, lead, and brass are different genera; likewise yarn of wool and hair, mutton, goat, and beef meat, tail fat and meat and belly fat are different genera; violet oil and wallflower oil are two genera; oils with different origins are different genera; and it is not permissible to sell a ratl of unboiled oil for a ratl of boiled perfumed oil because the perfume is an increase.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling passage explaining the cause (illah) of riba according to the Hanafi school. It opens with the statement from the matn that the cause of riba is capacity (qadr) and genus (jins). The commentator then provides multiple interpretations: some say it refers to the obligation of equality, whose absence leads to riba; others say it is the cause for prohibition of increase. The passage then gives a lengthy linguistic and terminological analysis of the word 'illa itself, distinguishing it from conditions (shurut), reasons (asbab), and other concepts. In Hanafi usul, 'illa is defined as that to which the ruling is directly attributed without intermediary. The passage then specifies that capacity means kilo for measurable items and weight for weighable items, and genus means similarity in essence. The author notes that while the word 'capacity' might seem to include other measures like length or count, these are not considered in riba; rather, in practice, capacity has been restricted to kilo and weight. The genus is determined by specific name and purpose: thus wheat and barley are different genera, dates are one genus, different meats are different genera, etc. The passage ends with a practical example: selling unboiled oil for boiled perfumed oil of the same weight is not permissible because the perfume adds value (an increase). This lesson is a definitional ruling, clarifying the precise cause of riba in Hanafi law.

Key Terms
العلة (al-‘illah): That to which the establishment of a ruling is ascribed without intermediary, e.g., capacity and genus are the cause of riba.
القدر (al-qadr): Capacity; specifically, in riba law, it means kīl (measure of volume) for measurable items and wazn (weight) for weighable items.
الجنس (al-jins): Genus; the essential similarity between items; determined by the specific name and purpose (e.g., wheat and barley are different genera; dates are one genus).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct definition of 'illa in usul?
A) That to which the establishment of a ruling is ascribed through an intermediary.
B) That to which the establishment of a ruling is ascribed without an intermediary.
C) A condition that must be present for the ruling to apply.
D) The general principle underlying the ruling.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi cause of riba is capacity (qadr) – restricted to kīl and wazn – and genus (jins), determined by specific name and purpose; any excess in a transaction of same genus and same capacity constitutes riba.

The Cause of Riba: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on the cause of riba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the effective cause of riba and explain the Hanafi rebuttal using capacity and genus.

Core Idea
Riba's cause is capacity and genus (Hanafi), not edibility and currency (Shafi'i).

This passage presents the classic difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on what triggers riba. The debate centers on the famous hadith of six commodities. Understanding the illah is essential for correctly applying riba rules to modern transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its authority
Locate the six-commodities hadith and note the discussion on its transmission (tawatur) and the grammatical variants. This establishes the textual basis.
The hadith is not mutawatir but is widely narrated.
2
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
The Shafi'i school argues that the cause of riba is edibility (tu'm) for foodstuffs and currency (thimaniyyah) for gold and silver, with genus as a condition. Their proof links the hadith's conditions (like for like, hand-to-hand) to esteem and danger.
3
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school holds that the cause is capacity (kilo/weight) and genus (jins). They argue that equality in form (via capacity) and meaning (via genus) is essential to prevent surplus that constitutes riba.
The Hanafi cause is broader than the Shafi'i one.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i argument
The Hanafis rebut: edibility does not explain riba in all cases (e.g., different meats are all edible but different genera). The hadith's goal is to ensure equality, which is measured by capacity and genus.
See the passage: 'wa lahu anna al-mumathalah bayna al-shay'ayn...'
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis apply riba rules to all items of the same genus measured by weight/volume (e.g., iron, wool). Shafi'is restrict it to foodstuffs and precious metals.
This affects many modern transactions.

وفي المعراج : القدر عبارة عن العيار والجنس عبارة عن مشاكلة المعاني ا اهـ. والأصل في هذا الباب الحديث المشهور وهو قوله «الحنطة بالحنطة والشعير بالشعير والتمر بالتمر والملح بالملح والذهب بالذهب مثلاً بمثل يداً بيد وفيه روايتان بالرفع الحنطة أي بيع مثل وينصب على الحال وكذلك روي الرفع والنصب في يداً بيد» فالرفع عطف على الخبر أي مثل ومقبوضة والنصب على الحال بتأويله بالمشتق متناجزين. وهذا الحديث لشهرته ظن بعض العلماء أنه متواتر وليس كذلك لأنه لا يصدق عليه حده وقال الجصاص : إنه يقرب من المتواتر لكثرة رواته وهو مروي عن ستة عشرة صحابياً. عمر وعبادة بن الصامت وأبو سعيد الخدري وسارية بن أبي سفيان وبلال وأبو هريرة ومعمر بن عبد الله وأبو بكر وعثمان وهشام بن عامر والبراء وزيد بن أرقم وخالد بن عبيد وأبو بكرة وابن عمر وأبو الدرداء رضي الله تعالى عنهم. وقد أطال الكلام في بيانه في البناية ثم قال آخراً: وليس في الأحاديث المذكورة البداءة بالحنطة وإنما هي مذكورة في أثنائه، ولكنه ذكره في المبسوط عن محمد عن أبي حنيفة عن عطية العوفي عن أ أبي سعيد الخدري بادئاً بالحنطة ا هـ . والحكم معلول بإجماع القايسين لكن العلة عندنا ما ذكرناه وعند الشافعي الطعم في المطعومات، والثمنية في الأثمان، والجنسية شرط والمساواة مخلص والأصل هو الحرمة عنده لأنه نص على شرطين التقابض والمماثلة، وكل ذلك يشعر بالعزة والخطر كاشتراط الشهادة في النكاح فيعلل بعلة تناسب إظهار الخطر والعزة وهو الطعم لبقاء الإنسان والثمنية لبقاء الأخوال التي هي مناط المصالح بها ولا أثر للجنسية في ذلك فجعلناه شرطاً، والحكم قد يدور مع الشرط. ولنا أنه أوجب المماثلة شرطاً في البيع وهو المقصود بسوقه تحقيقاً لمعنى البيع إذ هو ينبئ عن التقابل وذلك بالتماثل أو صيانة لأموال الناس عن التوي أو تتميماً للفائدة باتصال التسليم به، ثم يلزم عند فوته حرمة الربا والمماثلة بين الشيئين باعتبار الصورة والمعنى والمعيار يسوي الذات والجنسية تسوي المعنى فيظهر الفضل على ذلك فيتحقق الربا لأن الربا هو الفضل المستحق كما قدمناه ولا يعتبر الوصف لأنه لا يعد تفاوتاً عرفاً أو لأن في اعتباره سد باب

في حيز المنع غاية الأمر أنهم أرادوا هذا المعنى من اللفظ وهذا لا يفيد عدم شموله لغيره وضعاً، نعم في الحواشي السعدية يمكن أن يقال الألف واللام في القدر للعهد والمراد الكيل والوزن. قوله :
And in al-Mi'raj: Capacity is expression of standard (ayar) and genus is expression of similarity of meanings. The foundation of this chapter is the famous hadith, which is his saying: 'Wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, gold for gold, silver for silver, like for like, hand to hand.' And there are two transmissions: with raf' (nominative) 'al-hintatu' meaning a sale of the like, and with nasb (accusative) as a circumstantial accusative, and likewise both raf' and nasb are transmitted in 'yadan bi yadin'. So raf' is an conjunction on the predicate, meaning 'like and received'; and nasb is a circumstantial accusative interpreting it as a derived verbal noun meaning 'taking hand to hand.' This hadith, due to its fame, some scholars thought it was mutawatir, but it is not, because it does not satisfy its definition. Al-Jassas said: it is close to mutawatir due to the many narrators; it is narrated by sixteen companions: 'Umar, 'Ubadah ibn al-Samit, Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, Sariyah ibn Abi Sufyan, Bilal, Abu Hurayrah, Ma'mar ibn 'Abd Allah, Abu Bakr, 'Uthman, Hisham ibn 'Amir, al-Bara', Zayd ibn Arqam, Khalid ibn 'Ubayd, Abu Bakrah, Ibn 'Umar, and Abu al-Darda', may Allah be pleased with them. And he (the commentator) spoke at length about its explanation in al-Binayah, then said at the end: 'And in the mentioned hadiths there is no beginning with wheat, rather it is mentioned in the middle, but he (Imam Muhammad) mentioned it in al-Mabsut from Muhammad from Abu Hanifah from 'Atiyyah al-'Awfi from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, starting with wheat.' And the ruling is made with a cause by the consensus of those who perform qiyas. However, the cause according to us (Hanafis) is what we mentioned (capacity and genus); according to al-Shafi'i, edibility (tu'm) in foodstuffs, and currency value (thimaniyyah) in precious metals, and genus (jinsiyyah) is a condition, and equality is a means of exemption. The original ruling for him is prohibition because the text prescribes two conditions: hand-to-hand and equality. All of this indicates esteem and danger, like requiring witnesses in marriage, so it is caused by a cause appropriate to showing danger and esteem, which is edibility for human survival and currency for the survival of conditions (which are the basis of interests), and genus has no effect in this, so we make it a condition. And the ruling may rotate with the condition. And our (Hanafi) argument: He (the Prophet) made equality a condition in the sale, and it is the purpose of its legislation to actualize the meaning of sale, for it indicates reciprocal exchange, and that is through equality, or to protect people's wealth from loss, or to complete the benefit by connection with delivery. Then upon its loss, the prohibition of riba becomes necessary. And equality between two things is considered in terms of form and meaning; the standard (miyar) equalizes the essence, and genus equalizes the meaning, so the surplus (fadl) appears on that, thus riba is realized because riba is the surplus that is due (al-fadl al-mustahaqq) as we have presented. And the description (wasf) is not considered because it is not regarded as a difference customarily, or because considering it would block the door... This is subject to objection; at most they intended this meaning from the wording, and this does not entail that it does not include others by common usage. Yes, in al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyyah it can be said that the alif and lam in 'al-qadr' are for a specific reference (al-'ahd) and what is meant is kilo and weight. His statement: '...'
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the effective cause ('illah) of riba. It begins by citing the famous hadith of the six commodities (wheat, barley, dates, salt, gold, silver), with a note on its grammatical variants and transmission. The author discusses whether it is mutawatir; Al-Jassas considers it near-mutawatir due to numerous narrators, but the author says it does not meet the definition of tawatur. The hadith is reported from sixteen companions. The key dispute: Hanafis hold that the cause of riba is capacity (kilo/weight) and genus (jins), while Shafi'is hold it is edibility (tu'm) for foodstuffs and currency (thimaniyyah) for gold and silver, making genus a condition rather than part of the cause. The Shafi'i argument is that the hadith mentions two conditions—hand-to-hand and equality—indicating esteem, like witness in marriage, so the cause must be something that reflects esteem: edibility for human survival and currency for the preservation of worldly interests. Genus is irrelevant to esteem, so it is only a condition. The Hanafi response is that equality is itself a condition in sale to actualize exchange or protect property; the loss of equality constitutes riba. Equality is measured by form (via capacity) and meaning (via genus). Without considering genus, surplus (fadl) may be hidden; considering genus ensures that items of different intrinsic value are not exchanged equally, which would constitute riba. The passage also notes a terminological point: 'al-qadr' (capacity) sometimes refers specifically to kilo and weight as a standard. This lesson is a classic usul-i fiqh debate: how to deduce the cause from a text. The Hanafi school's emphasis on capacity and genus leads to different rulings than the Shafi'i school on items like vegetables or commodities not covered by the six.

Key Terms
الطعم (al-tu‘m): Edibility; Shafi'i cause for riba in foodstuffs.
الثمنية (al-thimaniyyah): Currency value; applied to gold and silver (and by analogy to other currencies) according to Shafi'is.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi argument in the passage, why is genus (jins) considered part of the cause of riba?
A) Because the hadith mentions genus explicitly.
B) Because genus equalizes the meaning, revealing surplus (fadl) between different types.
C) Because genus alone prevents riba without considering capacity.
D) Because the Shafi'i school accepts genus as a condition.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines the cause of riba as capacity and genus, a broader scope than the Shafi'i school's cause of edibility and currency.

Defining Jins and Prohibiting Unequal Exchange of Same-Jins Oil
Defining jins and the ruling on oil sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi definition of jins for riba purposes and apply it to determine the validity of an exchange of same-jins commodities.

Core Idea
In riba, jins is defined by origin; exchanging same jins unequally is haram even if processed differently.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies what constitutes the same 'jins' (genus) in sales transactions subject to riba prohibition. It gives examples of different commodities and then presents a ruling: selling one measure of unboiled oil for the same measure of boiled perfumed oil is not allowed. The key is that the added perfume is considered an excess in a same-jins exchange, making it riba al-fadl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall ruling
Locate the final ruling in the passage: selling one ratl of unboiled oil for one ratl of boiled perfumed oil is not permissible. Recognize that the reason given is 'because the perfume is an increase'.
This is a clear statement of prohibition.
2
Understand the definition of jins
The passage first defines jins by giving examples: different cloth types are different jins, all dates are one jins, iron/lead/brass are different jins, different meats are different jins, oils of different origins are different jins. The underlying principle is that jins is based on the essence or origin, not on accidental qualities like processing or added substances.
In Hanafi law, riba applies only to exchanges within the same jins for specified commodities.
3
Apply the jins definition to the oil example
Both unboiled oil and boiled perfumed oil are still oil – they share the same origin. The boiling and perfuming do not change the jins. Therefore they belong to the same jins.
If they were different jins, unequal exchange would be permissible.
4
Recognize the riba factor
Since the oils are the same jins, the sale must be equal in measure. The perfume represents an extra (fadl) because it is an additional substance not compensated for. This excess makes the transaction riba al-fadl (riba of excess), which is haram.
The prohibition holds even though the perfume itself may be valuable; in a same-jins exchange, any extra makes it riba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The chapter on riba - with sukun on the ra - two types due to difference in craftsmanship and the garment's value, and likewise the watered silk woven in Baghdad and Khorasan, felt of Lamti and Talqani, all dates are one type, iron, lead, and brass are different types, and likewise yarn of wool and hair, meat of sheep, goat, and cow, the fat tail, meat, and abdominal fat are different types, oil of violet and wallflower are two types, and oils of different origins are different types, and it is not permissible to sell a ratl of unboiled oil for a ratl of boiled perfumed oil because the perfume is an increase.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It first defines 'jins' (genus) for riba purposes: items sharing essence or origin are one jins, even if quality varies. Examples: different cloth types are different jins; all dates one jins; iron, lead, brass each distinct; different animal meats and fats each distinct; oils from different sources distinct. Then a specific ruling: selling one ratl of unboiled oil for one ratl of boiled perfumed oil is invalid because the added perfume is an extra (fadl), making it riba al-fadl since both are same jins (oil) and unequal in measure.

Key Terms
الجنس (al-jins): In riba, jins refers to items sharing the same essence or origin (e.g., all dates, all oils)
الربا (al-riba): Any excess (fadl) or delay (nasi'ah) in barter of six specified commodities or their analogues

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is selling one ratl of unboiled oil for one ratl of boiled perfumed oil impermissible?
A) Because boiling changes the jins of oil
B) Because the perfume constitutes an extra (fadl) in an exchange of the same jins
C) Because the exchange is equal in measure
D) Because oil is not a ribawi commodity

Key Takeaway
The jins for riba is determined by origin; any excess in same-jins exchange constitutes riba al-fadl.

The Illa of Riba: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Citing the hadith and analyzing the illa for riba with Shafi'i disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the illa of riba and explain the practical difference.

Core Idea
Riba applies to all measurable same-genus items (Hanafi) vs only food and currency (Shafi'i).

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq dissects the famous hadith on riba and reveals the core disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The effective cause (illa) determines which items fall under riba, and this has major practical implications in commerce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its transmission status
The passage cites the famous hadith listing six items (wheat, barley, etc.) requiring equality and hand-to-hand exchange. Note that it is not mutawatir but close due to many narrators.
2
Define the two candidate illas
Hanafis: qadr (measurable by weight/volume) and jins (same genus). Shafi'is: tum (food) for foodstuffs and thumaniyya (monetary value) for currencies.
3
Trace the Shafi'i argument
The hadith conditions indicate high value/importance, so illa should be food and currency; equality is just a condition, not the cause.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Equality is the essence of sale; the illa objectively follows from the hadith's explicit requirement of equality and hand-to-hand exchange. The Shafi'i reliance on 'honor' is subjective.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafis consider all makil/mawzun items ribawi; Shafi'is restrict to foodstuffs and currencies. This affects daily transactions like exchanging grain, oil, or metals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

مثلاً بمثل يداً بيد وفيه روايتان بالرفع الحنطة أي بيع مثل وينصب على الحال وكذلك روي الرفع والنصب في يداً بيد» فالرفع عطف على الخبر أي مثل ومقبوضة والنصب على الحال بتأويله بالمشتق متناجزين. وهذا الحديث لشهرته ظن بعض العلماء أنه متواتر وليس كذلك لأنه لا يصدق عليه حده وقال الجصاص : إنه يقرب من المتواتر لكثرة رواته وهو مروي عن ستة عشرة صحابياً. عمر وعبادة بن الصامت وأبو سعيد الخدري وسارية بن أبي سفيان Al-hintah. And in al-Mi'raj: 'al-qadr' means measure and 'al-jins' means similarity of meanings. The basis of this chapter is the famous hadith - his saying: 'Wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, gold for gold, like for like, hand to hand...' There are two narrations: with raf' (nominative) on 'al-hintah' meaning 'a sell of like' and with nasb (accusative) as a hal; similarly raf' and nasb are narrated in 'yadan bi yad'. The raf' is an appositive to the predicate, i.e., 'like and possessed', and the nasb is a hal interpreting it as a derived term meaning 'mutanajizin' (hand-to-hand). This hadith, due to its fame, some scholars thought it is mutawatir, but it is not because it does not satisfy its definition. Al-Jassas said it is close to mutawatir due to the multiplicity of its narrators; it is narrated from sixteen companions... The ruling is made effective (ma'lul) by consensus of those who perform qiyas, but the 'illa (effective cause) according to us is what we mentioned (qadr and jins), and according to al-Shafi'i, it is tum (food) in foodstuffs and thumaniyya (monetary value) in currencies, with jinsiyya as a condition and equality as a means of safety. The original is prohibition according to him because the text stipulates two conditions: hand-to-hand exchange and equality, and all this indicates honor and importance, like stipulating witnesses in marriage, so it is attributed to a cause that suits the manifestation of honor and importance, i.e., tum for the sustenance of humans and thumaniyya for the sustenance of transactions, and jinsiyya has no effect in that, so we made it a condition... And for us, he required equality as a condition in the sale, which is the intended purpose of the market to realize the meaning of sale, since it indicates exchange, and that is by equality... then when it is absent, the prohibition of riba applies. Equality between two things is with respect to form and meaning; measure equalizes substance and jins equalizes meaning, so excess appears in that and riba is realized... and description is not considered because it is not a recognized disparity customarily, or because considering it would close the door... At most, they intended this meaning from the wording, and this does not preclude it from including others by usage. Yes, in al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyya it can be said that the definite article in 'al-qadr' is for the specific referent, meaning measure by volume or weight.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the effective cause (illa) of riba. It starts with definitions of qadr (measure) and jins (genus) from al-Mi'raj. The famous hadith listing six ribawi items is cited, requiring equality and hand-to-hand exchange. The hadith is well-known but not mutawatir; al-Jassas says it is close. The key dispute: Hanafis hold the illa is qadr and jins – any measurable item of the same genus is ribawi. Shafi'is hold the illa is being a food (tum) for foodstuffs and being a medium of exchange (thumaniyya) for currencies, with jinsiyya as a mere condition. The Hanafi response: equality (mumathala) is explicitly required, and it is achieved only through qadr and jins. The hadith's mention of hand-to-hand and equality indicates the need for both, and any excess in same-genus measured items is riba. The Shafi'i argument that these conditions indicate high value is rejected; the illa is objective. The passage ends with a note from al-Hawashi that 'al-qadr' may refer specifically to volume or weight measurement.

Key Terms
العلة (al-illa): The effective cause that triggers the ruling of riba; Hanafis: qadr and jins; Shafi'is: tum and thumaniyya
القدر (al-qadr): In riba, the quality of being measurable by weight or volume
الجنس (al-jins): Common genus or substance (e.g., all grains, all oils)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the effective cause for riba according to the Hanafi school?
A) Being a food (tum)
B) Being a currency (thumaniyya)
C) Being measurable (qadr) and same genus (jins)
D) Being valuable

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that riba applies to all items that are measurable by weight/volume and are of the same genus, while the Shafi'i school restricts riba to food items and currencies.

Conditions for Riba al-Fadl and Riba al-Nasi'ah
Explaining conditions for riba al-fadl and riba al-nasi'ah with examples and intra-school discussion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions triggering prohibition of riba al-fadl and riba al-nasi'ah in Hanafi fiqh and explain the role of shubha in extending prohibition.

Core Idea
Delay is haram with one condition; excess is haram only with both.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the matn's rules for riba. It clarifies that riba al-nasi'ah (delay) is prohibited when either qadr (measure) or jins (genus) is present, while riba al-fadl (excess) requires both. The commentator uses the concept of shubha (semblance) to justify prohibition even when only one condition exists, and addresses objections from Shafi'is and within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
Qadr (measurability by weight or volume) and jins (same genus/type) are the two relevant attributes for ribawi items.
2
Apply the three-case rule
Case 1: Both conditions present → excess and delay haram. Case 2: Only one present → delay haram, excess halal. Case 3: Neither present → sale valid.
The passage gives examples: wheat for barley (different jins, same qadr) → only delay prohibited if credit; Marwi garment for two (same jins, no qadr) → hand-to-hand valid, credit haram.
3
Understand the shubha argument
When one condition is present, the transaction resembles riba enough (shubha) to prohibit delay. This differs from Shafi'is who require both conditions for any prohibition.
Hanafis argue that shubha of riba is like the reality; the cause (illa) is the presence of jins or qadr.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi refinement
Mulla Akmal raises 'shubhat al-shubha' (semblance of semblance) but the response clarifies that the shubha is in the cause and locus, not an infinite regress.
The shubha is considered a valid basis for prohibition.
5
Note objections and responses
Shafi'i objection: jins alone does not create shubha of excess. Hanafi response: the presence of jins creates a shubha of riba in wealth, which is sufficient. Also, the hadith on selling animals on credit supports the Hanafi view.
The passage also addresses salam contracts and the example of selling a slave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الإطلاق بأبلغ الوجوه لشدة الاحتياج إليها دون التضييق فلا يعتبر بما ذكره ؛ كذا في الهداية قوله : (وحرم الفضل والنساء بهما) أي بالقدر والجنس لوجود العلة بتمامها والفضل الزيادة والنساء بالمد التأخير، ولم متفاضلاً. لا نسيئة. الثانية باع ثوباً مروياً بمرويين جاز حاضراً، ولو باع عبداً بعبد إلى أجل لا يجوز لوجود الجنس. وقال الشافعي: الجنس بانفراده لا يحرم النساء لأنه لا يثبت بالتأخير إلا شبهة الفضل وحقيقة الفضل جائز فالشبهة أولى ولنا أنه مال الربا من وجه نظرا إلى القدر أو إلى الجنس والنقدية أوجبت فضلاً في المالية فيتحقق شبهة الرب وهي مانعة عن الجواز كالحقيقة كذا في الهداية. قال مولانا الأكمل : فيه بحث من وجهين: أحدهما ما قيل إن كونه من مال الربا من وجه شبهة وكون الشبهة أوجبت فضلاً شبهة فصارت شبهة الشبهة فالشبهة هي المعتبرة دون النازل عنها. والثاني أن كونها شبهة الربا كالحقيقة إما أن يكون مطلقاً أو في محل الحقيقة، والأول ممنوع، والثاني مسلم لكنها كانت جائزة فيما نحن فيه فيجب أن تكون الشبهة كذلك. والجواب عن الأول أن الشبهة الأولى في المحل، والثانية في الحكم، وثمة شبهة أخرى وهي التي في العلة، With both (qadr and jins) (riba al-fadl and nasi'ah are prohibited), and with only one of them (only nasi'ah is prohibited), and when both are absent (the sale is valid). The sale of measured items like wheat, barley, dates, salt - sales are valid or due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Its good and bad are equal.' And tum (food) and thumaniyya (monetary value) are among the greatest benefits, and the way in such things is to allow them in the most complete manner due to severe need, not to restrict, so what he mentioned is not considered. Thus in al-Hidayah. His statement: 'And the prohibition of excess and delay with both' i.e., with qadr and jins, because the cause is complete. 'Al-fadl' is excess, 'al-nisa'' with madd is delay. He did not mention it in al-Misbah but mentioned al-nasi'... In al-Binaya: 'al-nisa'' with fat-h al-nun and madd is sale for a term, and in Fath al-Qadir it is with madd only. His statement: 'And (prohibition of) delay only with one of them' i.e., the prohibition of delay only, not excess, when only qadr exists or only jins exists. There are two cases: first, he sold wheat for barley with excess (but hand-to-hand) — only nasi'ah is prohibited? Actually the text says 'la nasi'ah' meaning no delay? The second, he sold a garment of Marwi for two garments of Marwi, it is permissible hand-to-hand; but if he sold a slave for a slave on credit, it is not permissible due to the existence of jins. And al-Shafi'i said: jins alone does not prohibit nasi'ah because delay only establishes a semblance (shubha) of fadl, and actual fadl is permissible, so the semblance is more appropriate. But for us, it is riba-money from one aspect, considering qadr or jins, and the monetary value necessitates a fadl in wealth, so a shubha of riba is realized, which prevents permissibility like the reality... Some argued for our school with his prohibition (peace be upon him) of selling animals for animals on credit, narrated by Abu Dawud... An objection was raised that it is only part of the cause... Another objection: the apparent meaning of the author's statement 'and delay only with one of them' prevents the validity of salam (advance payment) of currencies for saffron or cotton due to the existence of qadr, i.e., weight, while it is valid. The answer from al-Hidayah is that they do not agree in the description of weight... And (the example of selling a slave for a slave) was objected to by some scholars that the cause here is the slave's non-acceptance of deferment, not the existence of jins, so if he had given the example of a Marwi garment for a similar one, it would be better...
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, expanding on the matn's conditions for riba al-fadl and riba al-nasi'ah. It states: when both qadr (measurability) and jins (same genus) exist, both excess and delay are prohibited. When only one exists, only delay is prohibited. When neither, the sale is valid (e.g., different jins). The commentator clarifies linguistic terms: 'nisa'' with madd means delay, synonymous with 'nasi'ah'. Two examples of 'delay only with one' are given: 1) selling wheat for barley with excess but hand-to-hand – only delay is prohibited? Actually the text says 'la nasi'ah'? 2) selling a Marwi garment for two such garments hand-to-hand is valid, but selling a slave for a slave on credit is invalid due to same jins. The Shafi'i objection that jins alone should not prohibit delay is refuted: the presence of either qadr or jins creates a shubha (semblance) of riba, which is sufficient. Mulla Akmal's objection about shubhat al-shubha is answered: the shubha is in the cause, not an infinite regress. An additional proof is the hadith prohibiting selling animals for animals on credit (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). A further objection: salam (advance payment) of money for saffron would be valid even though both are weighty, because they differ in weight-standard (money by scales, saffron by pounds). Finally, the example of selling a slave is criticized: the cause is the slave's inability to accept deferment, not jins; but the commentator says the example is for illustration only.

Key Terms
النساء (al-nisa'): In riba, deferment or delay of payment in barter (also nasi'ah)
الفضل (al-fadl): Excess in quantity/value in same-jins exchange
الشبهة (al-shubha): A semblance or doubt; presence of one condition creates shubha of riba, sufficient to prohibit delay
القدر (al-qadr): Measurability by weight or volume, one of the two conditions for riba
الجنس (al-jins): Genus or type; same species or category of commodity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is riba al-nasi'ah (delay) prohibited?
A) Only when both qadr and jins are present
B) Only when either qadr or jins is present
C) Only when jins is present but not qadr
D) Only when the two items are of the same type

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, riba al-nasi'ah is prohibited when either qadr or jins is present, while riba al-fadl requires both.

Riba: The Hanafi Ruling on Measure, Genus, and Deferment
Explains the basic Hanafi ruling on riba with conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on riba al-fadl and riba al-nasi'ah when both measure and genus are present, and when only one is present, and apply the ruling to barter transactions.

Core Idea
When both genus and measure coincide, any excess or deferment is riba; when only one coincides, only deferment is prohibited.

Riba in sales has two dimensions: excess (riba al-fadl) and deferment (riba al-nasi'ah). The Hanafi school distinguishes between the presence of both genus (jins) and measure (qadr) versus only one. This lesson unpacks the conditions under which each type becomes prohibited, based on the complete cause (illa) of riba. We will work through the key examples given in the text to solidify the rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two ribawi conditions
Recognize that riba is triggered by two attributes: genus (jins) and measure (qadr – weight or capacity). When both are present in an item, it is a ribawi commodity.
Examples: gold, silver, wheat, barley are ribawi because they have both measure and genus (by type).
2
Understand the two prohibitions
When both genus and measure are shared in a barter exchange, both excess (fadl) and deferment (nasi'ah) are prohibited. When only one of them is shared, only deferment is prohibited; excess is allowed if hand-to-hand.
Wheat for barley: different genus, same measure – excess allowed hand-to-hand, deferment prohibited.
3
Apply to the slave example
Slave for slave: same genus (human), even without measure – deferment is prohibited because genus alone suffices for the shubha of riba.
This is the Hanafi position; Shafi'i disagrees (covered in the next lesson).
4
Note the lexical nuances
The terms nasi'ah (delay) and nasi' (deferred sale) are derived from the same root; the text clarifies definitions from various sources.
This helps avoid confusion in terminology.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صح البياعات أو لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام جيدها ورديئها سواء والطعم والثمنية من أعظم وجوه المنافع والسبيل في مثلها الإطلاق بأبلغ الوجوه لشدة الاحتياج إليها دون التضييق فلا يعتبر بما ذكره ؛ كذا في الهداية قوله : (وحرم الفضل والنساء بهما) أي بالقدر والجنس لوجود العلة بتمامها والفضل الزيادة والنساء بالمد التأخير، ولم يذكره في المصباح وإنما ذكر النسيء فقال : والنسيء مهموز على فعيل ويجوز الإدغام لأنه زائد وهو التأخير. والنسيئة على فعليه مثله وهما اسمان من نسأ الله أجله من باب نفع وأنساه الله بألف إذا أخره ا هـ. وفي البناية : النساء بفتح النون والمد البيع إلى أجل وفي فتح القدير أنه بالمد لا غير. قوله: (والنساء فقط بأحدهما) أي وحرم التأخير لا الفضل بوجود القدر فقط والجنس فقط وله صورتان : إحداهما باع حنطة بشعير متفاضلاً. لا نسيئة. الثانية باع ثوباً مروياً بمرويين جاز حاضراً، ولو باع عبداً بعبد إلى أجل لا يجوز لوجود الجنس. وقال الشافعي: الجنس بانفراده لا يحرم النساء لأنه لا يثبت بالتأخير إلا شبهة الفضل وحقيقة الفضل جائز فالشبهة أولى ولنا أنه مال الربا من وجه نظرا إلى القدر أو إلى الجنس والنقدية أوجبت فضلاً في المالية فيتحقق شبهة الرب وهي مانعة عن الجواز كالحقيقة كذا في الهداية. قال مولانا الأكمل : فيه بحث من وجهين: أحدهما ما قيل إن كونه من مال الربا من وجه شبهة وكون الشبهة أوجبت فضلاً شبهة فصارت شبهة الشبهة فالشبهة هي المعتبرة دون النازل عنها. والثاني أن كونها شبهة الربا كالحقيقة إما أن يكون مطلقاً أو في محل الحقيقة، والأول ممنوع، والثاني مسلم لكنها كانت جائزة فيما نحن فيه فيجب أن تكون الشبهة كذلك. والجواب عن الأول أن الشبهة الأولى في المحل، والثانية في الحكم، وثمة شبهة أخرى وهي التي في العلة، ولشبهة العلة والمحل تثبت شبهة الحكم لا شبهة الشبهة وعن الثاني أن القسمة غير حاضرة بل الشبهة مانعة في محل الشبهة إذا وجدت العلة بكمالها اهـ. واستدل بعضهم لمذهبنا بنهيه عليه السلام عن بيع الحيوان بالحيوان نسيئة رواه أبو داود. وقال الترمذي : إنه حدیث حسن صحيح. قال : والعمل عليه عند أكثر أهل العلم وتمامه في البناية. وأورد أنه بعض العلة فلا يثبت به الحكم. وأجيب بأنه علة تامة لحرمة النساء وإن كان بعض علة الحرمة الفضل فلا يؤدي إلى توزيع أجزاء الحكم على أجزاء العلة كذا في المعراج. وأورد أيضاً أن ظاهر قول المصنف والنساء فقط بأحدهما يمنع جواز إسلام النقود في الزعفران أو القطن لوجود القدر وهو الوزن مع أنه جائز . فأجاب عنه في الهداية بأنهما لا يتفقان في صفة الوزن، أما إذا اختلفا في المعنى فيجوز لأن النقود توزن بالصنجات والزعفران بالأمناء (ولو باع عبداً بعبد الخ) اعترضه بعض الفضلاء بأن علة الحكم هنا عدم قبول العبد التأجيل لا وجود الجنسية فلو مثل ببيع هروي بمثله لكان أولى .اهـ. وهو مناقشة في المثال والمقصود منه التوضيح على ومعنى فنقول : الدراهم مع الزعفران وإن اتفقا في الوزن صورة فقد اختلفا فيما يوزن به صورة وحكماً فيجوز التأخير، أما الاختلاف الصوري فما بيناه وأما الاختلاف في المعنى فلأن النقود لا تتعين بالتعيين والزعفران ونحوه يتعين، وأما الاختلاف في الأحكام فيجوز التصرف في النقود قبل قبضها بخلاف المثمن فلم يجمعهما القدر من كل وجه فنزلت الشبهة فيه إلى شبهة الشبهة فإن الموزونين إذا اتفقا كان المنع للشبهة وإذا لم يتفقا كان ذلك شبهة الوزن والوزن وحده شبهة فكأن ذلك شبهة الشبهة وهي غير معتبرة. والصنجات بتحريك النون جمع صنجة. وعن ابن السكيت لا يقال بالسين وإنما يقال بالصاد. وفي المغرب : الصنجات بالتحريك جمع صنجة بالتسكين. وعن الفراء بالسين أفصح، وأنكر القتبي السين أصلاً.
Correct the sales or due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Its good and its bad are equal.' And taste and currency are among the greatest aspects of benefits, and the way in such matters is to allow by the most emphatic methods due to severe need for them without restriction, so no consideration is given to what he mentioned; as in al-Hidayah. His statement: 'And prohibited is excess and deferment in both,' meaning by measure and genus, due to the complete existence of the cause. Excess is increase, and an-nisa' with prolongation is delay. He did not mention it in al-Misbah but mentioned an-nasi', so he said: An-nasi' is emphasized on the pattern of fa'il, and it is permissible to assimilate it because it is extra, and it is delay. An-nasi'ah on the pattern of fa'ilah is similar, both are nouns from nasa'a Allah ajalahu, from the category of nafa'a, and ansahu Allah with an alif when he delays it, end. In al-Binaya: an-nisa' with fatih on the nun and prolongation is sale to a term, and in Fath al-Qadir it is with prolongation, no other. His statement: 'And deferment only with one of them,' meaning deferment is prohibited, not excess, by the existence of only measure and only genus. It has two cases: one, he sold wheat for barley with excess, no deferment. Second, he sold a cloth for two cloths, it is permissible if present, and if he sold a slave for a slave to a term, it is not permissible due to the existence of genus. Al-Shafi'i said: Genus alone does not prohibit deferment because only the shubha of excess arises from deferment, and actual excess is permissible, so shubha is more deserving. And for us, it is ribawi property from one perspective, considering measure or genus and monetary value caused excess in value, so the shubha of riba is realized, and it prevents permissibility like reality, as in al-Hidayah. Our master al-Akmal said: There is discussion in two respects: first, what was said that its being ribawi property from one perspective is shubha, and that shubha caused excess is a shubha, so it became shubha of shubha, and shubha is what is considered, not the lower than it. Second, that its being shubha of riba like reality is either absolute or in the place of reality; the first is denied, the second is conceded, but it was permissible in our case, so the shubha should be likewise. The answer to the first: the first shubha is in the place, the second in the ruling, and there is another shubha which is in the cause, and due to the shubha of cause and place, the shubha of ruling is established, not shubha of shubha. And as for the second: the division is not present, rather shubha is preventive in the place of shubha when the cause is complete, end. Some of our school adduced the prohibition of the Prophet, peace be upon him, of selling an animal for an animal on credit, narrated by Abu Dawud. Al-Tirmidhi said: It is a hasan sahih hadith. He said: Acting upon it is according to most scholars, and its completion is in al-Binaya. It was objected that it is part of the cause, so the ruling is not established by it. And it was answered that it is a complete cause for the prohibition of deferment, even if it is part of the cause of prohibition of excess, so it does not lead to distributing parts of the ruling upon parts of the cause, as in al-Mi'raj. It was also objected that the apparent meaning of the author's statement 'and deferment only with one of them' prevents the permissibility of salam of coins in saffron or cotton, due to the existence of measure, which is weight, while it is permissible. He answered in al-Hidayah: They do not agree in the quality of weight; as for when they differ in meaning, it is permissible because coins are weighed with scales and saffron with manna. And if he sold a slave for a slave, etc., some scholars objected that the cause of the ruling here is the slave's not accepting deferment, not the existence of genus, so if he had given the example of selling a Herawi for its like, it would have been better, end. It is a criticism of the example, and the purpose of it is clarification upon meaning. So we say: Dirhams with saffron, even if they agree in weight in form, they differ in what is weighed with, in form and ruling, so deferment is permissible. As for the formal difference, we have explained it; as for the difference in meaning, because coins are not specified by specification, while saffron and the like are specified; as for the difference in rulings, it is permissible to dispose of coins before taking possession, unlike the sold item, so measure does not unite them from every aspect, so the shubha falls to shubha of shubha. For if the two weighed items agree, prohibition is due to shubha; if they do not agree, that is shubha of weight, and weight alone is shubha, so it is as if that is shubha of shubha, and it is not considered. And as-sanajat with a harakah on the noon is plural of sanjah. From Ibn al-Sikkit, it is not said with sin, only with sad. In al-Mughrib: as-sanajat with harakah is plural of sanjah with sukun. From al-Farra, with sin is more eloquent, and al-Qutaybi rejected the sin entirely.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expounding the rules of riba in sales. It begins by explaining that the correct view is to allow transactions in weights and measures due to need, citing the hadith 'its good and its bad are equal'. Then it defines key terms: riba al-fadl (excess) and riba al-nasi'ah (deferment). The phrase 'wa hurrima al-fadlu wa al-nisa'u bihima' means both excess and deferment are prohibited when both genus and measure are present, as the complete cause (illa) exists. When only one of them exists, only deferment is prohibited, not excess. The author gives two examples: exchanging wheat for barley with excess but hand-to-hand is permissible (since different genus), and selling a cloth for two cloths hand-to-hand is permissible (since not measured). However, selling a slave for a slave on credit is prohibited because of same genus. Then the Shafi'i position is presented: they argue that genus alone should not prohibit deferred payment, because deferment only creates a shubha (doubt) of excess, and actual excess is permissible, so shubha is even more permissible. The Hanafi response is that the item is ribawi from one perspective (measure or genus and monetary value), which creates a shubha of riba, and this shubha is preventative like actual riba. The commentator al-Akmal refines this: he distinguishes between shubha in the place, in the ruling, and in the cause, concluding that only the shubha of the cause is effective. The author then supports the Hanafi view with the hadith of the Prophet prohibiting selling animals on credit (narrated by Abu Dawud, declared hasan sahih by Tirmidhi). Some objected that this hadith only proves part of the cause, but the answer is that it is a complete cause for prohibiting deferment. Another objection concerns the apparent meaning of the author's phrase: it seems to prohibit salam (forward sale) of coins in saffron or cotton, but such salam is permissible. The answer clarifies that although both are weighed, they differ in the method of weighing (scales vs. manna), in legal rulings (coins are not specified by specification, can be disposed before possession), so the shubha is only shubha of weight (a lower level), which is not considered. Finally, some objected to the example of selling a slave for a slave, arguing the cause is the slave's inability to accept deferment, not genus; the response is that this is a mere criticism of the example, not the ruling itself. The passage ends with lexical notes on 'sanajah' (scale).

Key Terms
ربا الفضل (riba al-fadl): Excess in a barter exchange of ribawi items of the same genus or measure.
ربا النساء (riba al-nasi'ah): Deferred payment in a barter exchange of ribawi items; prohibited when genus or measure is present.
قدر (qadr): Measure or weight, the quantitative attribute that makes an item ribawi when combined with genus.
جنس (jins): Genus or type, the qualitative attribute that makes items belong to the same ribawi category.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, which of the following transactions is prohibited due to riba al-nasi'ah?
A) Selling wheat for barley with excess, hand-to-hand.
B) Selling a cloth for two cloths, hand-to-hand.
C) Selling a slave for a slave on credit.
D) Selling gold for silver with deferment.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits deferment whenever genus or measure is shared; when both are shared, both excess and deferment are prohibited.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
12 min
The Shafi'i Dispute: Does Genus Alone Prohibit Deferment in Riba?
Presents the Shafi'i objection and the Hanafi response with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi argument that genus alone prohibits deferment (nasi'ah) in ribawi items, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument involving shubha.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, shubha of riba is treated like reality when the cause is complete, whereas Shafi'i holds that shubha of a permissible thing cannot prohibit.

The Hanafi school maintains that genus alone is sufficient to prohibit deferred payment in barter exchanges, even without measure. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that deferment only creates a shubha (doubt) of excess, and since excess itself is permissible in some contexts, the shubha should also be permissible. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi response, including the refinement by al-Akmal, and the hadith evidence prohibiting animal-for-animal on credit. We also address objections raised against the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disagreement
The issue: Does the presence of genus alone in a ribawi item make deferred exchange haram? Hanafi says yes; Shafi'i says no.
The thamarah (practical effect): Shafi'i permits selling a slave for a slave on credit; Hanafi prohibits it.
2
Understand the Shafi'i argument
Shafi'i argues that deferment creates only a shubha of excess. Since actual excess is permissible in some sales (e.g., different genera), the shubha is even more deserving of permissibility.
This is based on the principle that what is permissible in reality is also permissible in its shubha.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
Hanafi responds that the item is ribawi from one perspective (considering genus and monetary value), which creates a shubha of riba. This shubha is preventative like actual riba because the cause (illa) is partially present. The item is 'mal al-riba min wajh'.
The shubha here is not of a permissible thing, but of a prohibited thing (riba).
4
Examine al-Akmal's refinement
Al-Akmal distinguishes between shubha in the place (mahal), in the ruling (hukm), and in the cause (illa). He argues that only the shubha of the cause (i.e., genus as part of the illa) is effective, not lower-level shubha.
This refines the Hanafi argument and counters the Shafi'i objection.
5
Evaluate the hadith evidence
The Hanafi school adduces the hadith prohibiting animal-for-animal on credit (Sunan Abi Dawud). This is a direct proof that genus alone (animals, same genus) triggers the prohibition of deferment.
Objections that it is only part of the cause are answered: it is a complete cause for prohibiting deferment.
