Specification vs. Possession in Non-Sarf Ribawi Items
Explaining that in ribawi items other than sarf, specification suffices without immediate possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school distinguishes between sarf and non-sarf ribawi items regarding the requirement of immediate possession, and apply the ruling to trade scenarios.

Core Idea
In non-sarf ribawi items, specification suffices; possession is required only in sarf.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a critical distinction in Hanafi sales law: the role of immediate possession (taqabud) in ribawi transactions. While common understanding might assume possession is always required, the Hanafi school limits it to currency exchange (sarf). For other ribawi goods like wheat or barley, specifying the item (ta'yin) is enough. Understanding this distinction is key to correctly applying riba rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the specific transaction type (sale of ribawi items non-sarf) and the Hanafi ruling: validity with specification alone, no possession required.
The act is a sale of two ribawi items (e.g., wheat for wheat) that are not currency exchange.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the hadith cited regarding 'yad' (hand) and how it is used as proof for the ruling.
The hadith is not quoted in full, but the interpretation of 'yad' is central.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the word 'yad' in the hadith is interpreted as specification (ta'yin) for non-sarf items, versus possession for currencies.
The text states: 'والمراد باليد في الحديث التعيين' – the meaning of hand is specification.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize that other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require possession in all ribawi transactions, making this a point of scholarly difference.
The Hanafi position is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf: how the difference affects the validity of sales in real life.
For non-sarf ribawi items, Hanafis validate without handover; others may require it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب الربا التعيين دون التقابض في غير الصرف من الربويات وصح بيع الحفنة بالحفنتين والتفاحة تنفذ من عقد البيع حتى لو اشترى حنطة أو شيئاً فوجده رديئاً بلا عيب لا يرده كما في المحيط من الصرف وقدمناه في خيار العيب وتعتبر في الأموال الربوية في مال اليتيم فلا يجوز للوصي بيع قفيز حنطة جيدة بقفيز رديء، وينبغي أن تعتبر في مال الوقف لأنه كاليتيم وقد كتبنا في الفوائد أنها معتبرة في أربعة هذان وفي حق المريض حتى الثلث وفي الرهن القلب إذا انكسر عند المرتهن ونقصت قيمته فإن المرتهن يضمن قيمته ذهباً ويكون رهناً عنده قوله: (ويعتبر التعيين دون التقابض في غير الصرف من الربويات) لأنه متعين فلا مبيع يشترط فيه القبض كغير مال الربا لحصول المقصود وهو التمكن من التصرف بخلاف الصرف لعدم تعينه إلا بالقبض فاشترط فيه ليتعين والمراد باليد في الحديث التعيين وهو في النقدين بالقبض، وفي غيرهما بالتعيين فلم يلزم الجمع بين معنيين مختلفين وإنما اشترط القبض في المصوغ من الذهب والفضة باعتبار أصل خلقته وبيانه كما ذكره الأسبيجابي بقوله : وإذا تبايعا كيلياً بكيلي أو وزنياً بوزني كلاهما من جنس واحد أو من جنسين مختلفين فإن البيع لا يجوز حتى يكون كلاهما عيناً أضيف إليه العقد وهو حاضر أو غائب بعد أن يكون موجوداً في ملكه، والتقابض قبل الافتراق بالأبدان ليس بشرط لجوازه إلا في الذهب والفضة. ولو كان أحدهما عيناً أضيف إليه العقد والآخر ديناً موصوفاً في الذمة فإنه ينظر؛ إن جعل الدين منهما ثمناً والعين مبيعاً جاز البيع بشرط أن يتعين الدين منهما قبل التفرق بالأبدان، وإن جعل الدين منهما مبيعاً لا يجوز وإن أحضره في المجلس. والذي ذكر فيه الباء ثمن وما لم يذكر فيه إذا قال بعت هذه الحنطة على أنها قفيز بقفيز حنطة جيدة أو قال بعث منك وبيانه : مبيع هذه الحنطة على أنها قفيز بقفيز من شعير جيد فالبيع جائز لأنه جعل العين منهما مبيعاً والدين الموصوف ثمناً ولكن قبض الدين منهما قبل التفرق بالأبدان شرط لأن من شروط جواز هذا البيع أن يحصل الافتراق عن عين بعين وما كان ديناً لا يتعين إلا بالقبض، ولو قبض الدين منهما ثم تفرقا جاز البيع قبض العين منهما أو لم يقبض، ولو قال اشتريت منك قفيز حنطة جيدة بهذا القفيز من الحنطة أو قال اشتريت منك قفيزي شعير جيد بهذا القفيز من الحنطة فإنه لا يجوز وإن أحضر الدين في المجلس لأنه جعل الدين مبيعاً فصار بائعاً ما ليس عنده وهو الباء يجوز اهـ . لا بالحقاق ويحسب بالأرطال، وهذا معنى نسبته إلى الرطل وحينئذ فالحق يسمى أوقية. قوله: (وفي التبيين وهذا مشكل الخ) قال في النهر : وقدمنا عن الفتح أنه لو باع الفضة بجنسها في كفة ميزان جاز لانتفاء احتمال التفاضل، وهذا يؤيد ما ادعاه الشارح. وعن الصيرفية أيضاً: لو تبايعا تبراً بذهب مضروب كفة بكفة لا يجوز ما لم يعلما وزن الذهب لأنه وزني وهذا يشهد لصاحب الهداية :
Book of sale, chapter of riba: specification without immediate possession in non-sarf ribawi items. And the sale of a handful for two handfuls, and an apple... proceeds from the contract. Even if one buys wheat or something and finds it defective without a defect, he cannot return it, as in al-Muhit from al-Sarf, and we presented it in the option of defect. Consideration of ribawi wealth is in the wealth of an orphan: the guardian cannot sell a qafiz of good wheat for a qafiz of bad wheat. It should also be considered in the wealth of a waqf because it is like an orphan. We have written in al-Fawa'id that it is considered in four: these two, and in the case of a patient up to one-third, and in a pledge of a heart when it breaks with the pledgee and its value decreases, then the pledgee guarantees its value in gold and it remains a pledge with him. The author's statement: (Specification is considered without immediate possession in non-sarf ribawi items) because it is specified, so no sold item requires possession like non-riba wealth, because the purpose—the ability to dispose—is achieved, unlike sarf which is not specified except by possession, so it is required for specification. The meaning of 'hand' in the hadith is specification; in currencies it is by possession, in others by specification, so it does not necessitate combining two different meanings. Possession in manufactured gold and silver is required based on their original creation. Its explanation is as al-Asbajabi mentioned: When two parties trade a measured item for a measured item or a weighed item for a weighed item, both of the same kind or different kinds, the sale is not valid unless both are a specific 'ayn added to the contract, present or absent, after being in his ownership. Possession before physical separation is not a condition for validity except in gold and silver. If one is a specific 'ayn and the other is a debt described in the dhimmah, then there is consideration: if the debt is made the price and the 'ayn the sold item, the sale is valid with the condition that the debt becomes specified before separation. If the debt is made the sold item, it is not valid even if brought to the session. [Examples are given]. The statement: 'And in al-Tabyin, this is problematic...' He said in al-Nahr: We presented from al-Fath that if one sells silver for its like in a scale pan, it is valid because the possibility of inequality is removed, and this supports what the commentator claimed. And from al-Sayrafiyyah: If two trade bullion for struck gold pan for pan, it is not valid unless they know the weight of the gold because it is weighed, and this supports the author of al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq along with its commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The ruling states that in ribawi items other than currency exchange (sarf), specification (ta'yin) of the item in the contract is sufficient, and immediate possession (taqabud) at the contract session is not required. This is because the item is already determined by its specific identity. In contrast, in sarf (exchange of gold and silver), the item is not considered specified without actual hand-to-hand delivery. The commentary then clarifies that this applies only to non-sarf ribawi items; for sarf, both specification and possession are necessary. The author cites a hadith where 'hand' (yad) means specification, but in currencies it is achieved by possession, while in other items it is by identification. Additional rulings: if a guardian buys wheat for an orphan and finds it defective without a defect, he cannot return it. Similarly, a guardian cannot exchange good wheat for bad wheat. The same applies to waqf property. The commentary also addresses cases involving debt, where if the debt is made the price, the sale is valid but possession of the debt before separation is required. If the debt is made the sold item, the sale is invalid because it would be selling what one does not possess. The passage ends with a discussion of weighing silver in a balance scale, citing al-Fath and al-Sayrafiyyah.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification of the exact item sold, making it determinate.
تقابض (taqabud): Immediate hand-to-hand possession at the contract session.
ربويات (ribawiyat): Goods subject to riba (usury) rules, typically those measured or weighed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Hanafi sale of wheat for wheat (both ribawi), which of the following is required for validity in the contract session?
A) Immediate possession (taqabud) and specification (ta'yin).
B) Specification only, without possession.
C) Possession only, without specification.
D) Neither specification nor possession.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, non-sarf ribawi items require only specification (ta'yin) for validity; immediate possession is not a condition.

The Validity of Unequal Exchange When Legal Measurement is Absent
Ruling with proof through talil (reasoning)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits selling a handful for two handfuls, and identify the condition (absence of legal measure) that prevents riba.

Core Idea
Riba requires capacity; no capacity when no legal measure exists.

You might think any unequal exchange of the same good is riba. Not so in the Hanafi school. The key is whether the item has a legal standard for measurement or weight. This lesson unpacks that reasoning through the examples of a handful, an apple, an egg, and a walnut.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its examples
Read the matn: the sale of a handful for two handfuls, an apple for two apples, etc., is valid. Note the pattern: unequal exchange of the same kind is permitted.
The items listed are those not subject to legal measurement or weight.
2
Locate the effective cause ('illa)
The commentary explains that riba in ribawi goods requires both kind and capacity. Here, capacity is absent because these items are not legally measured (kayl) or weighed (wazn). The 'illa is the absence of a shari'ah-defined standard.
Capacity (al-qadr) is one of the two effective causes for riba.
3
Understand the condition of legal measurement
For a handful of wheat, it must be less than a sa' (the minimum legal measure). If half a sa' exists, selling less-than-half for half is invalid because measurement is present from both sides. The boundary is half a sa'.
The Hanafi rule: items below the shari'ah threshold are not considered measurable.
4
Apply to borderline cases and note the internal ikhtilaf
The passage discusses almond kernels vs walnuts: kernels are weighed, so the transaction is suspect. Later scholars (e.g., in Jam' al-Tafariq) hold that riba is established. There is also a narration from Muhammad (through al-Mu'alla) disapproving a date for two dates.
The mufta bihi is the permissive view, but caution is advised.

The author's statement: (And the sale of a handful for two handfuls, an apple for two apples, an egg for two eggs, a walnut for two walnuts, a date for two dates is valid) because they are neither measured nor weighed, so one of the two effective causes—capacity—is absent, so disparity is permitted, whether it is double or more, as long as it does not fall under measurement or weight. Then he said in it: If one sells an iron vessel for iron, if the vessel is sold by weight, equality in weight is considered, otherwise not. Likewise if the vessel is of brass or copper, selling it for [the same kind] is considered. The author says: Apparently they are two opposing statements, and Allah is the granter of success. So reflect. And his statement (And al-Mu'alla narrated...) on this, what he investigated is not contrary to the transmitted; rather it is a preference for this narration.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling that selling items in unequal quantities is valid if the items are not legally considered measured (makil) or weighed (mawzun). The matn lists examples: a handful for two handfuls, an apple for two apples, etc. The commentary explains that the effective cause ('illa) for riba in ribawi items is both kind and capacity; here capacity is absent because these items have no standard measure in shari'ah. For a handful of wheat or barley, it means less than a sa' (a known measure), so it is not subject to the rules of measurement. However, if half a sa' exists, then selling less than half a sa' for half a sa' would be invalid due to the presence of measurement. The commentary then cites Fath al-Qadir and Jam' al-Tafariq, where there is a difference of opinion: some say that riba is established even in such transactions, and it is necessary to prohibit them to protect people's wealth. The author then discusses guarantee: if a handful is usurped and destroyed, the guarantor must pay its value, not its like, because it is not from the category of measured goods. The passage also includes rulings on fish and iron vessels. Finally, the commentary addresses the issue of almond kernels and walnuts, noting that the correct opinion is that riba is established in that case because kernels are weighed. The author concludes by mentioning a narration from al-Mu'alla that Muhammad disliked selling a date for two dates, applying the principle that what is prohibited in large amounts is also prohibited in small amounts.

Key Terms
حفنة (hafnah): A handful; an amount less than a legal measure (sa').
حد الشرع (hadd al-shar'): Legal standard for measurement or weight (e.g., sa', ratal). Items below this have no standard.
تمرة (tamrah): A single date; considered individually not measured.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because wheat is not a ribawi item.
B) Because a handful is not a legally defined measure, so the condition of equality is waived.
C) Because the two amounts are equal in value.
D) Because it is a sale with immediate possession.

Key Takeaway
Unequal exchange of the same kind is permissible when both items lack a legal measure or weight; riba's capacity condition is absent.

Unequal Exchange of Non-Measured Items: The Handful Case
Commentary on permissibility of excess in items not measured by weight or volume

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on selling items not measured by weight or volume with excess, identify the effective cause (illa) of riba, and apply the condition that the handful must be less than half a sa'.

Core Idea
Excess in exchange of non-measured items is permissible because the illa of riba is absent, but the handful must be less than half a sa'.

The passage addresses a common transaction: exchanging one date for two, or a handful of wheat for two handfuls. The Hanafi school generally permits this because these items are not customarily sold by weight or volume. However, the commentator introduces a crucial nuance: a handful (hafna) is only considered non-measured if it is less than half a sa'—the smallest standard measure set by the Law. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this rule, examines the intra-Hanafi disagreement (Imam Muhammad disliked such exchanges), and clarifies the practical boundaries of the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The matn states that selling a handful for two handfuls, an apple for two apples, etc., is valid. Why? Because they are not measured by weight or volume.
The general rule applies to items that are not customarily sold by kail or wazn.
2
Understand the illa of riba
The Hanafi school holds that the effective cause (illa) for riba in items of the same genus is either measurement by volume (kayl) or by weight (wazn). When both are absent, excess is permitted.
This illa is derived from the hadith of riba and is the basis for the ruling.
3
Analyze the qualification for the handful
The handful is only non-measured if it is less than half a sa'. If it reaches or exceeds half a sa', it becomes measured and excess is prohibited. Why? Because the Law sets a minimum standard of measurement at half a sa'.
Half a sa' is the threshold; below that, the item is considered insignificant in terms of measurement.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad disliked selling a date for two dates, using the principle: 'Whatever is prohibited in large quantities, its small quantity is also prohibited.' This creates a tension between the general permissibility and this cautious view.
Muhammad's view is based on analogy (qiyas) from large to small, prioritizing caution.
5
Apply the ruling to other items
The commentary extends the rule to fish, iron utensils, and pulp (lubb) vs. walnuts, showing that the key factor is whether the item is customarily measured.
Custom ('urf) determines whether an item is considered measured or not.

And the sale of a handful for two handfuls, an apple for two apples, an egg for two eggs, a walnut for two walnuts, a date for two dates, and a fulus for two fulus in their specific forms is valid. He said: (And the sale of a handful for two handfuls, an apple for two apples, an egg for two eggs, a walnut for two walnuts, a date for two dates) because they were not measured by volume or weight, so one of the two causes (of riba), which is quantity, ceases to exist, thus excess is permissible, whether it be double or more, since it does not fall under volume or weight. Similarly, if the utensil is of copper or brass, he sells it for brass. End. He said: And apparently, these are two opposing statements, and Allah gives success. He said: (And the correct (view) is that riba is established) this is problematic regarding pulp for walnuts, because pulp is weighed unlike walnuts. Consider why it is not made like oil for olives. It may be said: what is meant by his statement (And the correct (view) is that riba is established) is with consideration to it, because its shell has value; and the author will mention that selling walnuts for their oil and dates for their pits is like oil for olives, i.e., it is permissible to sell them by consideration, so reflect. And refer to his statement: (And al-Mu'alla narrated) upon this, his research is not contrary to what is transmitted, but rather it is a preponderance for this narration.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn ruling regarding the permissibility of selling certain items that are not measured by weight or volume in unequal quantities in a spot transaction. The author explains that the effective cause (illa) for riba in these items is either weight (wazn) or volume (kayl). Since items like apples, eggs, walnuts, and dates are not customarily measured by weight or volume, the absence of this cause permits excess. However, the author introduces a nuance: the handful (hafna) of wheat or barley is considered only if it is less than half a sa', because the Law has set a minimum standard for measurement. If it equals or exceeds half a sa', the item is considered measured and excess is prohibited. The text also discusses the opinion of Imam Muhammad who disliked selling one date for two, analogizing that prohibition in large quantities implies prohibition in small. The guarantee (daman) of a handful is by its value, not by mithl, except for countable items like walnuts. The commentary then addresses further branches regarding fish, iron utensils, and the correct view on riba for pulp (lubb) and walnuts, noting that the pulp is weighed and thus prohibited in excess. The passage concludes with a note that the transmitted narration from al-Mu'alla supports the view of prohibition.

Key Terms
الحفنة (al-hafna): The amount that fills the palm of the hand; specifically less than half a sa' in the legal context.
العلة (al-illa): The effective cause (of riba) which is measurement by weight or volume.
التفاضل (al-tafadul): Excess in quantity of one item over another in an exchange of the same genus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the passage, when is selling a handful of wheat for two handfuls NOT permissible?
A) If the handful is less than half a sa'.

D) If the wheat is of different quality.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of exchanging non-measured items with excess hinges on the absence of the illa of riba (kail or wazn), with the important condition that a handful must be less than half a sa' to be considered non-measured.

Ruling on Selling Specified Fulus with Excess: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on permissibility of excess in specified fulus exchange

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on selling specified fulus with excess, explain the reasoning based on thamaniyya and istilah, and identify the four scenarios of specification.

Core Idea
Fulus can become commodities by agreement, permitting excess in exchange, but only when specified in the contract.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute over the sale of copper coins (fulus) with excess value. The foundational issue is whether fulus are inherently thaman (price) or can be treated as commodities by convention. The matn adopts the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, allowing excess when fulus are specified, while Muhammad forbids it. Understanding their differing premises is key to grasping the Hanafi approach to custom and the nature of currency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
What is the precise case under dispute? A person sells one specific fulus for two specific fulus. Is the excess permissible?
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say the sale is valid (sahih). Muhammad says it is invalid (batil) because it leads to riba.
3
Analyze the proof of each
Muhammad argues fulus in circulation are thaman, inherently non-specific, so excess implies riba. The two argue fulus are not thaman by creation; they became thaman by convention, which the parties can nullify, making them specific commodities.
4
Explore the responses to objections
The text addresses two objections: (1) copper is weighed, so nullifying thamaniyya should prohibit excess; answer: counting convention remains. (2) nullification requires universal consensus; answer: their agreement aligns with the original status (fulus as 'urud), so it is valid.
5
Apply to the four scenarios
Only when both fulus are specified and the parties nullify thamaniyya is the sale valid according to the two. In the other three scenarios (unspecified combinations), all agree it is invalid.

And the fulus for two fulus in their specific forms: meaning that the sale of a specified fulus for two specified fulus is valid according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Muhammad said: It is not permissible because circulating fulus are prices (athman) and they are not specific; for this reason fulus are not specified when exchanged with their own genus unlike the two precious metals (gold and silver), and the sale is not invalidated by their destruction. If they are not specified, it leads to riba or its possibility: the seller may take the two fulus or not, and return one for a debt and take the other without compensation, so it becomes as if they were not specified. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): they (fulus) are not prices by original creation; rather they became prices by convention (istilah). They have agreed to nullify the price-status, so it becomes null, even if they are prices for others due to their convention of price-status, since others have no authority over them, unlike the two precious metals because price-status in them is by original creation, so it is not nullified by convention. Therefore, when price-status is nullified, they become specific, so it does not lead to riba, unlike when they are unspecified, as we explained. It was objected: if price-status is nullified, then excess should not be permitted because copper is weighed, and it became counted only by convention of price-status, so if it is nullified, it returns to its original state. The answer: their convention of counting (as coins) is not nullified, and there is no necessary connection (between price-status and counting), for many counted items are not prices. It was also objected: their being prices after demonetization (kasād) is only by consensus of all, so similarly, nullification of price-status requires consensus. The answer: their convention to nullify its price-status is in accordance with the original principle (asl) because they are commodities, unlike their convention to make it price, which opposes the original and the opinion of all, so it is not valid. It is restricted by specification, because if the fulus were unspecified and the two fulus also unspecified, it is not permissible. There are four cases: when all are unspecified even if they take possession in the session (majlis) — as in al-Muhit; when the fulus is specified only; when both are unspecified; in these three, it is impermissible unanimously, but in the last two, if he takes possession of what was a debt in the session, it becomes permissible. The point of disagreement is the case of the book (matn), and the basis of the disagreement is that fulus do not become specific by specification according to Muhammad, but become specific according to the two, so the contract is void by its destruction. In al-Muhit, they are not specific and the contract is not void by their destruction. It is restricted by permission of excess, because credit (nasi'ah) is prohibited unanimously, since the genus alone prohibits it, as we mentioned. In al-Dhakhira: Muhammad mentioned this case under the chapter of exchange (sarf) and did not require hand-to-hand possession, indicating it is not a condition. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, he indicated that it is a condition. Some of our scholars did not authenticate what is in al-Jami' al-Saghir because hand-to-hand possession is only required in exchange (sarf) and this is not exchange. Some authenticated it because it has the ruling of commodities in one respect and the ruling of price in another, so excess is permitted due to the first, and the condition of hand-to-hand possession is stipulated due to the second, acting on both evidences as far as possible. Their intent is not specifically the sale of one fulus for two, but rather the statement of permissibility of excess; even if one sells a fulus for a hundred by specification, it is permissible according to the two. Appendix on rulings of fulus: In al-Muhit: If one sells fulus for fulus, or for dirhams, or for dinars... He said: (And the answer that their convention to nullify its price-status, etc.) from this it is understood that the convention of a party on something in accordance with the original is considered, even if it opposes the convention of all. He said: (Appendix) on rulings of fulus, he said.

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of copper coins (fulus) when specified in the contract. The matn states that selling a specific fulus for two specific fulus is valid (sahih), adopting the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad al-Shaybani opposes, arguing that fulus in circulation are thaman (prices) and as such they are inherently non-specific; allowing excess leads to riba or its suspicion. The two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) respond that fulus are not prices by original creation but by convention. The parties can nullify that convention, making fulus a commodity like any other, and thus excess is permitted. The text then addresses objections: (1) copper is weighed by nature, so nullifying thamaniyya should revert it to weighed status, prohibiting excess; answer: the counting convention remains, and not all counted items are prices. (2) nullification of thamaniyya after its establishment requires consensus; answer: their nullification is in line with the asl (fulus are 'urud), so it is valid. The disagreement is further broken down into four scenarios based on specification, with only one case (both specified) being permissible according to the two. The text also discusses whether hand-to-hand possession (taqabud) is required, with differences among later Hanafi scholars. The appendix confirms that the convention of some people to treat fulus as commodities is valid even if others still treat them as prices. The overall ruling: permissibility of excess in specified fulus according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, which is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
الفلس (al-fals): Copper coin used as currency; in this context, specifically a coin that can be treated as a commodity by convention.
الثمنية (al-thamaniyya): The quality or status of being a price (thaman), i.e., a medium of exchange.
الاصطلاح (al-istilah): Convention or agreement among parties regarding the status of fulus as price or commodity.
التعيين (al-ta'ayyun): Specification (making a specific item pinpointed in the contract).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, what condition makes a sale of one fulus for two fulus valid?
A) The fulus are unspecified in the contract.
B) The fulus are specified and the parties agree to nullify thamaniyya.
C) The transaction is on credit (nasi'ah).
D) The fulus are in different denominations.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of excess in specified fulus exchange hinges on the parties' ability to nullify the coin's price-status by agreement, a principle unique to non-precious metal currencies in the Hanafi school.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Specified Fils Exchange
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of selling specified fulus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf versus Imam Muhammad on selling a specific fils for two specific fils and explain the proof for each.

Core Idea
Fulus are thaman by convention, not creation — the parties can annul that convention and treat them as specified commodities.

In the chapter of riba, a key intra-Hanafi dispute arises: can a specific copper coin (fils) be sold for two specific copper coins of the same type? The two imams, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, allow it, while Imam Muhammad prohibits it. The difference hinges on the nature of fulus as thaman (price) and whether they can be specified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two positions
The act is selling one specified fils for two specified fils. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule it valid (sahih); Muhammad rules it invalid (batil).
Remember the key figures within the Hanafi school.
2
Understand Muhammad's proof
Muhammad argues that fulus are thaman by prevalent usage (raulaj) and thus cannot be specified. Selling one for two leads to riba because of disparity in number and potential for one coin to be taken without compensation.
He relies on the maxim that thaman cannot be specified when exchanged against its own kind.
3
Understand the two's proof
The two argue that fulus are thaman only by convention (istilah), not by inherent creation. The parties can agree to annul that convention, making the coins specified commodities ('ayan). Once specified, they are no longer thaman, so disparity is allowed.
They distinguish fulus from gold and silver, which are thaman by original creation.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to the two, the sale is valid and binding; according to Muhammad, it is void (batil) and must be reversed.
The mufta bihi position is that of the two.

Book of sale, chapter of riba. And [the ruling on] a fils for two fils with specification: meaning the sale of a specific fils for two specific fils is valid according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Muhammad said: it is not permissible because prevalent fils are prices (thaman) and they are not specific, therefore fils are not specified when exchanged against their own kind, unlike the two precious metals. And the sale is not invalidated by their destruction, so if they are not specified it leads to riba or its possibility: either the seller of the fils takes the two fils or not, so he returns one as payment of debt and takes the other without compensation, so it becomes as if they were without specification. According to the two: they are not prices by creation, rather they were prices by convention, and they (the two parties) have agreed to annul the price-ness, so it becomes void even if they are prices in the view of others because the convention of others on their price-ness remains, since others have no authority over them, unlike the two precious metals because price-ness in them is by original creation so it is not annulled by convention. So when price-ness is annulled they become specified, thus it does not lead to riba, unlike the case when they are unspecified, because it leads to riba as we explained. An objection: if price-ness is annulled then disparity should not be allowed because copper is weighed, and it only became counted by the convention of price-ness; when it is annulled it returns to its origin. Answer: their convention of counting is not annulled and there is no necessary connection; many counted things are not prices. Also objected: its being price after kasad cannot be except by the convention of all, so likewise the annulment of price-ness. Answer: their convention of annulling its price-ness is in accordance with the origin because it is a commodity, unlike their convention of making it price after that, which opposes the origin and the view of all, so it is not valid. And it is qualified by specification because if the fils was unspecified and the two fils likewise, it is not permissible. Its forms are four: when all are unspecified even if they hand over in the session, as in al-Muhit; when only the fils is specified; when only the two fils are unspecified; in these three it is not permissible by agreement, but in the last two forms if he takes possession of what was a debt in the session it is permissible, as in al-Muhit. The locus of disagreement is the issue of the book. The basis of the disagreement is that according to Muhammad fils are not specified by specification, but according to the two they are specified, so the contract is invalidated by their destruction, as in Fath al-Qadir. In al-Muhit: they are not specified and the contract is not annulled by their destruction. It is qualified by permissibility of disparity because nasa (delay) is forbidden by agreement because the single genus prohibits it as we have presented. In al-Dhakhira: Muhammad mentioned this issue in the original [chapter] of sarf and did not stipulate mutual handover, so this indicates that it is not a condition. In al-Jami' al-Saghir there is what indicates that it is a condition. Some of our mashayikh did not authenticate what is in al-Jami' al-Saghir because mutual handover with specifieness is only stipulated in sarf and this is not sarf. Some authenticated it because it has the ruling of commodities from one aspect and the ruling of price from another aspect, so disparity is permitted for the first and stipulation of handover for the second, acting on both evidences as much as possible. End. And they did not mean specifically the sale of a fils for two fils, but rather the statement of permissibility of disparity, so even if one sells a fils for a hundred with specification it is permissible according to the two.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of selling a specific copper coin (fils) for two specific copper coins. The core issue is whether copper coins (fulus) are considered as thaman (price) or as a commodity ('urud). Imam Muhammad holds that they are thaman by prevalent usage, hence they are not specified (ghayr mu'ayyan) when exchanged against their own kind, leading to potential riba. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf argue that fulus are thaman only by convention, and the two parties have agreed to annul that convention, making them specified objects ('ayan). The passage then addresses objections and further qualifies the ruling: the dispute only applies when the coins are specified; in other cases there is agreement. It also discusses whether mutual handover (taqabud) is required, with some Hanafi scholars preferring Muhammad's original view from al-Dhakhira that it is not a condition, while others require it due to the coins' dual nature. The mufta bihi position according to the author is that specified fulus can be exchanged with disparity, and taqabud is not required in such sales (as opposed to sarf).

Key Terms
فلس (fils): A copper coin used as currency in the classical Islamic world; plural: fulus.
ثمنية (thamaniyya): The quality of being a price (thaman) or medium of exchange.
التعيين (al-ta'yin): Specification, i.e., designating a particular coin as the object of sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, why is selling a specific fil for two specific fils valid?
A) Because fulus are gold and silver.
B) Because fulus are thaman by creation and thus can be specified.
C) Because fulus are thaman by convention, which the parties can annul, making them specified commodities.
D) Because the sale involves a specified fil, so it is a barter of equal weight.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi allows the exchange of specified fulus with disparity because their thamaniyya is conventional and can be annulled.

Objections and Responses: Strengthening the Two's Argument
Analysis of objections and responses to the two's ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two objections raised against Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's view and state the responses provided in the text.

Core Idea
Copper's original nature is weighed, but counting convention overrides; annulment of thamaniyya is valid because it returns to the original commodity status.

After presenting the positions, the passage addresses two objections that skeptics might raise against the two's ruling. These objections challenge the logical consistency of allowing disparity when thamaniyya is annulled. The responses clarify the distinction between counting convention and price-ness, and emphasize that annulling a conventional ruling is easier than establishing one against the original nature.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first objection
If price-ness is annulled, copper is by nature weighed (mawzun), not counted. Disparity in weighed items is not allowed in ribawi transactions, so how can disparity be permitted?
The objection assumes that annulling thamaniyya returns copper to its original classification as a weighed commodity.
2
Understand the response to the first objection
The counting convention (al-istilah 'ala al-'add) is independent of thamaniyya. Even if thamaniyya is annulled, the convention of counting remains. There is no necessary correlation between being thaman and being counted; many counted items are not prices.
This response decouples the two conventions.
3
Identify the second objection
If thamaniyya requires general convention to be established, its annulment should also require general convention. The two parties alone cannot annul what society has established.
The objection argues that thamaniyya is a social fact, not a private agreement.
4
Understand the response to the second objection
The original state of copper is that of a commodity ('urd). Making it thaman is a departure from the original. Annulling that departure returns to the original, which is permissible by the parties because the original is the default. In contrast, establishing thamaniyya against the original requires broader consensus.
This response invokes the legal principle that returning to the original (al-'awd ila al-asl) is easier than departing from it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب الربا
والفلس بالفلسين بأعيانهما أي وصح بيع الفلس المعين بفلسين معينين عندهما. وقال محمد: لا يجوز لأن الفلوس الرائجة أثمان وهو لا يتعين ولذا لا تتعين الفلوس إذا قوبلت بخلاف جنسها كالنقدين، ولا يفسد البيع بهلاكها فإذا لم تتعين يؤدي إلى الربا أو يحتمله بأن يأخذ بائع الفلس الفلسين أو لا فيرد أحدهما قضاء لدينه ويأخذ الآخر بلا عوض فصار كما لو كان بغير أعيانهما. ولهما أنها ليست أثماناً خلقة وإنما كانت ثمناً بالاصطلاح وقد اصطلحا على إبطال الثمنية فتبطل وإن كانت ثمناً عند غيرهما لبقاء اصطلاحهم على ثمنيتها إذ لا ولاية للغير عليهما بخلاف النقدين لأن الثمنية فيهما بأصل الخلقة فلا تبطل بالاصطلاح، فإذا بطلت الثمنية تعينت فلا يؤدي إلى الربا بخلاف ما إذا كانت غير معينة فإنه يؤدي إلى الربا على ما بيناه. وأورد أن الثمنية إذا بطلت وجب أن لا يجوز التفاضل لأن النحاس موزون وإنما صار معدوداً بالاصطلاح على الثمنية، فإذا بطلت عاد إلى أصله وأجيب بأن اصطلاحهما على العد لم يبطل ولا يلازمه فكم من معدود لا يكون ثمناً، وأورد أيضاً أن كونها ثمناً بعد الكساد لا يكون إلا باصطلاح الكل فكذا بطلان الثمنية وأجيب بأن اصطلاحهما على بطلان ثمنيتها موافق للأصل لكونها عروضاً بخلاف اصطلاحهما على كونها ثمناً بعد مخالف للأصل ولرأي الجميع فلم يصح، وقيد بالتعيين لأن الفلس لو كان بغير عينه والفلسان كذلك لم يجز وصورها أربع ما إذا كان الكل غير معين وإن تقابضا في المجلس؛ كذا في المحيط . وما إذا كان الفلس معيناً فقط، وما إذا كانا غير معينين فقط ففي هذه الثلاثة لا يجوز اتفاقاً لكن في الصورتين الأخيرتين لو قبض ما كان ديناً في المجلس جاز؛ كذا في المحيط . ومحل الخلاف مسألة الكتاب وأصل الخلاف مبني على أن الفلس لا يتعين بالتعيين عند محمد، ويتعين عندهما فيبطل العقد بهلاكه ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفي المحيط أنها لا تتعين ولا ينفسخ العقد بهلاكها. قيد بحل التفاضل لأن النساء حرام اتفاقاً لأن الجنس بانفراده يحرمه كما قدمناه. وفي الذخيرة ذكر محمد هذه المسألة في صرف الأصل ولم يشترط التقابض فهذا دليل على أنه ليس بشرط، وذكر في الجامع الصغير ما يدل على أنه شرط ومن مشايخنا من لم يصحح ما في الجامع الصغير لأن التقابض مع العينية إنما يشترط في الصرف وليس به، ومنهم من صححه لأن لها حكم العروض من وجه وحكم الثمن من وجه فجاز التفاضل للأول واشتراط التقابض للثاني عملاً بالدليلين بقدر الإمكان .اهـ. وليس مرادهم خصوص بيع الفلس بالفلسين بل بيان حل التفاضل حتى لو باع فلساً بمائة على التعيين جاز عندهما .
Book of sale, chapter of riba. And [the ruling on] a fils for two fils with specification: meaning the sale of a specific fils for two specific fils is valid according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Muhammad said: it is not permissible because prevalent fils are prices (thaman) and they are not specific, therefore fils are not specified when exchanged against their own kind, unlike the two precious metals. And the sale is not invalidated by their destruction, so if they are not specified it leads to riba or its possibility: either the seller of the fils takes the two fils or not, so he returns one as payment of debt and takes the other without compensation, so it becomes as if they were without specification. According to the two: they are not prices by creation, rather they were prices by convention, and they (the two parties) have agreed to annul the price-ness, so it becomes void even if they are prices in the view of others because the convention of others on their price-ness remains, since others have no authority over them, unlike the two precious metals because price-ness in them is by original creation so it is not annulled by convention. So when price-ness is annulled they become specified, thus it does not lead to riba, unlike the case when they are unspecified, because it leads to riba as we explained. An objection: if price-ness is annulled then disparity should not be allowed because copper is weighed, and it only became counted by the convention of price-ness; when it is annulled it returns to its origin. Answer: their convention of counting is not annulled and there is no necessary connection; many counted things are not prices. Also objected: its being price after kasad cannot be except by the convention of all, so likewise the annulment of price-ness. Answer: their convention of annulling its price-ness is in accordance with the origin because it is a commodity, unlike their convention of making it price after that, which opposes the origin and the view of all, so it is not valid. And it is qualified by specification because if the fils was unspecified and the two fils likewise, it is not permissible. Its forms are four: when all are unspecified even if they hand over in the session, as in al-Muhit; when only the fils is specified; when only the two fils are unspecified; in these three it is not permissible by agreement, but in the last two forms if he takes possession of what was a debt in the session it is permissible, as in al-Muhit. The locus of disagreement is the issue of the book. The basis of the disagreement is that according to Muhammad fils are not specified by specification, but according to the two they are specified, so the contract is invalidated by their destruction, as in Fath al-Qadir. In al-Muhit: they are not specified and the contract is not annulled by their destruction. It is qualified by permissibility of disparity because nasa (delay) is forbidden by agreement because the single genus prohibits it as we have presented. In al-Dhakhira: Muhammad mentioned this issue in the original [chapter] of sarf and did not stipulate mutual handover, so this indicates that it is not a condition. In al-Jami' al-Saghir there is what indicates that it is a condition. Some of our mashayikh did not authenticate what is in al-Jami' al-Saghir because mutual handover with specifieness is only stipulated in sarf and this is not sarf. Some authenticated it because it has the ruling of commodities from one aspect and the ruling of price from another aspect, so disparity is permitted for the first and stipulation of handover for the second, acting on both evidences as much as possible. End. And they did not mean specifically the sale of a fils for two fils, but rather the statement of permissibility of disparity, so even if one sells a fils for a hundred with specification it is permissible according to the two.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of selling a specific copper coin (fils) for two specific copper coins. The core issue is whether copper coins (fulus) are considered as thaman (price) or as a commodity ('urud). Imam Muhammad holds that they are thaman by prevalent usage, hence they are not specified (ghayr mu'ayyan) when exchanged against their own kind, leading to potential riba. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf argue that fulus are thaman only by convention, and the two parties have agreed to annul that convention, making them specified objects ('ayan). The passage then addresses objections and further qualifies the ruling: the dispute only applies when the coins are specified; in other cases there is agreement. It also discusses whether mutual handover (taqabud) is required, with some Hanafi scholars preferring Muhammad's original view from al-Dhakhira that it is not a condition, while others require it due to the coins' dual nature. The mufta bihi position according to the author is that specified fulus can be exchanged with disparity, and taqabud is not required in such sales (as opposed to sarf).

Key Terms
عد ('add): Counting; the convention of treating an item as counted rather than weighed.
أصل (asl): Original nature or default ruling.
عروض ('urud): Commodities (non-monetary goods).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the text respond to the objection that annulling thamaniyya should require general consensus?
A) It agrees and revokes the ruling.
B) It argues that the parties' agreement suffices because returning to the original is easier than departing.
C) It says that general consensus is not needed because fulus are not important.
D) It claims that the objection is irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
The two's ruling is defended by distinguishing conventions and applying the principle that returning to the original is easier than departing from it.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

8 min
The Four Forms of Fils Exchange and the Taqabud Ikhtilaf
Analysis of the four cases and the taqabud ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four forms of fils exchange described in the text and state the ruling for each, and explain the internal ikhtilaf on whether mutual handover (taqabud) is required.

Core Idea
The dispute only applies when both fils are specified; in all other combinations, the sale is invalid by agreement.

After establishing the main dispute, the passage delineates four possible scenarios for the sale of one fils for two fils, depending on which coins are specified. In three of these scenarios, there is agreement among the Hanafi imams that the sale is invalid. The fourth scenario is precisely the case of the dispute. The passage then adds a further layer of ikhtilaf regarding whether mutual handover (taqabud) is a condition in such sales, a debate that reflects the dual nature of fulus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four forms
The text lists four possibilities: (1) all coins unspecified; (2) only the single fils specified; (3) only the two fils unspecified; (4) both fils specified (the locus of dispute).
Memorize these forms as they are key to applying the correct ruling.
2
Note the agreed-upon rulings
In forms (1), (2), and (3), the sale is invalid (la yajuz) by agreement among the three imams. However, in forms (2) and (3), if the debt (dīn) is paid in the session (majlis), it becomes permissible.
This exception shows that specification can be cured by immediate handover in some cases.
3
Understand the taqabud ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad's original position in al-Dhakhira did not require taqabud, but in al-Jami' al-Saghir there is an indication that it is required. Some later scholars prefer the non-requirement, while others require it due to the dual nature of fulus (part commodity, part price).
This ikhtilaf affects whether the sale can be concluded without immediate exchange.
4
Apply the broader principle
The author notes that the discussion is not limited to the specific case but is a general statement about permissibility of disparity in specified fulus. Even a sale of one fils for a hundred specified fils is permissible according to the two.
The principle is that specification allows disparity, not that the ratio must be exactly 1:2.

The Effect of Kasad (Obsolescence) on Fulus Transactions
Rulings from al-Muhit on kasad of fulus in sale and loan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on when fulus become obsolete before receipt in a sale or loan, and explain the intra-madhhab difference between Abu Hanifa and the two companions.

Core Idea
Kasad of fulus is treated as destruction — the sale may be annulled by istihsan over qiyas.

This lesson focuses on a key area of Hanafi muamalat: the effect of kasad (obsolescence) on fulus (copper coins). The passage from al-Muhit presents three scenarios: fulus as goods, fulus as price, and fulus as loan. In each, kasad triggers a legal consequence that differs between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples. Understanding these rulings requires appreciating the principle that kasad is analogous to destruction (halak), a point where istihsan overrides qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage discusses (a) fulus bought as goods become kasid before receipt, (b) fulus that are the price become kasid before receipt, and (c) fulus given as a loan become kasid.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
For (a), by qiyas the sale is not void and the buyer has an option; by istihsan it is void. For (b), Abu Hanifa says void, the two say not void but value must be paid. For (c), Abu Hanifa says repay like amount, the two say repay value.
Memorize the ruling for each.
3
Understand the reasoning
Kasad is treated as destruction (halak) because the purpose of fulus is circulation. Istihsan overrides qiyas due to this special nature.
Key principle: kasad equals halak.
4
Compare the positions
Abu Hanifa consistently takes a stricter view: kasad voids the contract. The two allow continuation with compensation in value.
This is a classic intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Source Text

واللحم بالحيوان والكرباس بالقطن وكذا بالغزل كيفما كان والرطب بالرطب أو بالتمر متماثلاً، وعند محمد يوم الكساد، فنقد أحدهما دون الآخر جاز، وإن افترقا لا عن قبض أحدهما جاز، ولو اشترى مائة فلس بدرهم فقبض الدرهم ولم يقبض الفلوس حتى كسدت لم يبطل البيع قياساً ويتخير المشتري إن شاء قبضها كاسدة وإن شاء فسخ البيع، ويبطل البيع استحساناً لأن كسادها بمنزلة الهلاك لأن المقصود منها الرواج فهو لها كالحياة. ولو قبض منها خمسين ثم كسدت بطل البيع في النصف ورد نصف درهم اعتباراً للبعض بالكل، ولو رخصت لم يبطل ولا خيار للمشتري . ولو كسدت الفلوس الثمن قبل قبضها بطل البيع عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما لا يفسد ويجب قيمتها. ولو كسدت أفلس القرض فعليه مثلها عنده وعندهما قيمتها من الدراهم، وكذا لو غصب واستهلك . ثم عند أبي يوسف تعتبر القيمة القبض، يوم والأصح عند الإمام أن عليه قيمتها يوم الانقطاع من الذهب والفضة. ولو اشترى فلوساً وتقابضا على أن كل واحد منهما بالخيار وتفرقا على ذلك فسد البيع لأن الخيار يمنع صحة القبض، ولو كان أحدهما بالخيار فالبيع جائز عندهما لأن الخيار لا يمنع ثبوت الملك له في المبيع فوجد القبض المستحق في أحدهما، وعلى قول أبي حنيفة لا يجوز لأن الخيار يؤثر في الجانبين فيمنع صحة القبض. وإن باع فلساً بعينه بفلسين بأعيانهما بشرط الخيار يجوز اهـ. ما في المحيط من باب بيع الفلوس واستقراضها
And meat for animal, and cotton cloth for cotton, and likewise for yarn in any case, and fresh dates for fresh dates or for dried dates equal. And according to Muhammad on the day of kasad?… then if one pays without the other it is permissible, and if they separate without one having received it is permissible. And if one buys a hundred fils for a dirham and receives the dirham but does not receive the fils until they become kasid (fall out of use), the sale is not annulled by qiyas, and the buyer has the option: if he wishes he may take them as kasid, if he wishes he may rescind the sale. And it is annulled by istihsan because its becoming kasid is like destruction, since the purpose of them is circulation, which is like life for them. And if he receives fifty of them and then they become kasid, the sale is annulled for half and he returns half a dirham, treating the part as the whole. And if they become cheap (rakhusa), it is not annulled and there is no option for the buyer. And if the fulus which are the price become kasid before receipt, the sale is annulled according to Abu Hanifa, but according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is not annulled and their value must be paid. And if fulus given as a loan become kasid, he must pay the like according to him (Abu Hanifa), but according to the two their value in dirhams. Likewise in case of usurpation and consumption. Then according to Abu Yusuf the value is considered on the day of receipt, but the more correct according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa) is that he must pay their value on the day of cessation (from circulation) in gold and silver. And if one buys fulus and they hand over on condition that each has the option and they separate on that basis, the sale is void because the option prevents valid receipt. And if only one has the option, the sale is valid according to the two because the option does not prevent ownership in the sold item, so the required receipt exists in the one. According to Abu Hanifa, it is not permissible because the option affects both sides and prevents valid receipt. And if one sells a specific fil for two specific fils with a condition of option, it is permissible. End. That which is in al-Muhit from the chapter of buying and selling fulus and giving them as loans.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of rulings from al-Muhit regarding fulus (copper coins). It covers several scenarios: selling meat for animal (permissible despite genus difference), selling cloth for cotton, etc. Then it details cases of kasad (depreciation/withdrawal from circulation) of fulus. The key ruling: if the price (fulus) becomes kasid before receipt, Abu Hanifa says the sale is annulled, while the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it remains valid but the value must be paid. For a loan of fulus that becomes kasid, Abu Hanifa requires repayment of the same number of fils, while the two require the value in dirhams. The passage also discusses the effect of option (khiyar) on the validity of the sale: if both parties have option and separate, the sale is void; if only one has option, it is valid according to the two. The final line reminds that selling a specific fil for two specific fils with option is permissible (as per earlier dispute). This text is a set of practical rulings for the student to memorize, based on the authoritative manual al-Muhit.

Key Terms
كساد (kasad): The state where fulus (copper coins) become obsolete or no longer circulate as currency.
رخص (rakhusa): The state where fulus become cheaper in value but still circulate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when fulus given as a loan become kasid, according to Abu Hanifa?
A) The borrower must repay the value in dirhams.
B) The borrower must repay the same number of fils.
C) The loan is forgiven.
D) The borrower must repay in gold or silver.

Key Takeaway
Kasad of fulus is treated as destruction, leading to annulment of sale (istihsan) or repayment in kind (Abu Hanifa), but the two companions prefer value compensation.

The Effect of Khiyar (Option) on Fulus Sales
Rulings from al-Muhit on khiyar in fulus sales.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the validity of a fulus sale when one or both parties have option, and identify when option invalidates receipt.

Core Idea
In a fulus sale, option prevents valid receipt only when both parties have the right to cancel.

This lesson focuses on another set of rulings from the same passage in al-Muhit: the effect of khiyar (option) on the sale of fulus. The key distinction is whether the option is granted to both parties or only one. This determines if the sale is valid or void, based on whether the option impedes the required receipt (qabd) of the goods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two khiyar scenarios
The passage discusses (a) both parties have option, (b) only one party has option.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
For (a): the sale is void. For (b): the sale is valid according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) but invalid according to Abu Hanifa.
Memorize the rulings.
3
Understand the reasoning
Option prevents valid receipt (qabd) because it suspends ownership. When both have option, neither side fully owns, so receipt is defective. When only one has option, ownership transfers to the other party, so receipt is valid for that side.
The principle: khiyar affects qabd only when it is bilateral.
4
Compare the positions
Abu Hanifa holds that even unilateral option prevents receipt because the option affects both sides indirectly. The two consider the option only affects the party who holds it.
Another intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Selling Meat for a Live Animal: The Weighed vs. Unweighed Distinction
Expansion of rulings on meat-for-animal and analogous exchanges

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad on selling meat for a live animal of the same species, and explain the reasoning based on the weighed/unweighed distinction.

Core Idea
Meat (weighed) and live animal (unweighed) are different categories—sale valid per majority, but Muhammad requires excess meat for offal.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, the commentator expands on the ruling for exchanging meat for a live animal. While the base text from al-Muhit might have stated a simple ruling, the commentary reveals a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute. Understanding the reasoning—whether the items are weighed or not—is key to grasping the school's approach to riba in barter exchanges.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Base Ruling
The base text (likely from al-Muhit) says 'meat for animal' is valid. Note who holds this: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad disagrees under certain conditions.
The passage states 'and meat for animal' meaning the sale is valid.
2
Contrast the Two Positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit it without condition because meat is weighed (mawzun) and a live animal is not weighed, so they are different genera. Muhammad prohibits it if the meat is of the same species, unless the meat sold exceeds the meat on the animal to account for offal (saqt).
Muhammad's concern is riba due to genus similarity with a difference in quantity.
3
Analyse the Reasoning of the Two
They analogize to selling a sword for iron: a sword (unweighed) for iron (weighed) is valid. Similarly, live animal (unweighed) for meat (weighed) is valid.
This is qiyas based on the illah of different measurement categories.
4
Understand the Offal (Saqt) Exception
Muhammad requires the meat sold to be more than the meat on the animal so that the excess compensates for the offal. If equal or less, riba might occur because the meat on the animal is weighed when alive? Actually, Muhammad considers the animal as a whole to be potentially same genus.
The passage defines saqt (skin, stomach, etc.) as non-meat, so it's not riba-generating.
5
Apply the Principle to Other Scenarios
The commentator extends the ruling: slaughtered sheep for live sheep is valid by all; milk in udder for milk of same kind is subject to same dispute; cotton cloth for cotton is valid because different genera.
Also notes a correction by al-Ramli about separation without receipt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (واللحم بالحيوان) أي وصح بيع اللحم بالحيوان عند أبي حنيفة وعند أبي يوسف وقال محمد: لا يجوز إذا كان من جنسه إلا إذا كان اللحم المفرز أكثر من اللحم الذي في الحيوان ليكون اللحم بمقابلة ما فيه والباقي من اللحم بمقابله السقط - وهو بفتحتين - ما لا ينطلق عليه اسم اللحم كالجلد والكرش والأمعاء والطحال وصار كالحل - وهو بالمهملة - دهن السمسم ولهما أنه باع الموزون بما ليس بموزون فصار كبيع السيف بالحديد لأن الحيوان لا يوزن عادة ولا يمكن معرفة ثقله بالوزن بخلاف تلك المسألة لأن الوزن في الحل يعرف قدر الدهن إذا ميز. وذكر الشارح: وإنما لا أحدهما بالآخر نسيئة لأن المتأخر منهما لا يمكن ضبطه لا لأنها جنس واحد ألا ترى بيع أنه لا يجوز ذلك إذا بيع بغيره من خلاف الجنس أيضاً .اهـ. ولو باع شاة مذبوحة بشاة حية يجوز عند الكل وعلى هذا شاتان مذبوحتان غير مسلوختين بشاة مذبوحة لم تسلخ يجوز . وفي شرح الطحاوي : لو كانت الشاة مذبوحة غير مسلوخة فاشتراها بلحم الشاة فالجواب في قولهم جميعاً كما قال محمد، وأراد بغير المسلوخة غير المفصولة عن السقط. وفي الحاوي: لو باع شاة في ضرعها لبن بجنس لبنها فهو على الاختلاف الذي في اللحم . قوله : (والكرباس بالقطن وكذا بالغزل كيفما كان أي صح لاختلافهما جنساً لأن الثوب لا ينقض ليعود غزلاً يجوز . الرملي : وسيأتي مزيد بحث في أحكام الفلوس من كتاب الصرف. قوله : (وإن افترقا لا عن قبض أحدهما جاز) قال الرملي: صوابه لا يجوز». قوله : (وفي الحاوي لو باع شاة الخ) قال في النهر :
His saying: (and meat for animal) meaning the sale of meat for an animal is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad said: it is not permissible if it is of the same genus, except if the separated meat is more than the meat in the animal so that the meat is in exchange for what is in it, and the rest of the meat is in exchange for the offal (saqt) – with two fathas – that which the name 'meat' does not apply to, like skin, stomach, intestines, spleen, and it is like al-hall – with a muhmala – sesame oil. According to the two, he sold a weighed item for a non-weighed item, so it is like selling a sword for iron, because an animal is not usually weighed and its weight cannot be known by weighing, unlike that issue because the weight of al-hall is known as the amount of oil when distinguished. And the commentator mentioned: they are not (sold) one for the other on credit because the later one cannot be fixed, not because they are a single genus – do you not see that it is not permissible when sold for something else of a different genus also. End. And if one sells a slaughtered sheep for a live sheep, it is permissible by all. Likewise two slaughtered unsold sheep for a slaughtered unsold sheep is permissible. In Sharh al-Tahawi: if the sheep was slaughtered but not skinned, and he buys it for the meat of a sheep, the answer in all their statements is as Muhammad said. He meant by 'not skinned' not separated from the offal. In al-Hawi: if one sells a sheep with milk in its udder for milk of its own kind, it is subject to the disagreement about meat. His saying: (and cotton cloth for cotton, and likewise for yarn in any case) meaning it is valid because they are different in genus, because the garment is not unraveled to return to yarn; it is permissible. Al-Ramli: more research on rulings of fulus will come in the book of sarf. His saying: (and if they separate without one having received, it is permissible) al-Ramli said: the correct is 'not permissible.' His saying: (and in al-Hawi: if one sells a sheep…) he said in al-Nahr…
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is the commentator's expansion (sharh) on the base text from al-Muhit. It focuses first on the ruling of selling meat for an animal (live). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit it, while Muhammad prohibits it if the meat is of the same genus (except when the meat sold is more than the meat on the animal, so that the excess compensates for the offal). The reasoning is that meat is a weighed commodity while an animal is not weighed, so they are different categories and thus not subject to riba. The commentator then discusses various sub-scenarios: slaughtered sheep for live sheep (permissible by all), and milk in the udder for milk (subject to same disagreement). He also comments on cotton cloth for cotton: they are different genera and thus valid. Finally, notes a correction by al-Ramli regarding separation without receipt. The passage provides critical refinement of the base text, clarifying the legal reasoning and reconciling apparent contradictions.

Key Terms
سقط (saqt): Offal or non-meat parts of an animal (skin, stomach, intestines, spleen).
حل (hall): Sesame oil (or other expressed oil). Used as an analogy for a non-weighed item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit selling meat for a live animal of the same species?
A) Because both are the same genus and thus subject to riba.
B) Because meat is weighed and an animal is not, making them different categories.
C) Because the animal is considered as offal.
D) Because the sale is on credit.

Key Takeaway
The sale of meat for a live animal is valid in the Hanafi school because meat (weighed) and the animal (unweighed) are different categories, thus no riba.

The Core Ruling on Kasad: Qiyas vs Istihsan
Intra-Hanafi dispute: Qiyas vs Istihsan on kasad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the qiyas and istihsan rulings on kasad of coins in a sale and apply the istihsan ruling to determine the sale's validity.

Core Idea
Kasad (worthlessness) is treated as destruction; by istihsan the sale is void, by qiyas it remains valid.

This lesson examines the Hanafi treatment of coins that become worthless (kasad) after a sale contract but before delivery. The passage from al-Muhit presents both the analogical ruling (qiyas) and the juristic preference (istihsan). Understanding this distinction is crucial because the school relies on istihsan in practice, considering the essential function of coins as currency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the act
Consider the sale: buyer purchases 100 copper fils for 1 dirham, takes possession of the dirham but not the fils, then the fils become worthless before delivery. The act is the sale contract, and we must determine its validity.
The fils are the subject matter (mabi'), the dirham is the price (thaman).
2
Apply qiyas
By qiyas (analogy), since the physical coins still exist, the sale remains valid. The buyer may take the worthless coins or rescind the sale, but the contract is not automatically void.
The qiyas is based on the principle that physical existence is sufficient for a valid sale.
3
Apply istihsan
By istihsan (juristic preference), the sale is invalid (batil) because kasad is analogous to destruction (halak). The essential benefit of coins is their circulation (rawaj); without it, they are like dead objects. Therefore, the sale is void ab initio.
This istihsan overrides the qiyas and is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.
4
Examine partial kasad
If the buyer had taken possession of some fils (e.g., 50) and the rest become worthless, the sale is void only for the undelivered portion. The price is adjusted proportionally.
The ruling treats part of the subject matter as the whole; the buyer recovers half the price.
5
Distinguish mere price drop (rukhs)
A mere fall in market value (rukhs) does not invalidate the sale. The buyer has no option to rescind because the coins retain their function as currency.
Only complete worthlessness (kasad) triggers the istihsan ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعند محمد يوم الكساد، فنقد أحدهما دون الآخر جاز، وإن افترقا لا عن قبض أحدهما جاز، ولو اشترى مائة فلس بدرهم فقبض الدرهم ولم يقبض الفلوس حتى كسدت لم يبطل البيع قياساً ويتخير المشتري إن شاء قبضها كاسدة وإن شاء فسخ البيع، ويبطل البيع استحساناً لأن كسادها بمنزلة الهلاك لأن المقصود منها الرواج فهو لها كالحياة. ولو قبض منها خمسين ثم كسدت بطل البيع في النصف ورد نصف درهم اعتباراً للبعض بالكل، ولو رخصت لم يبطل ولا خيار للمشتري . ولو كسدت الفلوس الثمن قبل قبضها بطل البيع عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما لا يفسد ويجب قيمتها. ولو كسدت أفلس القرض فعليه مثلها عنده وعندهما قيمتها من الدراهم، وكذا لو غصب واستهلك . ثم عند أبي يوسف تعتبر القيمة القبض، يوم والأصح عند الإمام أن عليه قيمتها يوم الانقطاع من الذهب والفضة. ولو اشترى فلوساً وتقابضا على أن كل واحد منهما بالخيار وتفرقا على ذلك فسد البيع لأن الخيار يمنع صحة القبض، ولو كان أحدهما بالخيار فالبيع جائز عندهما لأن الخيار لا يمنع ثبوت الملك له في المبيع فوجد القبض المستحق في أحدهما، وعلى قول أبي حنيفة لا يجوز لأن الخيار يؤثر في الجانبين فيمنع صحة القبض. وإن باع فلساً بعينه بفلسين بأعيانهما بشرط الخيار يجوز اهـ. ما في المحيط من باب بيع الفلوس واستقراضها
According to Muhammad, on the day of depreciation, if one pays (cash) without the other, it is permissible; if they separate without one taking possession, it is permissible. If someone buys one hundred fils for a dirham, takes possession of the dirham but not the fils until they become worthless, the sale is not invalidated by qiyas, and the buyer has a choice: if he wishes, he may take possession of them as worthless; if he wishes, he may rescind the sale. By istihsan, the sale is invalidated because their worthlessness is like destruction, because the purpose of them is circulation, which is like life for them. If he took possession of fifty then they became worthless, the sale is invalidated in half and half a dirham is returned, considering the part as the whole. If their price fell, the sale is not invalidated, and there is no option for the buyer. If the coins (as price) became worthless before taking possession, the sale is invalidated according to Abu Hanifa; according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is not invalidated and their value must be paid. If the loaned fils become worthless, he must return the like according to him (Abu Hanifa); according to them, their value in dirhams. Likewise if he usurped and consumed them. Then according to Abu Yusuf, the value is considered on the day of taking possession; the more correct opinion according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa) is that he must pay their value in gold and silver on the day of [the coins'] cessation. If someone bought coins and they exchanged possession on the condition that each of them has an option, and they separated on that, the sale is invalid because the option prevents the validity of possession. If one of them has an option, the sale is valid according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because the option does not prevent the establishment of ownership in the sold item, so the required possession is found in one of them. According to Abu Hanifa, it is not valid because the option affects both sides, thus preventing the validity of possession. If he sold a specific fils for two specific fils with the condition of an option, it is valid. End of what is in al-Muhit from the chapter on sale of coins and lending them.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of coins (fulus) and the effect of their depreciation (kasad). It is quoted from al-Muhit. The ruling discusses the scenario where coins become worthless after the sale contract but before delivery. By qiyas (analogy), the sale remains valid because the physical coins still exist. However, by istihsan (juristic preference), the sale is invalidated because the essential benefit of coins is their circulation (rawaj); their worthlessness is akin to destruction. The passage then details various sub-cases: partial delivery, coins as the price (thaman), loans, and the effect of khiyar (option). The dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) appears in the ruling on the coins becoming worthless when they are the price: Abu Hanifa says the sale is invalid, while the Sahibayn say it remains valid and the value must be paid. The issue of khiyar also differs: Abu Hanifa holds that khiyar affects both sides and prevents valid possession, while the Sahibayn hold that if only one party has khiyar, the sale is valid because ownership is established. The passage concludes with a ruling on selling one coin for two coins with khiyar, which is allowed.

Key Terms
كساد (kasad): Depreciation or worthlessness of coins; loss of circulation value.
رواج (rawāj): Circulation or acceptance of coins as currency; their essential benefit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the istihsan ruling in this lesson, what happens to a sale of coins if they become worthless (kasad) before the buyer takes possession?
A) The sale remains valid and the buyer may choose to take the worthless coins.
B) The sale becomes invalid (batil) because kasad is like destruction.
C) The buyer has the option to either take the coins or rescind the sale.
D) The sale is suspended until the coins regain value.

Key Takeaway
Kasad (total worthlessness) voids a sale by istihsan because it destroys the essential purpose (rawaj) of coins.

Kasad of the Price: Dispute Between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute: Kasad of coins as price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the effect of kasad when coins are the price (thaman), and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
When the price coins become worthless, Abu Hanifa voids the sale; the Sahibayn enforce payment of value.

This lesson focuses on a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens when the coins given as the price (thaman) become worthless before delivery? The passage from al-Muhit records the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this dispute clarifies the school's reliance on purpose over physical form.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario: coins as price
Consider a sale where the price is a certain number of fils, and those fils become worthless before the seller receives payment. The subject matter (goods) may still be with the seller.
This is different from Lesson 1 where the subject matter was coins.
2
State Abu Hanifa's view
Abu Hanifa holds that the sale is invalid (batil) because the price has lost its function. The buyer must return the goods and the seller returns any coins paid.
This aligns with the istihsan principle: kasad is destruction.
3
State the Sahibayn's view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the sale remains valid. The buyer must pay the value (qimah) of the coins in a stable currency (gold/silver) on the day they became worthless.
They consider physical existence sufficient; the obligation shifts to value.
4
Examine the ruling for loans and usurpation
If loaned fils become worthless, Abu Hanifa says the borrower returns like (mithl); the Sahibayn say the value (qimah) in dirhams. Similarly for usurped and consumed coins.
The same principle applies: physical like vs market value.
5
Determine the valuation date
Abu Yusuf values the coins on the day of taking possession (of the loan/price); Abu Hanifa (the more correct view) values them on the day of cessation (the day they became worthless) in gold or silver.
This affects the amount the debtor must pay.

Source Text

قيمة (qīmah): Market value, assessed in gold or silver.
مثل (mithl): Like for like (identical coins) in loan repayment.

According to the Sahibayn, what happens to the sale when the coins given as price become worthless before delivery?
A) The sale is void.
B) The buyer must pay the value of the coins in a stable currency.
C) The seller must accept the worthless coins.
D) The sale is suspended.

Key Takeaway
When the price coins become worthless, the relied-upon view voids the sale; the Sahibayn's view requires payment of value.
